رکوع اور سجدے میں حدث لاحق ہو جائے نماز کا حکم
و من احدث في ركوعه او سجوده توضأ و بنى ولا يعتد بالتي احدث فيها لان اتمام الركن بالانتقال كو الحدث لا يتحقق فلابد من الاعادة
ترجمہ اور جس شخص کو حدث ہوا اس کے رکوع میں یا سجدہ میں تو وضو کرے اور بناء کرے اور نہ شمار کرے اس رکن کو جس میں ہے حدث ہوا کیونکہ رکن کا اتمام اس رکن سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف منتقل ہونے سے ہے۔ اور حدث کے ساتھ انتقال محقق نہیں ہوا کیا اس رکن کا اعاد و ضروری ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی کو رکوع یا سجدہ کی حالت میں حدث ہوا خواہ وہ منفرد ہو یا امام یا مقتدی تو اس کو چاہئے کہ وضو کر کے مجد اور جس رکن میں حدث پیش آیا ہے اس کو شمار نہ کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک رکن اس وقت مکمل ہوتا ہے جب کہ اس سے دوسرے قضا طرف منتقل ہو جائے اور یہ انتقال فرض ہے اور حدث کے ساتھ انتقال متحقق نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ منتقل الیہ ( جس کی طرف منتقل ہو گا نما گھر جزء ہے اور حدث پیش آنے کے بعد نماز کا ایک جزء ادا کرنا بھی مفسد ہے اس لئے اس رکن کا اعادہ ضروری ہوگا ۔ مثلا اگر ر کو نائیں گے۔ ہوا تھا تو وضو کے بعد آکر رکوع ہی کرے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ جس قدر نماز اداء کی ہے وہ سب فاسد ہو جائے لیکن ہم نے قیاس کو اس حدینا مگر سے ترک کر دیا جو بنا نماز کے سلسلہ میں وارد ہوئی ہے۔ پس بمقتضی قیاس اس رکن کا ٹونا اور فاسد ہونا باقی رہا جس میں حدیث احق ہوا میں نے
العاده
امام کو رکوع سجدے میں حدث لاحق ہوا تو اس نے خلیفہ بنایا، خلیفہ نئے سرے سے رکوع سجدہ کرنے کے
ہوتی ولوکان اماما فقدم غيره وام المقدم على الركوع لانه يمكنه الاتمام بالات ترجمہ اور اگر یہ محدث امام تھا پس اس نے دوسرے کو خلیفہ کر دیا تو خلیفہ رکوع کی بعیت پر برابر رہے کیونکہ خلیفہ کور کو پوراک
رکھنے سے ممکن ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ محدث امام تھا جس کو رکوع میں حدث ہوا تھا پھر امام نے جھکے جھکے پھر کر دوسرے کو خلیفہ کر دیا توان از سر نور کوع کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ رکوع کی مقدار ای رکوع میں تھہرار ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس فعل پر دوام کیا جاتا ہے ہے کہ استدامت ( ٹھہرے رہنا ) کو از سر نو شروع کرنے کا حکم ہو جاتا ہے یہیں یہاں بھی خلیفہ کے لئے استدامت سے رکوع پورا کر نہیں اس لئے کہا گیا کہ وہ رکوع میں بقدر رکوع ٹھہرار ہے۔ از سر نور کوع کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
Ruling on hadath occurring in ruku' or sujud.
And whoever becomes hadath in his ruku' or sujud, he performs wudu and continues (bana), and does not count that in which hadath occurred, because completion of the rukn is by transition, and with hadath transition is not realized, so repetition is necessary.
Translation: And the person who had hadath in his ruku' or sujud, he should perform wudu and continue, and not count the rukn in which hadath occurred, because completion of the rukn is by transitioning from this rukn to another rukn. And with hadath, transition is not realized; so repetition of that rukn is necessary.
Explanation: The issue is that if someone has hadath in the state of ruku' or sujud, whether he is a munfarid, imam, or muqtadi, he should perform wudu and continue, and not count the rukn in which hadath occurred. The proof is that a rukn is completed only when one transitions from it to the next, and this transition is fard. With hadath, transition is not realized, because the next part is a part of prayer, and after hadath, performing any part of prayer is corrupting; thus repetition of that rukn is necessary. For example, if [hadath occurred] in ruku', he should come back and do ruku' after wudu. Sahib al-Inaya wrote that qiyas would require all the prayer performed to be invalid, but we abandon qiyas due to the hadith that has come regarding continuing prayer. So by qiyas, the corruption of that rukn remains.
[Imam case] And if he was an imam and had hadath in ruku' or sujud, he appoints a deputy; the deputy does not need to perform ruku' or sujud anew.
And if he was an imam and appointed another, the deputy remains upon the same ruku' because completion is possible by staying.
Translation: And if this hadath person was an imam, and he appointed another as deputy, the deputy remains upon the same ruku' because the deputy can complete it by staying.
Explanation: If the imam had hadath in ruku' and then, while still bent, he appointed someone as deputy, the deputy does not need to perform ruku' anew; rather he stays in ruku' for the measure of ruku'. The proof is that for an action that is continued, staying (istidamah) is considered like beginning anew; so here too, the deputy can complete the ruku' through istidamah. Therefore, it has been said that he stays in ruku' for the measure of ruku'. There is no need to perform ruku' anew.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where a person's wudu becomes invalid (hadath) while they are in the state of ruku' or sujud during prayer. The ruling applies to all: individual (munfarid), imam, and follower. The person must break the prayer, renew wudu, and then continue the prayer from where they left off. However, the specific rukn (ruku' or sujud) in which the hadath occurred is not considered valid; it must be repeated upon returning. The reason is that a rukn is considered complete only when the person transitions to the next rukn (e.g., from ruku' to standing). Since hadath prevents valid transition (because any part of prayer performed after hadath is corrupt), that rukn was not actually completed, so it must be redone. The text notes that according to qiyas (analogy), the entire prayer would be invalid, but the ruling is based on a hadith that permits continuation (bana'). 

A special sub-case: if the imam is the one who becomes hadath during ruku', he may appoint a deputy (khalifa) to lead the rest of the prayer. The deputy does not need to repeat the ruku' from the beginning; rather, he simply remains in the ruku' position for the required duration (istidamah). This is because staying in an action (istidamah) is legally equivalent to performing it anew for the purpose of completing the obligation.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind, urine, etc.
بناء (bana'): Continuing the prayer from the point of interruption after renewing wudu, rather than starting over.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone's wudu breaks during ruku', what must they do upon renewing wudu?
A) Start the entire prayer over from the beginning.
B) Continue from ruku' without repeating it.
C) Repeat only the ruku' in which hadath occurred.
D) Perform additional sajdah sahw.

Key Takeaway
When wudu breaks during ruku' or sujud, repeat only that rukn after wudu, not the whole prayer; based on istihsan over qiyas.

Imam's Hadath: Appointment of Deputy and the Principle of Istidamah
Sub-case: imam's hadath and deputy's action based on istidamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the deputy of an imam who had hadath does not need to repeat the rukn from the beginning, referencing the principle of istidamah (staying).

Core Idea
Istidamah (staying) legally equals beginning anew; the deputy completes the rukn by remaining.

This lesson addresses a nuanced scenario: the imam himself becomes hadath during ruku'. He appoints a deputy to lead. Does the deputy need to restart the rukn? The Hanafi school uses the principle of istidamah to rule that the deputy simply remains in the position, avoiding repetition. We will explore the reasoning and its legal basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam is in the state of ruku' when hadath occurs. He, while still bent, designates a deputy (khalifa) to lead the prayer.
The deputy must be valid for leadership; the imam cannot continue.
2
Determine the ruling for the deputy
The deputy does not perform ruku' anew. Instead, he remains in the ruku' position for the required duration (the measure of ruku').
This is an exception to the general rule that the affected rukn must be repeated.
3
Understand the principle of istidamah
Istidamah (staying) in an action is legally equivalent to performing that action anew. Since the deputy is already in ruku', his continued stay fulfills the obligation of that rukn.
This is similar to how staying in sujud counts as sujud.
4
Apply the principle
The deputy's istidamah completes the rukn. He then continues the prayer from that point. The imam's original ruku' is not relied upon; the deputy's own stay counts.
The deputy must have the intention to complete the rukn through staying.

Source Text

Recalling a Missed Sajdah During Ruku' or Sujud: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling for recalling a missed sajdah during ruku' or sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for performing a missed sajdah during ruku' or sujud, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on repeating the ruku', and apply the principle that tartib is not a condition for validity.

Core Idea
Tartib (order) is not a condition; performing a missed sajdah directly from ruku' or sujud is valid, though repetition is preferred.

In prayer, one may remember a missed sajdah (whether from tilawah or the prayer itself) while already in ruku' or sujud. The Hanafi school provides a flexible ruling: you can perform that sajdah immediately without breaking the prayer. However, a difference arises among the founders: does the ruku' or sujud need to be repeated after the missed sajdah? This lesson unpacks the debate and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the preferred action
The passage describes a person who remembers a missed sajdah during ruku' or sujud. The preferred action is to perform the sajdah immediately, then repeat the ruku' or sujud to maintain order as much as possible.
The text calls this 'awla' (preferred), not obligatory.
2
State the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
If one does not repeat the ruku' or sujud, the prayer remains valid. The proof is that tartib (order) is not a condition for the validity of prayer actions; only transition with taharah matters.
Example of masbuq (latecomer) is given to show that order is flexible.
3
Identify the opposing position (Imam Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds that if one goes directly from ruku' to the missed sajdah without standing (qawmah), the ruku' must be repeated. His proof: qawmah is fard, and omitting it invalidates the ruku'.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Abu Yusuf's view is not the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: if someone performs a missed sajdah directly from ruku' without standing, Abu Yusuf requires repeating that ruku'; the majority deems it valid without repetition, though repetition is preferred.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a person who remembers a missed sajdah during the first sujud and lifts the head to perform it. According to the majority, the first sujud is valid and does not need repetition, but repeating it is mustahabb.
The same logic applies to sujud as to ruku'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نمازی کو رکوع یا سجدہ میں یاد آیا کہ اس پر رکوع یا سجدہ باقی ہے اس کے لئے کیا حکم ہے
ولو تذكر وهو راكع او ساجد ان عليه سجدة فإنحط من ركوعه لها او رفع رأسه من سجوده فسجدها يعيد الركوع والسجود وهذا بيان الأولى لتقع الافعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن وان لم يعد اجزاه لان الترتيب في افعال الصلوة ليس بشرط و لان الانتقال مع الطهارة شرط وقد وجد وعن أبي يوسف انه يلزمه اعادة الركوع لان القومة فرض عنده

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی نے رکوع کی حالت میں یاد کیا کہ اس پر سجدہ باقی ہے یا سجدہ کی حالت میں یاد کیا کہ اس پر بعد دباتی ہے خواہ سجدہ تلاوت ہو یا سجدہ نماز ہو۔ پس اگر اس نے رکوع میں یاد کیا اور رکوع ہی سے اس کی قضاء کے واسطے جھک گیا اور سجدہ تفاء کیا۔ اور اگر سجدہ کی حالت میں اس کو سجدہ قضاء یاد آیا اور اس نے سجدہ موجودہ سے سر اٹھا کر سجدہ قضاء کیا تو جس رکوع یا سجدہ میں یاد کرکے قضاء کا سجدہ کیا ہے اس رکوع اور جمود کا اعادہ کرے۔ اور یہ اعادہ کرنا اولی اور مستحب ہے تا کہ جہاں تک ممکن ہوں افعال ترتیب کے ساتھ ادا ہوں۔ یعنی موجودہ رکوع سے سجدہ قضاء مقدم کرنا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو مقدم کرنا اولیٰ ہے اور اگر اس نے رکوع اور سجود کا مادہ نہیں کیا تب بھی درست ہے کیونکہ جس رکوع اور سجود میں سجدہ قضاء یاد آتا تھاوہ حقیقت میں تو ہو گیا اعادہ صرف ترتیب کے پیش نظر تھا کر چونکہ نماز کے افعال میں ترتیب شرط ہے اس لئے ترتیب افعال نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے نماز میں کوئی حرج واقع نہیں ہوگا ۔ افعال ما از تیب شرط نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسبوق اپنی نماز اس جگہ سے شروع کرتا ہے جہاں سے امام کو پاتا ہے پھر امام کے سلام پھر نے کے بعد اول نماز جو چھوٹی ہوئی ہے اس کو ادا کرتا ہے گویا مسبوق نے آخر نماز کو پہلے ادا کیا اور اول نماز کو بعد میں ادا کیا پس اگر تر تیب شرط بونی زمسبوق کے لئے عذر جماعت کی وجہ سے اس کا ترک کرنا جائز نہ ہوتا۔
وسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکوع یا سجود جس میں سجدۂ قضاء یاد کیا ہے اس سے دوسرے رکن کی طرف طہارت کے ساتھ منتقل ہونا شرط ہے جب مشخص رکوع سے سیدھا سجدہ میں چلا گیا یا سجدہ سے سراٹھا کر قضاء کے لئے سجدہ کیا تو طہارت کے ساتھ منتقل ہونا پایا گیا لہذاوہ رکوع یا جدہ جس میں قضاء کا سجدہ یاد آیا تھا اداء ہو گیا اس کے علاوہ کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔
امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر رکوع سے سر اٹھائے بغیر سیدھا سجدہ میں چلا گیا تو اس پر رکوع کا اعادہ لازم ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک قومہ یعنی رکوع سے سر اٹھانا فرض ہے پس جب اس نے رکوع سے سر نہیں اٹھایا بلکہ رکوع سے سیدھا کبد و میں چلا گیا تو اس نے فرض چھوڑ دیا اور جب فرض یعنی قومہ ترک کر دیا تو رو کوع بھی ادا نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب رکوع اداء نہیں ہوا تو
What is the ruling for the one who remembers in ruku' or sujud that there is a sajdah remaining upon him?
And if he remembers while he is in ruku' or sujud that he owes a sajdah, so he bends down from his ruku' for it, or lifts his head from his sujud and performs it, he repeats the ruku' and sujud. And this is a statement of precedence so that the actions occur in order as much as possible. And if he does not repeat, it suffices him, because order in the actions of prayer is not a condition, and because transition with taharah is a condition, and that has been found. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he must repeat the ruku' because qawmah is fard according to him.
Translation: And if the praying person remembers in the state of being in ruku' or sujud that he has a sajdah remaining, so he bends from his ruku' to fulfill it, or lifts his head from his sujud and performs the missed sajdah, he must repeat the ruku' and sujud. This is a statement of preference so that the actions occur in order as much as possible. And if he does not repeat, it is sufficient for him, because order in the actions of prayer is not a condition, and because transition with taharah is a condition, and that has been found. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he must repeat the ruku' because qawmah is fard according to him.
Explanation: The scenario is that a person remembers during ruku' that he owes a sajdah, or during sujud that he owes another sajdah, whether it is sajdat al-tilawah or a sajdah of the prayer. So if he remembers in ruku' and bends from that ruku' to perform the missed sajdah, or if he remembers in sujud and lifts his head from the present sujud to perform the missed sajdah, he should repeat that ruku' or sujud. This repetition is preferable and mustahabb so that actions are performed in order as much as possible. If he does not repeat, it is still valid because the ruku' or sujud in which he remembered actually occurred; the repetition was only for the sake of order, and since order is not a condition in prayer actions, no harm occurs. The proof that order is not a condition is that a masbuq starts his prayer where he finds the imam, then after the imam's salam, he performs the first part of his prayer that he missed; so he performed the last part first, then the first part later. If order were a condition, it would not be permissible for the masbuq to omit it due to the excuse of congregation. Another proof is that the condition is to transition from that ruku' or sujud to another rukn with taharah; when he went directly from ruku' to sujud, or from sujud to another sujud after lifting his head, the transition with taharah is found, so that ruku' or sujud in which he remembered the missed sajdah is considered performed, and no repetition is needed.
From Imam Abu Yusuf it is narrated that if he went directly from ruku' to sujud without lifting his head, he must repeat the ruku'. The proof is that according to Abu Yusuf, qawmah (standing after ruku') is fard. So when he did not lift his head from ruku' but went directly to sujud, he omitted the fard; and when the fard (qawmah) is omitted, the ruku' is also not performed. And since the ruku' is not performed...
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a person is engaged in the prayer and during the act of ruku' or sujud, they remember that they owe an additional sajdah – either a prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) or a missed sajdah from the current prayer (qada' sajdah). The ruling: they are allowed to immediately perform that missed sajdah by bending down from ruku' or lifting the head from sujud for that purpose. However, after performing that sajdah, it is preferable (awla) to repeat the ruku' or sujud that was interrupted, so that the sequence of actions is maintained as much as possible. If they do not repeat it, the prayer remains valid because sequence (tartib) is not a condition for the validity of prayer actions; the only condition is that transitions between actions occur with taharah (purity) intact, which is fulfilled here. The text cites the example of the masbuq (latecomer) who follows the imam and then completes his prayer out of order – this proves that sequence is not essential. 

A disagreement with Imam Abu Yusuf is mentioned: he holds that if the person goes directly from ruku' to the missed sajdah without standing upright (qawmah), then the ruku' must be repeated. This is because, according to Abu Yusuf, qawmah (standing after ruku') is an obligatory element (fard) of the prayer, and by omitting it, the ruku' itself is invalidated. Therefore, the ruku' must be performed again. The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, which does not require repetition, though it is recommended.

Key Terms
قومہ (qawmah): Standing upright after ruku' before going into sujud.
ترتیب (tartib): The sequential order of prayer actions (qiyam, ruku', sujud, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling if someone performs a missed sajdah directly from ruku' without standing up?
A) The ruku' must be repeated because it is invalid.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted.
C) The prayer remains valid, but repeating ruku' is preferred.
D) The missed sajdah is not valid because it was performed out of order.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, tartib is not a condition for prayer actions; a missed sajdah can be performed directly from ruku' or sujud, and the prayer remains valid without repeating the interrupted action, though repetition is recommended.

Remembering Missed Sajdah in Ruku' or Sujood
Ruling on remembering a sajdah during ruku' or sujood with an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a missed sajdah is remembered during ruku' or sujood, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the interrupted act must be repeated.

Core Idea
When you remember a missed sajdah in ruku', you may proceed directly to sujood — repeating the ruku' is optional, not required.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario in salah: what happens if you remember a missed sajdah while you are already in ruku' or sujood? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling, but there is a notable difference between Imam Abu Yusuf and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). We will explore the proof and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and immediate action
Identify that the person is in ruku' or sujood and remembers a missed sajdah. The immediate action is to go directly to sujood (from ruku') or raise the head (from sujood) to perform the missed sajdah.
2
Identify the preferred follow-up action
After performing the missed sajdah, it is preferred to repeat the interrupted ruku' or sujood so that the actions occur in order as much as possible.
The text says 'هذا بيان الأولى' – this is a statement of the preferred.
3
Understand the permissibility of not repeating
If one does not repeat, the prayer is still valid. The proof is that order (tarteeb) is not a condition for the validity of prayer actions, citing the example of a masbooq who prays the end before the beginning.
Another proof: the condition of transitioning with taharah is fulfilled.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that repetition is obligatory because he considers qoomah (standing after ruku') to be fard. Going directly from ruku' to sujood omits qoomah, invalidating the ruku'.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
The thamarah al-khilaf: According to the majority, if one does not repeat, the prayer is valid. According to Abu Yusuf, the prayer is invalid if repetition is omitted.
The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تذكر وهو راكع او ساجد ان عليه سجدة فإنحط من ركوعه لها او رفع رأسه من سجوده فسجدها يعيد الركوع والسجود وهذا بيان الأولى لتقع الافعال مرتبة بالقدر الممكن وان لم يعد اجزاه لان الترتيب في افعال الصلوة ليس بشرط و لان الانتقال مع الطهارة شرط وقد وجد وعن أبي يوسف انه يلزمه اعادة الركوع لان القومة فرض عنده
If a person remembers while he is in ruku' or sujood that he owes a sajdah, then he lowers himself from his ruku' for it, or raises his head from his sujood and performs the sajdah, he should repeat the ruku' and sujood. And this is a statement of the preferred action so that the actions occur in order to the extent possible. And if he does not repeat, it suffices him, because order in the actions of prayer is not a condition, and because transition with purity is a condition and it has been found. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that he is obligated to repeat the ruku' because according to him, rising from ruku' (qoomah) is obligatory (fard).
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a person praying remembers that he has missed a sajdah (either of prayer or tilawah) while he is already in ruku' or sujood. The ruling presents two scenarios: if he remembers during ruku', he should go directly into sujood from his ruku' without standing up; if he remembers during sujood, he should raise his head from that sujood and perform the qada sajdah. In both cases, after performing the qada sajdah, he should repeat the ruku' or sujood that he interrupted. However, this repetition is only preferred (first choice) to maintain the sequence of actions as much as possible. If he does not repeat, his prayer is still valid because sequence is not a condition for the validity of prayer actions. The proof given is the practice of the masbooq, who prays the end first and then completes the beginning. The second proof is that the transition between actions with purity (taharah) is a condition, and it has been fulfilled. Abu Yusuf holds a different view: he requires repetition of the ruku' because he considers qoomah (standing up after ruku') to be fard. According to Abu Yusuf, if the person goes directly from ruku' to sujood without standing, the ruku' is not valid because qoomah is missing. Therefore, the ruku' must be repeated. The Hanafi fatwa follows the first position (that repetition is not obligatory), but Abu Yusuf's view is noted.

Key Terms
قومة (qoomah): The act of standing erect after ruku' before proceeding to sujood. Abu Yusuf considers it fard; others consider it wajib or sunnah.
مسبوق (masbooq): A person who joins the congregation late and misses part of the prayer. The example is used to prove that order is not a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if a person remembers a missed sajdah while in ruku' and performs it immediately, what is the ruling on repeating the ruku'?
A) Obligatory (fard)
B) Necessary (wajib)
C) Preferred (mustahab)
D) Invalid (batil)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that if you remember a missed sajdah in ruku' or sujood, you may proceed directly to perform it; repeating the interrupted act is recommended but not required, and your prayer remains valid.

Automatic Succession of the Follower as Imam When the Imam Leaves Due to Hadath
Ruling on automatic imam succession after imam's exit due to hadath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an imam leaves the mosque due to hadath with a single male follower and identify the difference of opinion when the only follower is a child or woman.

Core Idea
A single male follower automatically becomes imam to preserve the prayer, even without explicit appointment.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: the imam experiences an event (hadath) that breaks his wudu and leaves the mosque without appointing a successor. What happens to the prayer? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that the sole follower automatically steps in as imam. However, if the only followers are a child or a woman, a difference of opinion arises among Hanafi scholars. Let us explore the legal reasoning behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon: the imam's departure and the follower's assumption of leadership. State the ruling: the prayer is valid (sahih) and the follower becomes imam.
The text uses 'فالمأموم امام' (the follower is the imam).
2
Recognize the Automatic Nature
Note that this happens whether the original imam intended it or not. The reason given is 'صيانة الصلاة' (preserving the prayer).
No explicit appointment (istikhlaaf) is needed.
3
Understand the Legal Indication
The text compares this to an actual appointment: 'كما اذا استخلفه حقيقة' (just as if he had appointed him). The purpose is to cut off competition (قطع المزاحمة). Since there is only one follower, there is no competition, so the designation is effective by legal implication.
This is based on the principle of necessity (darurah).
4
Analyze the Dispute with Child/Woman Follower
If the only follower is a child or a woman, two opinions exist: some say the prayer becomes invalid because the successor is unfit for imamah; others say it remains valid because the appointment was not intentional.
The text does not provide a tarjih, ending with 'والله اعلم'.
5
Derive the Practical Takeaway
For a single adult male follower, the ruling is clear and automatic. For a child or woman, the mufta bihi in later scholarship tends toward invalidity, but caution and further study are advised.
The heavy reliance on 'صيانة الصلاة' shows the importance of preserving the act of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أم رجلا واحدا فاحدث وخرج من المسجد فالمأموم امام نوى اولم ينو لما فيه من صيانة الصفر تعين الأول لقطع المزاحمة ويتم الأول صلاته مقتديا بالثانى كما اذا استخلفه حقيقة ولو لم يكن خلف صبى او امرأة قيل تفسد صلاته لاستخلاف من لا يصلح للامامة وقيل لا تفسد لانه لم يوجد الاستحال قصدا و هو لا يصلح للامامة والله اعلم
And whoever leads one man in prayer, then has an event and leaves the mosque, the follower is the imam, whether he intended or did not intend, because of preserving the prayer. The first one (the original imam) is designated to cut off competition, and the first completes his prayer by following the second, just as if he had actually appointed him as a deputy. And if there is only a child or a woman behind him, it is said that his prayer becomes invalid because he appointed someone unfit for imamah, and it is said that it does not become invalid because the appointment did not occur intentionally, and he is not fit for imamah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where an imam leading exactly one follower has an event (hadath) that invalidates his wudu, and he leaves the mosque. In this case, the follower automatically becomes the imam, even if the original imam did not explicitly appoint him as a successor (khalifah). The reason is to preserve the prayer, as the follower would otherwise be left without an imam. The original imam then completes his prayer by following this new imam, exactly as if he had actually appointed him. The text addresses an objection: why is the follower considered designated without explicit designation? The answer is that the purpose of designation is to remove conflict, and since there is no conflict here (only one follower), the designation is considered to have occurred by legal indication (hukman). The second part addresses a scenario where the only persons behind the imam are a child or a woman. The Hanafi scholars have a difference of opinion. Some say the imam's prayer becomes invalid because he has effectively appointed someone who is not qualified for imamah (since a child or woman cannot lead a man in prayer). Others say it does not invalidate the prayer because the imam did not intentionally appoint them; the succession occurred by default, and they are not fit for imamah anyway. The text ends with 'Allah knows best.'

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A ritual impurity that breaks wudu, requiring renewal before prayer.
خليفة (khalifah): The person appointed to lead the prayer after the imam's exit due to an excuse, or automatically in this context.
صيانة الصلاة (siyanat al-salah): Preservation of the prayer; the principle that prayer should not be invalidated unnecessarily.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the reason given for the follower automatically becoming imam when the imam leaves due to hadath?
A) Because the imam intended it
B) To preserve the prayer
C) Because the follower is the most knowledgeable
D) To avoid confusion

Key Takeaway
When an imam leading one man leaves the mosque due to hadath, the sole male follower automatically becomes the imam to preserve the prayer; if the only follower is a child or woman, there is a difference of opinion, with the stronger view being that the prayer becomes invalid.

Ma'mum Becomes Imam When Original Imam Leaves Due to Hadath
Ruling with proof on automatic imam appointment and ikhtilaf on child/woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a ma'mum automatically becomes imam due to the original imam's hadath, and explain the ikhtilaf when only a child or woman is present.

Core Idea
When the imam leaves due to hadath, the ma'mum automatically becomes imam to preserve the prayer.

In the Hanafi school, the preservation of the prayer (sianat al-salat) is paramount. When the original imam exits the prayer due to hadath, the ma'mum must take over to prevent the prayer from becoming invalid. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof, as well as a subtle ikhtilaf among later Hanafi scholars regarding the eligibility of the successor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary case and the ruling
The passage begins with a case: one man leading another; the imam gets hadath and leaves the mosque. The ruling: the ma'mum becomes imam automatically, whether the imam intended to appoint him or not.
This is the foundational scenario.
2
Understand the rationale
The auto-appointment is for sianat al-salat (preservation of the prayer) and to avoid competition (muzahama). Since there is only one ma'mum, there is no competition, so appointment is not needed explicitly.
The illa is preservation and avoidance of emptiness.
3
Trace the qiyas to explicit appointment
The passage compares this situation to when the imam explicitly appoints a successor (istikhlaf haqiqi). In both cases, the original imam follows the new imam to complete his prayer. The auto-appointment is considered legally equivalent (hukman).
This answers the objection: how can the ma'mum become imam without explicit apppointment?
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on child/woman
If behind the imam with hadath there is only a child or woman (unfit for imamah), two views exist: (1) the imam's prayer becomes invalid because he followed an unfit person; (2) it does not become invalid because no actual or legal appointment occurred.
This ikhtilaf is among later mashayikh within the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The passage ends with 'Wallahu a'lam', indicating the second view is preferred: the imam's prayer remains valid because neither haqiqi nor hukmi istikhlaf occurred.
The preferred view is that the imam's prayer is valid.

موقوف ہے اور وہ یہاں پایا نہیں گیا کیونکہ استخلاف (خلیفہ کرنا ) حقیقتہ ہو گیا یا حکما ہوگا۔ اور یہاں دونوں میں سے کوئی موجود نہیں،. اری رہا تو اس لئے نہیں کہ امام محدث کی طرف سے قصد ا خلیفہ کرنا نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور حکما اس لئے نہیں کہ بچہ یا عورت امامت کی صلاحیت
نہیں رکھتے۔
پس جب ان دونوں میں امامت کی صلاحیت نہیں تو حکما خلیفہ بھی نہیں ہو سکتے۔ پس جب نہ حقیقتہ کرنا پایا گیا اور نہ حکما تو امام محدث کی نماز بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ امام کی نماز کا فاسد ہونا مقندی کے خلیفہ ہو جانے پرمبنی ہے۔ واللہ علم بالصواب ۔ جمیل احمد
He was leading one person, then hadath occurred to him and he left the mosque, so the follower is the imam, whether the first imam intended to appoint a successor or not. And whoever leads one man, then has hadath and leaves the mosque, the follower is the imam, whether he intended or not, because of preserving the prayer; the first's appointment is to cut off competition, and here there is no competition. And the first completes his prayer by following the second, just as if he had appointed him in reality. And if behind him there was no one except a child or a woman, it was said: his prayer is invalidated because he appointed one unfit for imamah; and it was said: it is not invalidated because appointment by intention did not occur, and he is unfit for imamah. And Allah knows best. Translation: And the man who led one man, then hadath occurred to the imam and he left the mosque, then the follower is imam, whether the first imam intended appointment or not, because of preserving the prayer; and the first imam's appointing (someone) is to cut off competition, and here there is no competition; and the first imam completes his prayer by following the second, just as when he appoints him in reality. And if behind the imam with hadath there was no one except a child or a woman, then it was said: the imam's prayer becomes invalid because he appointed a person who is not fit; and it was said: the imam's prayer does not become invalid because intentional appointment was not found, and he is not fit for imamah. And the explanation: the scenario is that one man led another man, then hadath occurred to the imam and he left the mosque, then the follower becomes imam whether the first imam intended his appointment or not, provided that he is fit for imamah. In the phrase, there is also a probability that he (the follower) intended to become khalifah or not. The proof is that in this case, in the follower's becoming imam, there is protection of the follower's prayer, because if the imam is not determined, the place of imamah will be empty of an imam, and the emptiness of the place of imamah from an imam harms the follower's prayer; therefore we said that in the mentioned case the follower will automatically become imam. And 'Ta'yin al-awwal' is the answer to an objection. The objection is: determination (ta'yin) without appointing by the appointer is not realized? The situation is that the imam with hadath did not appoint the follower for imamah, so how can the follower be imam? The answer: The imam's appointing someone as khalifah is to cut off competition, and since there is no competitor here, it (appointment) exists in effect. And when the appointment exists in effect, it becomes as if the imam with hadath appointed him as khalifah. Now the imam with hadath completes his prayer by following him, just as if he had appointed him in reality. And if behind the imam with hadath there was no one except a minor child or a woman, then there is a difference of opinion among the mashayikh. Some said: the imam's prayer becomes invalid because he appointed a person who is not fit for imamah; so when a child or a woman is not fit for imamah, even if in effect, the imam with hadath would be following him. And the rule is that whoever follows a person who is not fit for imamah, his prayer becomes invalid. And some mashayikh said: the imam with hadath's prayer does not become invalid because the invalidation of prayer depends on the follower becoming khalifah, and that is not found here, because istikhlaf (making khalifah) occurs either in reality or in effect, and here neither is present. Not in reality because intentional appointment from the imam with hadath is not found; and not in effect because the child or woman do not possess the capacity for imamah. So when both lack capacity for imamah, they cannot be khalifah even in effect. So when neither reality nor effect is found, the imam with hadath's prayer does not become invalid, because the invalidation of the imam's prayer is based on the follower becoming khalifah. And Allah knows best what is correct. Jamil Ahmad.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya (a commentary on Al-Hidayah) presents a nuanced ruling about automatic imam appointment when the original imam exits the prayer due to hadath (ritual impurity). The scenario: one man (the original imam) is leading one other man (the ma'mum). The imam experiences hadath and leaves the mosque. At this point, the ma'mum automatically becomes the imam for the remainder of the prayer, regardless of whether the original imam had the intention to appoint him or not. The rationale is preservation of the prayer (sianat al-salat). If the imam were not automatically replaced, the place of imamah would be empty, voiding the ma'mum's prayer. The commentary addresses an objection: how can the ma'mum become imam without explicit appointment? The answer: in normal circumstances, the imam's appointment (ta'yin) of a successor is to avoid competition (muzahama). Since there is no competitor here (only one ma'mum), the appointment is considered to have occurred legally (hukman). This is qiyas (analogy) to the case where the imam explicitly appoints a successor. The passage then discusses a secondary issue: if behind the imam with hadath there is only a child or a woman (unfit for imamah), there is an ikhtilaf among the mashayikh. One view (qila) says the imam's prayer becomes invalid because he has effectively appointed someone unfit (istikhlaf of one not qualified). The other view says it does not invalidate because the imam lacked the intent to appoint, and since the child/woman is not fit, the appointment is legally nonexistent. The text sides with the second view by concluding: since neither actual nor legal appointment occurred, the imam's prayer remains valid. The authority weight: this is from the commentary tradition (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin level) but based on Hidayah which is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): Follower in prayer; the one being led by an imam.
خلیفہ (khalifah): Successor imam appointed by the original imam.
حدث (hadath): Minor ritual impurity that nullifies wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the original imam leaves due to hadath and only a child or woman is behind him, which view does the passage ultimately support regarding the imam's prayer?
A) The imam's prayer becomes invalid because he appointed an unfit person.
B) The imam's prayer remains valid because no actual or legal appointment occurred.
C) The prayer of both becomes invalid.
D) The matter is left undecided.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the imam exits due to hadath, the ma'mum automatically becomes imam; if the only followers are a child or woman, the imam's prayer is still valid per the preferred view.

Speaking Invalidates Prayer: Hanafi Proof and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speech during prayer and explain why forgetful speech invalidates, distinguishing the Shafi'i position and evidence.

Core Idea
Any speech, intentional or forgetful, invalidates prayer in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a core Hanafi ruling: speech invalidates prayer, whether intentional or forgetful. The Shafi'i school holds that forgetful speech is excused. We will explore the textual proofs from hadith and the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument, clarifying the legal principle behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: speech invalidates prayer whether intentional or forgetful. Note that this is the mufta bihi view from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Identify the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that speech due to error or forgetfulness does not invalidate if not lengthy.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Read the hadith of Mu'awiyah ibn al-Hakam: the Prophet said 'Our prayer is not suitable for people's speech.' This is a general prohibition covering all speech.
Dalil: general prohibition (amm) indicates invalidation.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (forgiveness for forgetfulness). The Hanafi response: this refers to sin (otherworldly), not invalidation (worldly).
Distinction between worldly and otherworldly consequences.
5
Determine the practical difference
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says any speech invalidates; Shafi'i says forgetful speech does not. Then note the exception of salam (dhikr when forgetful).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها
ومن تكلم في صلوته عامدا اوساهيا بطلت صلوته خلافا للشافعى فى الخطاء والنسيان و مفزعه الحديث المعروف ولنا قوله عليه السلام ان صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس وانما هي التسبيح والتهليل وقراءة القرآن ومارواه محمول على رفع الاثم بخلاف السلام ساهيا لانه من الاذكار فيعتبر ذكرا في حالة النسيان وكلاما في حالة التعمد لما فيه من كاف الخطاب

وحديث معاوية بن الحكم: قال صليت خلف رسول الله فعطش بعض القوم فقلت يرحمك الله فرماني القوه تنساه وه بابصارهم فقلت و الکل اماه مالی اراكم تنظرون الى شزرا فضربوا بايديهم على افخاذهم فعلم ذلك في انهم يسكتونتي فلما فرغ النبي دعانى فو الله مارأيت معلما احسن تعليما منه ما كهرني ولا زجونى ولكن قال ان صلاتنا هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس و انما هي التسبيح والتهليل و قراءة القرآن
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. And whoever speaks in his prayer intentionally or forgetfully, his prayer is invalidated, contrary to al-Shafi'i in error and forgetfulness, and his proof is the well-known hadith. Our evidence is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed this prayer of ours is not suitable for any speech of people; rather it is glorification, magnification, and recitation of the Quran.' And what he narrated is interpreted as lifting sin, unlike the salutation in forgetfulness, because it is from the remembrances, so it is considered remembrance in the state of forgetfulness and speech in the state of intention due to the address particle in it. And the hadith of Mu'awiyah ibn al-Hakam: He said: I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah and someone sneezed, so I said 'May Allah have mercy on you.' Then the people stared at me with their eyes, so I said 'May my mother be bereaved of me! Why do you look at me with stern looks?' Then they struck their hands on their thighs, so I understood that they were silencing me. When the Prophet finished, he called me. By Allah, I have never seen a teacher better than him; he did not scold me nor rebuke me, but said: 'Indeed this prayer of ours is not suitable for any speech of people; rather it is glorification, magnification, and recitation of the Quran.'
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on speech during prayer, engaging in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The ruling statement is clear: any deliberate or forgetful speech invalidates the prayer. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that speech due to error or forgetfulness does not invalidate, provided it is not lengthy. His proof is the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (My ummah is forgiven for error and forgetfulness). The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between worldly and otherworldly consequences: the hadith refers to sin (otherworldly), not invalidation (worldly). The Hanafi proof is the well-known hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that prayer is not a place for people's speech; it is only for glorification and Quran recitation. Additionally, the hadith of Mu'awiyah ibn al-Hakm demonstrates the Prophet's teaching that speech invalidates prayer, as he did not approve of the speech but instructed him kindly. The commentator elaborates that the salutation (salam) at the end of prayer is an exception: when uttered forgetfully, it is considered remembrance (dhikr) and does not invalidate, but when intentional, it is speech and invalidates. This distinction is based on the address particle 'kaf' in 'assalamu alaykum' which makes it directed to others, thus speech. The general principle: any utterance conveying meaning (kalam) invalidates prayer, even a single meaningful letter like 'ق' (qif = stop).

Key Terms
كلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Speech of people that is not from the remembrances of prayer
ساهيا (sahiyan): While forgetful or unaware of being in prayer
عامدا (amidan): Intentionally, with knowledge of being in prayer
السلام (al-salam): The salutation at the end of prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person speaks during prayer due to forgetfulness, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid.
B) The prayer remains valid, but they must perform prostration of forgetfulness.
C) The prayer is valid if the speech was brief.
D) The prayer is valid because forgetfulness is forgiven.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any speech, intentional or forgetful, invalidates prayer; the salutation is an exception when said forgetfully.

Speaking in Prayer: The Hanafi Position and Refutation of Imam Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deliberate and forgetful speech in prayer, explain the Shafi'i position, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof.

Core Idea
Forgetful speech does not invalidate prayer in the Hanafi school; only deliberate speech does.

In this lesson, we examine an inter-madhhab dispute regarding speaking during prayer. The Hanafi school holds that only deliberate speech invalidates prayer, while Imam al-Shafi'i maintains that any speech, even forgetful, breaks the prayer. We will explore the primary proofs from hadith, the analogical reasoning (qiyas) involving salam, and the Hanafi response based on usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
What exactly is disagreed upon between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding speech in prayer? The dispute is over the legal effect of forgetful/erroneous speech. Hanafis say only deliberate speech invalidates; Shafi'is say any speech invalidates unless very short.
The issue is the legal effect of nisyan and khata.
2
State the Hanafi proof
What is the primary dalil for the Hanafi position? The hadith of Muawiyah ibn al-Hakam where the Prophet explicitly forbids speech in prayer, indicating that the absence of speech is essential.
This hadith is explicit and directly addresses the issue.
3
Examine Imam Shafi'i's proof
What hadith does Shafi'i rely on and how does he interpret it? Shafi'i uses the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' to argue that error and forgetfulness have been lifted, so both sin and invalidity are removed.
He understands 'رفع' to include both worldly and otherworldly effects.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How do Hanafis refute the Shafi'i interpretation? Hanafis argue that lifting error and forgetfulness only removes sin (afterworldly), not the worldly legal consequence of invalidity. If both were intended, the word 'رفع' would need two different meanings simultaneously, which is not permissible in usul.
This is based on the principle that a common shared meaning (عموم مشترک) is not allowed.
5
Evaluate the qiyas (analogy) involving salam
How does the opponent use analogical reasoning, and how do Hanafis respond? The opponent argues that salam is like speech because both break prayer, and since forgetful salam does not invalidate, the same should apply to speech. Hanafis respond by distinguishing salam because it is inherently from the acts of prayer (adhkar) and a name of Allah, so it is not entirely like kalam.
This shows the Hanafi method of distinguishing the 'illa.

باب مايفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ اشرف البدا

۱۳۷
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيهه
اشرفی البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم یک ایھا النبی الخ اور سلام باری تعالیٰ کے اسما سنٹی میں سے ہے البتہ سلام نے کاف خطاب کی وجہ سے کلام کا حکم لے لیا۔ حاصل ہوا کہ السلام علیک من وجہ ذکر ہے اور من وجہ کلام ہے پس ہم نے دونوں وجہوں پر عمل کیا اور کہا اگر سلام ناسیا ہے تو وہ اذکار کے تو طلاق ہوگا۔ اور نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اور اگر عمدا ہے تو کا ہام کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گیا۔ اور نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Page 136. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Ashraf al-Bida. It is like the letter qaf meaning middle, and if a single meaningless letter occurs then it is not speech. According to Imam Shafi'i, in case of error and forgetfulness, a single word does not invalidate prayer provided it is not lengthy, because lengthy speech is contrary to error and forgetfulness. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the well-known hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' meaning error and forgetfulness have been removed from my ummah. The reason for deduction is that there are two types of rulings: worldly (that consequences attach) and otherworldly (sin). So it is as if the Prophet said that the ruling of error and forgetfulness is removed from my ummah in both worldly and otherworldly senses, meaning neither will anything become invalid nor will one be sinful in the afterlife. Fan an fi Sahib al-Inayah wrote that the reason for deduction is that the reality of both is not removed because they exist among people; rather the ruling (being invalidative) is removed. Our proof is the hadith of Muawiyah ibn al-Hakam al-Aslami (may Allah be pleased with him). The complete hadith is: 'Al-Khushu'... He said: I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah and a man sneezed, so I said 'May Allah have mercy on you.' Then the people glared at me with their eyes. I said, 'May my mother lose me, what is wrong with you that you look at me with stern eyes?' They struck their hands on their thighs, so I understood that they were telling me to be silent. When the Prophet finished, he called me. By Allah, I have never seen a better teacher than him; he did not rebuke me nor scold me, but said: 'In this prayer of ours, nothing of people's speech is appropriate; it is only glorification, declaration of Allah's oneness, and recitation of the Quran.' Translation: because it is khushu'... it will be speech of people... Translation: Muawiyah ibn Hakam says: I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah, then someone sneezed, so I said 'May Allah have mercy on you.' Then people... Commentary: From this hadith it is understood that the absence of speech in prayer is a requirement of prayer, just as the presence of purity is a requirement of prayer. Just as without purity prayer is not valid, similarly with the presence of speech it will not be valid. The response to Imam Shafi'i's presented hadith is that the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' is interpreted as removal of sin (the afterlife) only. If the worldly ruling (invalidity) were also intended, then a common shared meaning would be necessary, but a common shared meaning is not permissible. Contrary to the greeting (salam), any addition from the imam is invalidative... This is the response to the analogy. The second proof from analogy is that greeting (salam) is like speech, because each of them interrupts prayer. Regarding greeting, there is a distinction between forgetful and deliberate: forgetful greeting is not invalidative, deliberate is invalidative. So this same distinction should apply to speech: forgetful speech should not be invalidative, deliberate speech should be. The summary of the response is that greeting is not entirely like speech, because greeting is from the acts of prayer such that it is recited in al-Tahiyyat. This is also the saying of Imam Malik: it invalidates prayer, therefore... Page 137. Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Ashrafi al-Bidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 2. 'Ya ayyuha al-nabi' etc. And greeting (salam) is among the names of Allah Almighty. However, greeting took the ruling of speech due to the kaf of address. The conclusion is that 'al-salamu alayk' is in one respect dhikr and in another respect speech. So we have acted upon both aspects and said: if salam is done forgetfully, then it is classified among the adhkar and prayer is not invalid; but if deliberate, it attaches to kalam and prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding speaking in prayer. The Hanafi position is that deliberate speech invalidates prayer, but speech due to forgetfulness or error does not. Imam Shafi'i holds that any speech, whether deliberate or forgetful, invalidates prayer as long as it is not lengthy. The text presents Shafi'i's proof: the hadith 'رفع عن أمتي الخطأ والنسيان' (error and forgetfulness have been removed from my nation), which he interprets to mean both worldly and afterworldly consequences. The Hanafi response clarifies that this hadith only removes the afterworldly sin, not the worldly legal effect of invalidity, because if it removed both, the same word would have two different meanings simultaneously (common shared meaning), which is not permissible in usul. The Hanafi primary proof is the hadith of Muawiyah ibn al-Hakam, where the Prophet explicitly said that prayer does not accommodate any speech of people, only tasbih, takbir, and Quran. This establishes that speech is antithetical to prayer. Then a qiyas (analogy) is presented by the opponent: salam (greeting) is like speech since both interrupt prayer, and salam is invalid only if deliberate, so the same should apply to speech. The Hanafi response distinguishes salam because it is inherently from the acts of prayer (recited in al-Tahiyyat) and is a name of Allah. Thus, salam is not entirely like speech. The text concludes that the relied-upon Hanafi position stands: deliberate speech invalidates; forgetful speech does not.

Key Terms
كلام (kalam): Speech consisting of at least two letters or one meaningful letter that conveys meaning to others.
خطاء (khata): Error or mistake - acting contrary to the correct ruling without intentional neglect.
نسیان (nisyan): Forgetfulness - unintentional omission or commission due to lack of memory.
سلام (salam): The greeting of peace, specifically 'السلام عليكم' used at the end of prayer or as a general greeting.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning - applying a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to shared 'illa (effective cause).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person forgetfully says 'Assalamu alaykum' in the middle of prayer (not at the end), what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalidated because it is kalam.
B) The prayer remains valid because it is considered dhikr when done forgetfully.
C) The prayer is invalidated only if the greeting was addressed to someone specific.
D) The prayer becomes makruh but still valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, speech in prayer invalidates only if deliberate; forgetful speech is excused, based on the hadith of Muawiyah and the principle that error and forgetfulness remove sin but not the worldly ruling if the act is inherently incompatible with prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Groaning, Sighing, and Crying in Prayer: The Cause Determines the Ruling
Ruling on groaning/sighing/crying in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on groaning, sighing, and crying in prayer, distinguish between spiritual and worldly causes, and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Spiritual remembrance in prayer enhances khushu'; worldly distress invalidates it as speech of people.

In prayer, we aim for khushu' – humility and presence of heart. But what happens when sounds escape our lips? Does a groan of pain break the prayer, while a tear of longing for Paradise does not? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, where the cause of the sound – not just the sound itself – dictates whether it invalidates. We'll explore the proof from increased khushu' and the qiyas on explicit dhikr, and also examine an intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
Read the passage carefully: What are the specific sounds discussed? (aneen, awh, crying) What is the general ruling? The act can either invalidate or not, depending on the cause.
The act is any sound with letters produced intentionally or involuntarily.
2
Distinguish the Cause
The key distinction is the cause: spiritual recollection (of Jannah or Jahannam) vs. worldly pain or affliction. Identify which cause leads to invalidation and which does not.
The spiritual cause indicates increased khushu', the worldly cause shows jaza' and ta'assuf.
3
Apply the Proofs
Two proofs are given: (1) The sound from spiritual recollection demonstrates khushu', which is the goal of prayer, so it cannot invalidate. (2) Qiyas: if explicit invocation (e.g., 'Allahumma inni as'aluka al-jannah') is valid in prayer, then implicit allusion through groaning is even more fitting. Apply these to the case.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf distinguishes between 'ah' (never invalidates) and 'awh' (invalidates) based on a letter principle (original vs. extra letters). However, this principle is criticized as weak because meaning can be conveyed even with all extra letters.
The commentator rejects the letter principle and upholds the cause-based distinction as mufta bihi.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is the cause-based distinction: spiritual = valid, worldly = invalid. This is the zahir al-riwayah position, and Abu Yusuf's letter-based view is considered weak and not operative for fatwa.
This is supported by Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad as well.

نماز میں کراہنا اور رونا خواہ خشیت سے ہو یا تکلیف اور درد سے مفسد صلوٰۃ ہے یا نہیں
مان ان فيها او تاوه او بكى فارتفع بكاؤه فان كان من ذكر الجنة أو النار لم يقطعها لانه يدل على زيادة الخشوع وان كان من وجع او مصيبة قطعها لان فيه اظهار الجزع والتأسف فكان من كلام الناس وعن ابي يوسف ان قوله اه لم يفسد في الحالين واوه يفسد وقيل الأصل عنده ان الكلمة اذا اشتملت على حرفين رهما زاندتان او احداهما لاتفسد وان كانتا اصليتين تفسد و حروف الزوائد جمعوها في قولهم "اليوم تنساه" وهذا لا يقوى لان كلام الناس فى متفاهم العرف يتبع وجود حروف الهجاء وافهام المعنى و يتحقق دلك في حروف كلها زوائد
ترجمہ اور اگر نماز میں کوئی کراہا یا آہ کیا یا رو دیا پس اس کا رونا بلند ہوا پس اگر یہ جنت یا دوزخ کے ذکر سے ہے تو نماز کو قطع نہیں کرے کیونکہ یہ خشوع کی زیادتی پر دلیل ہےاور اگر در دیا مصیبت کی وجہ سے ہے تو نماز کو قطع کر دیگا کیونکہ اس میں جزع اور تاست کا اظہار ہے و کام الناس میں سے ہو گیا۔ اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ آہ کہنا دونوں حالتوں میں مفسد نہیں ہے اور وہ مفسد ہے۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یا پیسف کے نزدیک اصل یہ ہے کہ کلمہ جب دو حرفوں پر مشتمل ہو اور وہ دونوں زائد ہوں۔ یا ان دونوں میں ایک زائد ہو تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوئی اور گردونوں اصلی ہوں تو فاسد ہو جائے گی اور حروف زوائد کو اہل لغت نے اپنے قول اليوم تنساہ میں جمع کیا ہے اور یہ اصل قوی نہیں کیونکہ کام الناس ہونا عرف کی اصطلاح میں تابع ہوتا ہے حروف ہجاء کے پائے جانے اور معنی سمجھانے کے اور یہ تحقیق ہو جاتا ہے ایسے حروف میں کہ وہ سب کے سب زائد ہوں۔
تشریح این مبتلائے درد کی آواز جسکو اردو میں کر اپنا کہتے ہیں اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ انین آہ کہنا اور تاوہ او کہنا اور ارتفاع بار یہ ہے کہ اس سے حروف پیدا ہو جائیں حاصل مسئلہ یہ کہ نماز میں کراہنا یا اوہ کہا یا رو تا اس طور پر ہو کہ اس سے حروف پیدا ہو جائیں ان مل سے ہر ایک جنت یا دوزخ کرے ذکر کی وجہ سے ہوگا یا در دیا کسی اور مصیبت کی وجہ سے پس اگر اول ہے یعنی جنت یا دوزخ کے ذکر کی اہ سے رویایا اوہ کہا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ یہ خشوع کی زیادتی پر دلیل ہے اور چونکہ نماز میں خشوع ہی مطلوب ہے اس لئے خشوع کی زیادتی مفسد نماز کیسے ہو سکتی ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ کہ اگر یہ شخص صراحة اللهم اني اسألك الجنة واعوذ بك من النار کہتا تو نماز فاسد نہ ہوتی پس کنایہ کی صورت میں بدرجہ اولی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی یہ باتیں درد یا کسی مصیبت کی وجہ سے پیدا ہوئیں تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی میں قول امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے کیونکہ اس میں جزع اور تاسف کا اظہار ہے اس وجہ سے یہ کلام الناس میں سے ہو گیا اور کلام الناس ضد نماز ہے لہذا یہ بھی مفسد نماز ہوگا۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ یہ شخص اگر درد اور مصیبت کا اظہار بصراحت کرتا مثلا کہتا انسی مصاب خدایا
(Question:) Groaning and crying in prayer, whether due to fear of Allah or due to pain and suffering, does it invalidate the prayer? (Answer:) If one groans ['ah'] or sighs ['awh'] or cries and his crying becomes loud: if it is due to remembrance of Paradise or Hellfire, it does not interrupt the prayer because it indicates increased khushu' (humility). But if it is due to pain or affliction, it interrupts the prayer because it shows anxiety and regret, thus it becomes from the speech of people. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the word 'ah' does not invalidate in both cases, while 'awh' does. And it is said that the principle according to him is: if a word consists of two letters, and both are extra (zawaid) or one of them is extra, it does not invalidate; but if both are original letters, it does invalidate. The extra letters have been collected by linguists in their saying "اليوم تنساه". But this principle is not strong because being speech of people in the customary understanding follows the existence of letters of alphabet and conveying meaning, and this is realized even when all letters are extra. Commentary: 'Aneen' is the sound of a person in pain, which in Urdu is called 'karaahna'. And some scholars said that 'aneen' is saying 'ah', and 'ta'awwuh' is saying 'awh', and 'irtifa' of crying means that letters are produced from it. The summary of the issue: Groaning in prayer or saying 'oh' or crying in such a way that letters are produced: if it is due to remembrance of Paradise or Hell, then prayer is not invalid because it indicates increased khushu', and since khushu' is desired in prayer, its increase cannot invalidate prayer. Second proof: if this person were to explicitly say 'Allahumma inni as'aluka al-jannah wa a'udhu bika min al-nar', prayer would not be invalid; so by way of kinayah (implication), the prayer would a fortiori not be invalid. But if it is the second case (due to pain or affliction), then prayer becomes invalid. This is the saying of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, because it contains expression of anxiety and regret, thus it becomes from the speech of people, and speech of people is contrary to prayer, therefore it invalidates prayer. Second point: if this person expresses pain and affliction explicitly, e.g., says 'inni musabun ya Allah' (I am afflicted, O Allah)...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on groaning, sighing, and crying in prayer. The key distinction is the cause: if the sounds are due to spiritual recollection of the afterlife (Jannah or Jahannam), they indicate increased khushu' (humility before Allah), which is the very essence of prayer, so they do not invalidate. However, if they arise from worldly pain or affliction, they show jaza' (anxiety) and ta'assuf (regret), which are contrary to the state of prayer and considered 'kalam al-nas' (speech of people), thus invalidating the prayer. The text also mentions the opinion of Abu Yusuf, who distinguishes between the exclamation 'ah' (which does not invalidate in both cases) and 'awh' (which does). A principle is attributed to him regarding the letters: if a word consists of two extra letters (like 'ah' where both letters are exclamatory) it does not invalidate; if both are original (meaningful), it does. However, this principle is criticized because even words composed entirely of extra letters can convey meaning and thus be considered speech in the customary sense. The text then provides a second proof: if the person were to explicitly supplicate for Paradise and seek refuge from Hell, that would be legitimate dhikr, so alluding to it by groaning is even more fitting. Conversely, explicit expression of pain (like 'inni musabun') is clearly kalam and invalidates. The positions of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad are noted as also holding that such sounds from pain invalidate.

Key Terms
أنين (aneen): Groaning, the sound of a person in pain or distress, often expressed as 'ah'.
أوه (awh): An exclamation of pain or sorrow, often spelled 'اوہ' in Urdu.
خشوع (khushu'): Humility and calmness before Allah, a desired state in prayer.
جزع (jaza'): Anxiety, impatience, or distress in the face of hardship.
تأسف (ta'assuf): Regret, sorrow, or expression of grief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person in prayer experiences a sudden headache and involuntarily says 'Ah!' audibly. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because 'Ah' is speech of people.
B) The prayer remains valid because the sound was involuntary and from pain.
C) The prayer is invalid only if the person said 'Oh' instead of 'Ah'.
D) The prayer is invalid because any sound with letters invalidates.

Key Takeaway
The invalidity of sounds in prayer depends on their cause: spiritual recollection does not break prayer, while worldly distress does.

Coughing, Sneezing, and Responding to Sneeze in Prayer
Rulings on involuntary sounds and voluntary responses in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between voluntary and involuntary sounds in prayer, state when coughing invalidates prayer, and identify which verbal responses to a sneeze invalidate prayer.

Core Idea
Involuntary sounds are excused; voluntary speech, including conventional sneeze responses, invalidates prayer.

This lesson clarifies when sounds and responses during prayer affect its validity. Not all sounds break the prayer; the key distinction is whether the act is voluntary or involuntary, and whether a response is a social convention (kalam al-nas) or a dhikr. We'll examine the rulings on coughing, sneezing, belching, and responding to a sneeze.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Determine if the act is a bodily sound (cough, sneeze, belch) or a verbal response to a sneeze. Note whether it is voluntary or involuntary. The passage distinguishes between tanahnuh (cough) and atās (sneeze) with different rulings.
Sneezing and belching are typically involuntary.
2
Apply the rule for involuntary sounds
Involuntary sounds like sneezing and belching are excused even if they produce letters. They do not invalidate prayer. The same applies to a cough that is due to an excuse (e.g., illness or genuine need).
The text says 'عفو' (forgiven) for such cases.
3
Apply the rule for voluntary sounds
If a person deliberately coughs without excuse and letters are produced (like saying 'Akh'), the prayer is invalidated according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. This is because it constitutes voluntary speech.
The phrase 'ينبغى ان يفسد' indicates it is appropriate to rule it invalid.
4
Assess verbal responses to a sneeze
If a praying person says 'Yarhamukallah' in response to a sneeze, it invalidates because it is a conventional social response (kalam al-nas). Saying 'Alhamdulillah' does not invalidate because it is not used as a customary reply; it is a dhikr.
The criterion is whether the phrase is conventionally used as a response among people.

رجمہ اور اگر مصلی نے شیخ کیا بغیر عذر کے بائیں طور کو مدفوع الیہ نہ ہوا اور ا سے حروف پیدا ہو جائیں تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے اور سح عذر کی وجہ سے ہو تو یہ معاف ہے جیسے چھینک اور ڈکار جب کہ اس سے حروف پیدا ہو جائیں ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مصلی نے شیخ کیا یعنی کھنکھارا اور اس کی وجہ سے حروف بھی پیدا ہو گئے مثلات) بالفتح یا بانضم ) کہا تو اس کی صورتیں ہیں عذر کی وجہ سے ہوگا یا بغیر عذر کے۔ اگر بغیر عذر کے ہو یعنی اضطراری نہ ہو بلکہ اختیاری ہوتو طرفین کے نزدیک نماز فاسد : ہاں چاہنے اور اگر عذر کی وجہ سے ہے تو یہ معاف ہے یعنی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی جیسے چھینک اور ڈکار سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوتی اگر چہ اس سے ادب با ظاہر ہو جائیں۔
ال عطس فقال له آخر ير حمك الله وهو في الصلوة فسدت صلوته لانه يجرى في مخاطبات الناس لكان من كلامهم بخلاف ما اذا قال العاطس او السامع الحمد لله على ما قالوا لانه لم يتعارف جوابا رجمہ اور اگرکسی کو چھینک آئی پھر اس سے دوسرے نے جو نماز پڑھتا ہے کہا یرحمک اللہ تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ یہ وگوں کے مخاطبات میں جاری ہوتا ہے لہذا یہ لوگوں کے کلام سے ہوگا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب چھینکنے والے مصلی یا سننے والے مصلحی نے کہا الحمدللہ اس بناء پر جومشائخ نے کہا کیونکہ الحمد للہ کہنا جواب متعارف نہیں ہے۔ شریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کو چھینک آئی پس دوسرے آدمی نے جو نماز پڑھتا ہے یرحمک اللہ کہا تو اس قائل کی نماز فاسد ہو گی کیونکہ پیر حمک اللہ میں کاف خطاب او ہے اور لوگوں میں یہ بول چال جاری بھی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ کالام الناس کے قبیل سے ہو گا اور
And if he coughs without excuse, i.e., not compelled, and letters are produced by it, it is appropriate that it invalidates according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And if it is due to an excuse, it is forgiven, like sneezing and belching when letters are produced. Explanation: The matter is: if the praying person coughs, i.e., clears his throat, and letters are produced by it, such as saying 'Akh' (with fatha or dhamma), then there are two cases: either it is due to an excuse or without excuse. If without excuse, i.e., not involuntary but voluntary, then according to the two it invalidates prayer. And if due to an excuse, it is forgiven, i.e., prayer does not become invalid, just as sneezing and belching do not invalidate prayer even if letters appear from them. And if someone sneezes and another person, who is praying, says 'Yarhamukallah', his prayer becomes invalidated because this is used in people's address, so it is from their speech. Unlike when the sneezer or the listener (who is praying) says 'Alhamdulillah' based on what the scholars said, because saying 'Alhamdulillah' is not a conventional response. Explanation: The matter is: a person sneezed, then another man who is praying said 'Yarhamukallah', that speaker's prayer becomes invalid because 'Yarhamukallah' contains the letter of address 'kaf' and it is current usage among people. Therefore it is from the category of human speech.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides specific rulings on involuntary sounds and voluntary responses during prayer. It first addresses coughing (tanahnuh): if a person deliberately coughs without an excuse (e.g., not compelled by a genuine need) and letters are produced, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the two), the prayer is invalidated. However, if the cough is due to an excuse (e.g., a cough due to illness or an involuntary reflex), it is excused and does not invalidate the prayer. This is analogous to sneezing and belching, which are generally involuntary and do not invalidate prayer even if they produce letters. The rationale is that these are natural, uncontrolled bodily reactions, not deliberate speech. The second part addresses responding to a sneeze. If someone who is praying says 'Yarhamukallah' (May Allah have mercy on you) in response to a sneeze, his prayer is invalidated because this phrase is conventionally used as a response in people's speech; it is kalam al-nas (human speech). However, if the praying person (either the sneezer or the listener) says 'Alhamdulillah' (Praise be to Allah), the prayer is not invalidated because 'Alhamdulillah' is not conventionally used as a response to a sneeze (it is a dhikr). The distinction is based on customary usage: 'Yarhamukallah' is a common social response, while 'Alhamdulillah' is seen as a form of remembrance of Allah, not conversational speech.

Key Terms
تنحنح (Tanahnuh): Clearing the throat or coughing. If done deliberately without excuse, invalidates prayer when letters are produced.
عطاس (Atās): Sneezing. It is excused in prayer even if it produces letters.
یرحمک اللہ (Yarhamukallah): A conventional response to sneezing. If said by a praying person, it invalidates his prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must say 'Alhamdulillah' immediately to maintain validity.

Key Takeaway
Involuntary sounds and dhikr-like responses are excused; voluntary speech and conventional social responses invalidate prayer.

Sneezing in Prayer: The Ruling on Saying Alhamdulillah
Explains the ruling on sneezing and saying alhamdulillah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying 'Alhamdulillah' in prayer after sneezing and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement regarding tongue movement.

Core Idea
Saying 'Alhamdulillah' in prayer after sneezing is permissible as dhikr, but a rare narration warns against moving the tongue.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person sneezes while in prayer. The general rule is that speaking to people invalidates prayer, but the Hanafi school carves out an exception for dhikr. However, an isolated narration from Imam Abu Hanifa adds a condition that the tongue must not move. Let's examine the reasoning and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
What is the act being discussed? Saying 'Alhamdulillah' in response to a sneeze during prayer. The general ruling is that speech invalidates prayer.
The passage begins with this principle.
2
Locate the exception for dhikr
The mashayikh argue that 'Alhamdulillah' is not considered speech but dhikr, which is permissible in prayer. Thus, saying it does not invalidate.
Why is it not speech? In custom, it is not a response to sneezing but remembrance of Allah.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, reported in al-Muhit, states that if the person moves his tongue while saying it, the prayer becomes invalid.
This is a riwaya from the Nawadir (rare transmissions).
4
Evaluate the evidence and determine the mufta bihi
The mashayikh's view is preferred because it is based on the general principle of dhikr, and the riwaya is weak (nawadir). Thus, the relied-upon position is that it does not invalidate.
The later scholars adopted the view of the mashayikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کالام الناس مفسد نماز ہے لہذا یہ بھی مفسد نماز ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر چھینکنے والے مصلی نے یا سنے والے مصلی نے الحمد للہ کہا تو مشائخ کے قول کے مطابق مفسد نماز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ الحمد للہ کہنا عرف میں جواب شمار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ یہ ذکر اللہ ہے اور ذکر اللہ نماز میں جائز ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کہا گیا کہ الحمد للہ کہنے سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ صاحب عنایہ نے محیط کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ چھینکنے والا اپنے دل میں الحمد للہ کہے اور اپنی زبان کو حرکت نہ دے اگر اس نے اپنی زبان کو حرکت دی تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
The speech of people invalidates prayer, so this also invalidates prayer. Contrary to this, if the sneezing person or the hearing person said alhamdulillah, according to the mashayikh, it does not invalidate prayer because saying alhamdulillah is not considered a response in custom, rather it is dhikr of Allah, and dhikr of Allah is permissible in prayer. For this reason it was said that saying alhamdulillah does not invalidate prayer. The author of al-'Inayah wrote based on al-Muhit that there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa that the sneezing person should say alhamdulillah in his heart and not move his tongue; if he moves his tongue, his prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of responding to a sneeze during prayer. The general principle is that speaking to people invalidates prayer. However, saying alhamdulillah in response to a sneeze is an exception according to the majority of Hanafi mashayikh. They argue that in common custom, alhamdulillah is not considered a reply to a sneeze but rather dhikr of Allah, which is permissible in prayer. Therefore, it does not invalidate the prayer. The passage then mentions a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa, reported by the author of al-'Inayah from al-Muhit, that if the person moves his tongue while saying alhamdulillah, his prayer is invalid. This indicates a difference within the school: the mashayikh's view is that it is permissible without invalidation, while the riwaya suggests caution. The relied-upon position is the view of the mashayikh, as the riwaya is from the Nawadir (rare transmissions).

Key Terms
مصلی (musalli): A person engaged in formal prayer (salat).
الحمد للہ (alhamdulillah): An Arabic phrase meaning 'All praise is due to Allah', used as dhikr.
ذکر اللہ (dhikr Allah): Remembrance of Allah, which is permissible in prayer.
روایت (riwaya): A narration or transmitted report, often from an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It does not invalidate because it is dhikr.

D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, saying Alhamdulillah in prayer after sneezing is permissible as dhikr and does not invalidate, despite a rare narration warning against tongue movement.
