Ruling on Giving a Laqmah to a Non-Imam: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Repetition
States ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on laqmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving a prompt to a non-imam, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding repetition, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Prompting a non-imam invalidates prayer; the dispute is whether one act suffices or only repetition.

This lesson addresses a common situation during congregational prayer: a person gives a Quranic cue to someone other than his own imam. While the basic ruling is clear—such an act invalidates both parties' prayers—a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement exists concerning whether the act must be repeated to cause invalidation. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists classify actions (speech vs. act) and how later authorities resolve apparent contradictions within the school's foundational texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed (giving laqmah to a non-imam)? What is the initial hukm (invalidated prayer)?
The act is considered teaching/learning, categorized as kalam al-nas.
2
Understand the scenario
The passage outlines different combinations of requesters and givers. Focus on the case where both are in prayer but not as imam and muqtadi.
This is the primary scenario for invalidation.
3
Identify the dispute
Imam Muhammad has two statements: in al-Mabsut he conditions invalidation on repetition; in al-Jami' al-Saghir he does not. What is the basis for each?
One views laqmah as a fi'l (act), the other as kalam (speech).
4
Analyze the reasoning
Acts not part of prayer are pardoned if little but invalidate if excessive. Speech invalidates regardless of quantity. Which categorization leads to which ruling?
This is the core of the talil (cause-based reasoning).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later mashayikh preferred the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir (no repetition needed). Why? What is the authority weight of each source?
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is often considered more authoritative.

ذکر کی کہ لقمہ دینا ایک عمل ہے جو اعمال صلوۃ میں سے نہیں ہے اور منافی صلوۃ عمل اگر کثیر ہوتو مفسد نماز چھوڑ کر ہو گا اور اگر قلیل ہو تو مفسد نماز نہیں ہوتا پس ایک بار لقمہ دینا عمل قلیل ہے اور اس سے زائد عمل کثیر ہے اس وجہ سے امام محمد نے کہا کہ تر میں اگر تکرار پایا گیا تو نماز فاسد ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ یکن جامع صغیر میں یہ شہر دانہیں ہے کیونکہ لقمہ دینا کلام کرنا ہے اور کام کرنا بذات خود مفسد نماز ہے اگر چقلیل کیوں نہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ س دینے کومبسوط میں فعل شمار کیا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں قول اور کلام شمار کیا ہے اور فعل کثیر مفسد ہوتا ہے قلیل مفسد نہیں ہوتا اور کالام قلیل ند ہوتا ہے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اگر چہ کسی کو ترجیح نہیں دی لیکن بعض مشائخ نے جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اصح کہا ہے۔
And if he prompts (fataha) meaning... and if he asks for a prompt (istiftah) and he prompts him in his prayer, it invalidates. Its meaning is that the praying person prompts someone other than his imam, because it is teaching and learning, so it constitutes speech of people. Then the condition of repetition is made in al-Asl because it is not from the acts of prayer, so a little of it is pardoned. Al-Jami' al-Saghir did not stipulate this condition because speech inherently cuts off prayer even if little. ... Explanation: Istiftah is to request a prompt or assistance. Allah says 'yastaftihun' i.e. they ask for victory. Logically, istiftah has divisions. Because the one requesting and the one giving are either both not in prayer, or both in prayer, or only one is in prayer. The first case is outside our discussion. The second case has two subcases: either their prayers are connected (the requester is imam and the giver is muqtadi) or not. The latter subcase will be discussed later. In the second subcase, both prayers are invalidated because it is teaching and learning, which is speech of people and invalidates prayer. The mashayikh... The author of al-Hidayah said that Imam Muhammad wrote in al-Mabsut that if repetition occurs in prompting, prayer is invalid; if not, it is not invalid. The reason is that prompting is an act not from the acts of prayer; if it is excessive (kathir), it invalidates; if little, it does not. One time is little; more is excessive. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, this condition is not present because prompting is speech, and speech invalidates even if little. Thus al-Mabsut considers it an act, while al-Jami' al-Saghir considers it speech. Excessive act invalidates, little not; but speech invalidates even if little. The author of al-Hidayah did not prefer one, but some mashayikh said the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir is more correct.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a person in prayer gives a prompt (laqmah) to someone other than his own imam. The basic ruling is that it invalidates the prayer of both parties if they are both in prayer, because it constitutes teaching and learning, which falls under the category of 'speech of people' (kalam al-nas) that invalidates prayer. The passage then explains the different scenarios of the mustaftih (requester) and fatih (giver) and concludes that if both are in prayer but not as imam and muqtadi (i.e., not in the same prayer), both prayers are invalid. Then an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is presented: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Mabsut makes the invalidation conditional upon repetition (takrar), because he considers prompting an act (fi'l) rather than speech. Acts that are not part of prayer are pardoned if little but invalidate if excessive. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, he does not stipulate repetition because he considers prompting as speech (kalam), which invalidates regardless of quantity. The author of al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, does not give preference, but some later mashayikh (mashayikh) consider the report of al-Jami' al-Saghir as more correct (asahh). The relied-upon position is that prompting a non-imam invalidates prayer even if done once, as it is considered kalam.

Key Terms
لقمہ (laqmah): A prompt or cue given to someone reciting the Quran during prayer.
استفتاح (istiftah): Requesting a prompt or assistance during prayer.
کلام الناس (kalam al-nas): Speech of people that is not dhikr; it invalidates prayer.
مبسوط (al-Mabsut): One of Imam Muhammad's major works, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
جامع صغیر (al-Jami' al-Saghir): Another of Imam Muhammad's works, also part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving a single laqmah to a non-imam during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer of the giver only.
B) It invalidates the prayers of both the giver and the receiver if the act is repeated.
C) It invalidates the prayers of both the giver and the receiver even if done once.
D) It does not invalidate prayer at all.

Key Takeaway
Giving a laqmah to a non-imam invalidates both parties' prayers; the mufta bihi does not require repetition.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on a Muqtadi Prompting His Imam
States that a muqtadi prompting his imam does not invalidate prayer by istihsan and discusses intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prompting the imam does not invalidate prayer, identify the evidence (dalil naqli and istihsan), and explain the correct intention according to al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Prompting your imam is an act of prayer, not speech — necessity overrides analogy.

In congregational prayer, the imam may forget a verse. When a muqtadi (follower) prompts him, is this considered speech that invalidates the prayer? This passage from al-Hidayah resolves the issue using istihsan (juristic preference). Beyond the ruling itself, there is an important intra-Hanafi discussion about what the muqtadi should intend: to prompt or to recite? We will examine the ruling, its proofs, and the correct intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prompting (fat-h) of the imam by the muqtadi. The ruling: it is not considered speech and does not invalidate the prayer, based on istihsan.
The default analogy (qiyas) would treat it as speech, but istihsan intervenes.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith where the Prophet (SAW) approved being prompted by Ubayy ibn Ka'b, plus statements of Ali and Anas. These are the transmitted proofs.
The rational proof: the muqtadi is compelled to correct his prayer, so prompting becomes an act of prayer.
3
Understand the role of istihsan
Istihsan overrides the general rule that speech invalidates prayer. The basis is necessity (darurah) – the muqtadi needs to correct the imam to ensure his own prayer's validity.
This is a clear example of istihsan as a source of law in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyse the ikhtilaf on intention
Some mashayikh held that the muqtadi should intend Quran recitation (tilawah) to make the speech more virtuous. The author of al-Hidayah rejects this, saying he should intend to prompt (laqmah).
The basis: recitation behind the imam is prohibited (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school.
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The correct view: the muqtadi intends to prompt, not to recite. This avoids the prohibited recitation and follows the permitted action.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

If he prompts his imam, it is not considered speech by istihsan, because he is compelled to correct his prayer, so it becomes part of the acts of his prayer. And he should intend to prompt his imam, not recitation; that is correct because he is permitted to prompt and prohibited from recitation. ... This phrase explains the first case promised in the previous issue: if the mustaftih and fatih both are in prayer such that the mustaftih is the imam and the fatih is the muqtadi, then by istihsan it is not speech. The proof of istihsan is the athar narrated: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) recited Surah al-Mu'minun in prayer and missed a word. When he finished, he said, 'Is there among you Ubayy ibn Ka'b?' He said, 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'Why did you not prompt me?' He said, 'I thought it was abrogated.' He said, 'If it were abrogated, I would have informed you.' From this effect it is known that prompting one's imam does not invalidate prayer. And the saying of Ali (RA): 'When the imam asks you for a prompt, prompt him.' And from Anas (RA): 'We used to prompt the imams at the time of the Messenger of Allah (SAW).' The rational proof is that the muqtadi is compelled to correct his prayer, so this prompting becomes part of his prayer's acts. And there is no complete purpose in prayer, so prompting does not invalidate. There is difference among the mashayikh about whether the muqtadi should intend to prompt or to recite. Some said he should intend recitation, not prompting. The author of al-Hidayah said the correct is that he should intend to prompt, not to recite, because he is permitted to prompt and prohibited from recitation. So he should do that which is permitted and avoid what is prohibited.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where a muqtadi gives a prompt to his imam during prayer. The ruling is that by istihsan, this does not invalidate the prayer. Istihsan is based on necessity: the muqtadi is compelled to correct his imam's recitation to ensure the validity of his own prayer. Thus, prompting is considered an act of prayer, not worldly speech. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (SAW) missed a word in Surah al-Mu'minun and asked Ubayy ibn Ka'b why he did not prompt him, indicating that prompting is allowed. Additional support comes from the sayings of Ali (RA) and Anas (RA). The passage then addresses an ikhtilaf about the muqtadi's intention: should he intend to prompt or to recite the Quran? Some scholars said he should intend recitation (tilawah) so that his speech is considered Quran recitation. However, the author of al-Hidayah states that the correct view is to intend to prompt, because prompting is permitted, while recitation by the muqtadi behind an imam is prohibited (according to the Hanafi view). Therefore, he should intend the permitted action and avoid the prohibited one. The mufta bihi is that he intends to prompt.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): A person praying behind an imam (follower).
امام (imam): The leader of congregational prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from clear analogy due to a stronger evidence.
اثر (athar): A report or tradition, often from the Companions or the Prophet.
نیّت (niyyah): Intention, which distinguishes acts of worship from habits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He should intend to recite the Quran.
B) He should intend to prompt the imam.
C) He should intend both.
D) He should intend nothing specific.

Key Takeaway
Prompting the imam does not invalidate prayer; the muqtadi should intend to prompt, not to recite.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prompting the Imam in Prayer: The Hanafi Exception by Necessity
Ruling with proof for prompting the imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why prompting the imam is not considered invalidating speech by istihsan, identify the condition of necessity, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf when the imam moves to another verse.

Core Idea
Necessary prompting is an act of prayer, not speech; it does not invalidate salah.

In the Hanafi school, prayer is invalidated by external speech or excessive action. However, prompting the imam (lughma) when he forgets a verse is a unique exception. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, the reasoning of istihsan, and a disputed sub-case when the imam intentionally skips to another verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that lughma (prompting) is a verbal action. The primary ruling is that it is not considered kalam (speech) that invalidates prayer, by istihsan. Understand the distinction: in normal circumstances, any speech invalidates; but here, necessity makes it an act of prayer.
The passage contrasts two early views: Mabsut considers it action, Jami' al-Saghir considers it speech – the ruling by istihsan overrides the default analogy.
2
Examine the dalil from hadith
Review the hadith where the Prophet (saw) recited Surah al-Mu'minun, omitted a word, and after finishing, asked Ubayy ibn Ka'b why he did not prompt. The Prophet did not reproach him, indicating prompting is permissible and does not invalidate.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for the ruling by istihsan. Also cited: the saying of 'Ali and practice of Anas.
3
Understand the basis of istihsan
Analogy (qiyas) would treat prompting as speech and thus invalidate. However, istihsan (juristic preference) gives priority to necessity: the muqtadi is forced to correct the imam's recitation to save his own prayer, so it becomes part of prayer actions.
This is a classic Hanafi use of istihsan to override qiyas jali (clear analogy).
4
Analyze the sub-case: imam moves to another verse
If the imam abandons the verse he is reciting and moves to a different verse, the necessity for prompting vanishes. In this case, the majority of Hanafis (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the muqtadi's prayer is invalidated, and if the imam accepts the prompt, his prayer also invalidates. Abu Yusuf disagrees, citing the absolute hadith.
The author of Hidayah adopts the majority view. Later mashayikh preferred the narration of Jami' al-Saghir, but the basic permissibility remains.
5
Apply the practical guidance
The muqtadi should not hasten to prompt, and the imam should not force the muqtadi by lingering or repeating verses. The imam should either bow when the obligatory recitation is complete or move to another verse.
This guidance prevents unnecessary speech and protects the prayer's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

یکن جامع صغیر میں یہ شہر دانہیں ہے کیونکہ لقمہ دینا کلام کرنا ہے اور کام کرنا بذات خود مفسد نماز ہے اگر چہ قلیل کیوں نہ ہو۔ حاصل یہ ہے دینے کومبسوط میں فعل شمار کیا ہے اور جامع صغیر میں قول اور کلام شمار کیا ہے اور فعل کثیر مفسد ہوتا ہے قلیل مفسد نہیں ہوتا اور کلام قلیل ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اگر چہ کسی کو ترجیح نہیں دی لیکن بعض مشائخ نے جامع صغیر کی روایت کو اصح کہا ہے۔ مقتدی کا اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینے کا حکم
فتح على امامه لم يكن كلاما استحسانا لانه مضطر الى اصلاح صلاته فكان هذا من اعمال صلاته وينوى الفتح على امامه دون القراءة هو الصحيح لانه مرخص فيه و قراء ته ممنوع عنها
عہ اور اگر مقتدی نے اپنے امام کو لقمہ دیا تو یہ کلام نہ ہوگا ( اور یہ حکم ) استحسانی ہے کیونکہ مقتدی اپنی نماز درست کرنے کی طرف مجبور اس لئے یا لقمہ دینا معنی اس کی نماز کے اعمال میں سے ہو گیا اور مقتدی اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینے کی نیت کرے نہ کہ قرآت قرآن کی یہی نا ہے کیونکہ لقمہ دینا ایسا امر ہے جس کی اجازت دی گئی ہے اور مقتدی کا قرآن پڑھنا ایسا امر ہے کہ اس سے منع کیا گیا ہے۔ رح اس عبارت میں پہلی صورت جس کا گذشتہ مسئلہ میں وعدہ کیا گیا تھا اس کا بیان ہے یعنی اگر مستفتح اور فاتح دونوں کی نماز دو بایں طور کو مستفتح امام فاتح اور مقتدی ہو تو یہ استحسانا کلام نہ ہو گا دلیل استحسان وہ اثر ہے جس کو روایت کیا گیا ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قرأ فى الصلوة سورة المؤمنين فترك منها كلمته فلما فرغ منها قال صلى الله عليه وسلم سوبكن فيكم ابي بن كعب فقال بلى يارسول الله فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم هلا فتحت فقال ظننت انها نسخت قال عليه السلام لو نسخت لا نبأتكم لعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز میں سورہ مومنون پڑھی اور ایک کلمہ چھوڑ دیا پس جب آپ ا نا ہوئے تو فرمایا کہ تم نے لقمہ کیوں نہیں دیا۔ ابی بن کعب نے کہا کہ میں نے خیال کیا کہ یہ کلمہ منسوخ ہو گیا ہے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا اگر سنون ہوتا تو میں تم کو ضرور خبر کرتا۔ ( عنایہ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینا مفسد نماز نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کا قول ہے کہ اذا استطعمك الامام فاطعمة یعنی جب امام تجھ سے لقمہ مانگے تو اس کو لقمہ دو ۔ (فتح تی) حضرت انس رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ ہم لوگ زمانہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم میں اماموں کو لقمہ دیتے تھے۔ (حاکم) ایل نقلی یہ ہے کہ مقتدی اپنی نماز درست کرنے کی طرف مجبور ہے لہذا یہ لقمہ دینا معنی اس کی نماز کے اعمال میں سے ہوگا۔ اور نماز کا کوئی تمل مقصد نہیں ہے اس لئے لقمہ دینا مفسد نہیں ہو گا۔
مشائخ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ مقتدی اپنے امام کو لقمہ دینے کی نیت کرے یا قرآت قرآن کی نیت کرے بعض نے کہا کہ تاروت اور قرآت کی نیت کرے نہ کہ لقمہ دینے کی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ صحیح یہ ہے کہ لقمہ دینے کی نیت کرے نہ کہ قرآت قرآن کی یانہ مقتدی کولقمہ دینے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ اور قرآت کرنے سے روکا گیا ہے اس لئے جس چیز کی اجازت اس کو دی گئی ہے اس کو چھوڑا کر وہ کام نہ کرنے جس سے اس کو روکا گیا ہے یعنی قرآت کی نیت نہ کر ہے۔
لقمہ دینے میں جلد بازی سے کام لیا اور امام دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا ترجمہ پر تو لقمہ دینے والے کی نماز کا حکم
ولو كان الإمام انتقل الى آية اخرى تفسد صلوة الفاتح، وتفسد صلوة الامام لو اخذ بقوله لوجود التلف والتلقن من غير ضرورة وينبغي للمقتدى ان لا يعجل بالفتح وللامام ان لا يلجئهم اليه بل يركع اذاج اوانه او ينتقل الى أية أخرى
اور ابو یوسف امام ابو یوسف جواب اور استر تشریح :
ترجمہ اور اگر امام دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا تو لقمہ دینے والے کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر امام نے اس کے قول کو کیا لا اله الا تو امام کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مقتدی کا تلقین کرنا اور امام کو اس کا لینا بلا ضرورت کے پایا گیا۔ اور مقتدی کے لئے مناسب یہ کیا ہوگا اگر تا که و ہ ائمہ دینے میں جلدی نہ کرے اور امام کو چاہئے کہ مقتدیوں کو لقمہ دینے پر مجبور نہ کرے بلکہ رکوع کر دے جبکہ اس کا وقت آگیا ہے کے نزدیک نماز کالام معنی موضور دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام جس آیت پر انکا تھا وہ نکلی نہیں بلکہ وہ دوسری آیت پڑھنے لگا۔ پھر مقتدی نے لقمہ دیا تو لقمہ دیا اپنے نماز میں ہو والے کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر امام نے اس کے لقمہ کو لے لیا تو امام کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقتدی کی کرنا معنی موضوع لیہ سے تلقین اور امام کی طرف سے تلقین بلاضرورت پایا گیا اس لئے انتسان تو رہا نہیں البتہ بمقتضائے قیاس یہ کلام مفسد ہو جائے گا۔ الا اللہ کہنے سے یہ خیال رہے کہ یہ بعض مشائخ کا قول ہے جس کو مصنف ہدایہ نے اختیار کیا ہے اور بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ نہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگی ۔ طرفین کی مقتدی کی یعنی نہ لقمہ دینے والے کی فاسد ہوگی اور نہ لقمہ لینے والے امام کی فاسد ہوگی کیونکہ سابق میں جو اثر ان رسول اللہ فرنی ہو گیا اور مشترک الصلوۃ سورۃ المؤمنين گزارا ہے وہ مطلق ہے اور اس کے اطلاق کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ لقمہ دینے والے اور امام کی نماز کسی حال کیا ارادہ کیا تو اس کو فاسد نہ ہو۔
الناس چونکہ مفسداً صاحب ہدایہ نے امام اور مقتدی دونوں کو ہدایت فرمائی ہے چنانچہ فرمایا کہ مقتدی لقمہ دینے میں جلدی نہ کرے اور امام مقتدیوں کا صاحب عنا دینے پر مجبور نہ کرے مثلاً بار بار کسی آیت کو لوٹا تارہے یا خاموش کھڑا رہ جائے ایسا نہ کرے بلکہ جب مقدار مفروض یعنی امام صاحب اعتراض یہ نزدیک ایک آیت اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تین آیات پڑھ چکا تو رکوع کر دے اور بعض حضرات نے قرآت مستحب کا اعتبار کیا ہے حالانکہ اس وقت جب قرآت مستحب کر چکا تو رکوع کر دے یا امام دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے یعنی جس آیت پر انکا ہے اس کو چھوڑ کر دوسری نے فرمایا حالانکہ آپ شروع کر دے حاصل یہ کہ ان کو لقمہ دینے پر مجبور نہ کرے۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. In Jami' al-Saghir it [is stated] that [lughma] is not [invalidating] because giving a lughma is speech, and action itself invalidates prayer even if it is little. The summary: In Mabsut, it is considered an action, and in Jami' al-Saghir, it is considered speech and utterance. And a lot of action invalidates, little does not, and a little speech invalidates. The author of Hidayah did not give preference, but some mashayikh said the narration of Jami' al-Saghir is more correct. The ruling of a muqtadi prompting his imam: Prompting his imam is not speech by istihsan because he is forced to correct his prayer, so it becomes from his prayer actions. And he intends prompting his imam, not recitation; that is correct because it is permitted, and his recitation is prohibited. And if the muqtadi prompted his imam, it will not be speech (and this ruling) is by istihsan because the muqtadi is forced to correct his prayer, so prompting becomes from his prayer actions. And the muqtadi should intend prompting his imam, not recitation of Quran; that is correct because prompting is permitted, and the muqtadi's recitation is prohibited. In this phrase, the first case that was promised in the previous issue is explained: if mustaftah and fatih both are in prayer in a way that mustaftah is imam, fatih is muqtadi, then by istihsan it will not be speech. The proof of istihsan is the athar narrated: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) recited Surah al-Mu'minun in prayer and left out a word. When he finished, he said, 'Is there among you Ubayy ibn Ka'b?' He said, 'Yes, O Messenger of Allah.' He said, 'Why did you not prompt me?' He said, 'I thought it was abrogated.' He (peace be upon him) said, 'If it were abrogated, I would have informed you.' (Inayah) From this athar it is known that prompting one's imam does not invalidate prayer. And the saying of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'When the imam asks you for a prompt, give it to him.' (Fath, etc.) Anas (may Allah be pleased with him) narrated: 'We used to prompt the imams during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' (Hakim) The meaning of the proof: The muqtadi is forced to correct his prayer, so this prompting becomes from his prayer actions. And there is no worldly purpose in it, so prompting does not invalidate. There is disagreement among the mashayikh whether the muqtadi intends prompting or recitation of Quran. Some said he intends recitation, not prompting. The author of Hidayah said the correct is that he intends prompting, not recitation, because prompting is permitted and recitation is prohibited. So he should leave what is permitted and not do what is prohibited, i.e., not intend recitation. The ruling on the prompt of one who hastens and the imam moves to another verse: 'And if the imam moved to another verse, the prayer of the prompter becomes invalid, and the prayer of the imam becomes invalid if he takes his saying, because there is speech and prompting without necessity. And it is proper for the muqtadi not to hasten in prompting, and for the imam not to force them to prompt, but rather to bow when its time comes or move to another verse.' (Abu Yusuf, Imam Abu Yusuf, answer and explanation). Translation: And if the imam moved to another verse, the prayer of the prompter becomes invalid, and if the imam acted upon his saying, then the imam's prayer also becomes invalid, because the muqtadi's prompting and the imam's taking it occurred without necessity. And it is appropriate for the muqtadi not to hasten in prompting, and the imam should not compel the muqtadis to prompt, but rather bow when its time comes, or move to another verse. Explanation: The case is that the imam has not left the verse he was reciting but started another verse. Then the muqtadi prompted, so the prayer of the muqtadi becomes invalid. And if the imam accepted his prompt, his prayer also becomes invalid. The evidence: The muqtadi's prompting is a verbal response to the muqtadi's need, and the imam's taking it is without necessity, so it is not like ijtihad; rather by analogy this speech invalidates. Saying 'la ilaha illallah', note that this is the saying of some mashayikh which the author of Hidayah chose, and some say that neither the imam's prayer becomes invalid nor the muqtadi's, because the previous athar about the Prophet (saw) in Surah al-Mu'minun is absolute, and its absoluteness requires that the prompters and imam's prayer are not invalidated in any case. Because it is invalidating? The author of Hidayah gave guidance to both imam and muqtadi: he said the muqtadi should not hasten in prompting, and the imam should not force the muqtadis to prompt, for example by repeating a verse many times or standing silent; rather when he has recited the obligatory amount (according to Abu Hanifa one verse, according to the Sahibayn three verses) he should bow, and some considered the preferred recitation, so when he has completed the preferred recitation he should bow, or the imam should move to another verse, i.e., leave the verse he is on and start another. The conclusion is that he should not force them to prompt.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings of a muqtadi (follower) prompting (lughma) the imam during prayer. The passage type is a ruling with proof, specifically an expansion of a ruling from the Hidayah. The author first notes a difference between two early Hanafi sources: al-Mabsut considers giving a lughma to be an action, while al-Jami' al-Saghir considers it speech. This distinction matters because a small action does not invalidate prayer, but small speech does. The author of Hidayah does not choose between them, but some later mashayikh prefer the view of al-Jami' al-Saghir. The main ruling: a muqtadi prompting his imam is not considered invalidating speech (kalam) by istihsan (juristic preference) because the muqtadi is forced (mudtar) to correct his prayer; thus it becomes part of his prayer actions. The hadith of the Prophet (saw) with Ubayy ibn Ka'b is cited as evidence: the Prophet prompted Ubayy to continue recitation, and did not reproach him. Additionally, the acts of 'Ali and Anas are mentioned. The passage then clarifies that the muqtadi should intend prompting, not Quran recitation, because prompting is permitted while recitation by the follower is prohibited in prayer (since the follower must listen). Then a sub-case: if the imam moves to another verse (i.e., he abandons the verse he was reciting and starts a different one), and the muqtadi still prompts, the muqtadi's prayer becomes invalid because his prompt is no longer necessary; it becomes speech without need. If the imam accepts that prompt, his prayer also becomes invalid. There is disagreement among later scholars on whether the prayer becomes invalid in this case; some say the absolute hadith indicates permissibility in all cases. Finally, the author gives practical guidance: the muqtadi should not hasten, and the imam should not force the muqtadi by lingering or repeating verses; rather, after reciting the obligatory amount, the imam should bow or move to another verse. This shows the Hanafi concern for avoiding situations that cause unnecessary speech in prayer.

Key Terms
لقمہ (lughma): A prompt given by a muqtadi to the imam when the imam pauses or forgets a word in Quran recitation during prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from qiyas (analogy) for a stronger evidence (necessity, ease). Here, analogy would deem prompting as speech, but istihsan permits it due to necessity.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a muqtadi prompting his imam during prayer?
A) It is invalidating speech (kalam) and breaks the prayer.
B) It is permitted and not considered invalidating speech because of necessity (istihsan).
C) It is prohibited (haram) but does not break the prayer.
D) It is only allowed if the muqtadi intends Quran recitation.

Key Takeaway
Necessary prompting of the imam is an exception to the rule that speech invalidates prayer, based on the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b and the Hanafi principle of istihsan.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Responding with 'La Ilaha Illallah' in Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on responding in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and Abu Yusuf regarding responding with 'la ilaha illallah' in prayer, and explain the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.

Core Idea
Responding with 'la ilaha illallah' in prayer invalidates it according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf dissents.

Words that are normally permissible dhikr can become invalidating speech (kalam mufsid) when uttered as a reply. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over saying 'la ilaha illallah' in response to someone during prayer. The difference hinges on whether the context of a reply changes the legal nature of the utterance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is responding to another person with the phrase 'la ilaha illallah' while in salah. The dispute is whether this invalidates the prayer.
Consider that the same words could be recited as dhikr without breaking prayer.
2
State the positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: invalidating (kalam mufsid). Abu Yusuf: not invalidating, because the words are glorification (thana').
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the proofs (dalil) for each
For Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the utterance is in the form of a reply (makhraj al-jawab), so it becomes speech like other replies (e.g., yarhamukallah). For Abu Yusuf: the wording is intrinsically dhikr; intention does not change its essence.
Qiyas on other response utterances (e.g., blessing a sneezer) is invoked.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If invalidating: the prayer must be repeated. If not invalidating: the prayer remains valid without compensation.
The difference affects only the need to repeat the prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the response invalidates the prayer. This is the view recorded in the zahir al-riwayah and adopted by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
A mufti should follow this position unless a stronger contrary argument emerges.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو اجاب في الصلوة رجلا بلا اله الا الله فهذا كلام مفسد عند ابي حنيفة و محمد و قال ابويوسف لا يك مفسد او هذا الخلاف فيما اذا اراد به جوابه له انه ثناء بصيغته فلا يتغير بغريمته ولهما انه اخرج الذا نزد يك فاسد نہیں: مخرج الجواب و هو يحتملة فيجعـل جـوابـا كالتشميت والاسترجاع على الخلاف فی الصدر طرفین کی موافقت كہ فساد ہوتی ۔ شمس الائمہ پر پہنچ گئے تھے پر صاحب ہدایہ نے كم اختلاف ہے چنانچہ
And if he responded in prayer to a man with 'la ilaha illallah', then this is invalidating speech according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: it is not invalidating. And this difference is when he intended it as a response to him, because it is glorification in its form, so it does not change by the intention of response. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) that he brought it out in the form of a response, and it is possible, so it is made a response, like saying 'yarhamukallah' (blessing) and 'inn? lillah' (condolence) according to the difference in the earlier [positions] of the two parties, that it causes invalidity. Shams al-A'immah had reached, but the author of Hidayah had little difference, accordingly...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who, during prayer, responds to someone else by saying 'la ilaha illallah'. The majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) holds that this is invalidating speech (kalam mufsid) because the utterance is in response to another person, thus it is not pure dhikr but a reply. Abu Yusuf argues that it is not invalidating because the wording itself is glorification (thana'), and the intention to respond does not change its nature as dhikr. The author notes that Abu Yusuf compares it to saying 'yarhamukallah' (to someone who sneezes) or 'inna lillah' (upon hearing news of death), which also have differences of opinion. The text appears to reference Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani, who may have supported Abu Yusuf's view, but the Hidayah's author (al-Marghinani) seems to side with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The practical outcome: according to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), such a response invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
كلام مفسد (kalam mufsid): Speech that invalidates prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, certain utterances (like responding to someone) nullify the validity of the prayer.
ثناء (thana'): Glorification or praise of Allah. Here, 'la ilaha illallah' is considered a form of thana' by Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what happens if a person in prayer responds to someone with 'la ilaha illallah'?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer remains valid but requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The prayer is void only if the person intended it as a response.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, responding with 'la ilaha illallah' during prayer invalidates it, because the context of a reply transforms even dhikr into invalidating speech (kalam mufsid).

Ruling on Talqin (Prompting) in Prayer
Ruling on follower prompting imam to another verse in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin in prayer and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its effect on validity.

Core Idea
Prompting the imam without necessity invalidates the prayer of both prompter and imam.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on talqin (prompting) during prayer. The passage from Al-Hidayah addresses what happens when the imam recites incorrectly and a follower prompts him. The relied-upon position declares both prayers invalid due to unnecessary speech, but some later scholars disagree based on an athar. We will explore the proof, the dispute, and the practical guidance given.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Understand the situation described: the imam recites a different verse than intended, and a follower prompts him. Note the consequence: the prompter's prayer is invalidated, and if the imam accepts, his too.
The ruling applies only when talqin occurs 'without necessity' (min ghayr darurah).
2
Understand the reasoning (talil) behind invalidation
The text states that talqin constitutes 'talk' (talf) and 'prompting' (talaqqun) without necessity, which is prohibited speech in prayer, thus invalidating.
This is based on qiyas (analogy) to other forms of unnecessary speech.
3
Recognize the opposing view and its proof
Some later mashayikh (Hanafi scholars) argue that neither prayer is invalidated, citing an athar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowed prompting. This athar is considered by them to override the general analogy.
The athar is quoted incompletely in the text: 'Inna Rasul Allah…'
4
See the author's tarjih and practical guidance
Al-Marghinani (author of Al-Hidayah) prefers the invalidation view from Zahir al-Riwayah. He then advises both parties: the follower should not hasten to prompt, and the imam should not force them; instead, if the obligatory recitation is done, the imam should bow or move to another verse.
This guidance aims to prevent talqin altogether, preserving the sanctity of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصلوة وما يكره فيها
ولَوْ كَانَ الإِمَامُ انْتَقَلَ إِلَى آيَةٍ أُخْرَى تَفْسُدُ صَلَاةُ الْفَاتِحِ، وَتَفْسُدُ صَلَاةُ الْإِمَامِ لَوْ أَخَذَ بِقَوْلِهِ لِوُجُودِ التَّلْفِ وَالتَّلَقُّنِ مِنْ غَيْرِ ضَرُورَةٍ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْمُقْتَدِي أَنْ لَا يَعْجَلَ بِالْفَتْحِ وَلِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُلْجِئَهُمْ إِلَيْهِ بَلْ يَرْكَعَ إِذَا جَاوَزَ أَوَانَهُ أَوْ يَنْتَقِلَ إِلَى آيَةٍ أُخْرَى

تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام جس آیت پر تھا وہ نہیں پڑھی بلکہ دوسری آیت پڑھنے لگا۔ پھر مقتدی نے لقمہ دیا تو لقمہ دینے والے کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر امام نے اس کے لقمہ کو لے لیا تو امام کی نماز بھی فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقتدی کی طرف سے تلقین اور امام کی طرف سے تلقین بلا ضرورت پائی گئی، اس لیے یہ کلام مفسد ہو گا۔ البتہ بمقتضائے قیاس یہ کلام مفسد ہو گا۔ اور بعض مشائخ کا قول یہ ہے کہ نہ امام کی نماز فاسد ہوگی اور نہ مقتدی کی، کیونکہ سابق میں جو اثر "إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قرأ فرنی" اور "مشترک الصلوۃ سورۃ المؤمنين" ہے وہ مطلق ہے اور اس کے اطلاق کا تقاضہ ہے کہ لقمہ دینے والے اور امام کی نماز فاسد نہ ہو۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام اور مقتدی دونوں کو ہدایت فرمائی: مقتدی لقمہ دینے میں جلدی نہ کرے اور امام مقتدیوں کو لقمہ دینے پر مجبور نہ کرے، بلکہ جب مقدار مفروض پڑھ چکا تو رکوع کر دے یا دوسری آیت کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے۔
Prayer and what is disliked therein. If the imam moved to another verse, the prayer of the prompter is invalidated, and the prayer of the imam is invalidated if he accepts his statement due to the presence of talk (speech) and prompting without necessity. And it is befitting for the follower not to hasten in prompting, and for the imam not to compel them to it, but rather to bow when its time has passed or to move to another verse. Explanation: The scenario is that the imam was on a verse but did not recite it and began reciting another verse. Then the follower prompted him. So the prayer of the prompter becomes invalid, and if the imam accepts his prompt, the imam's prayer also becomes invalid. The proof is that prompting from the follower and taking by the imam occurred without necessity, so this speech becomes invalidating. However, by analogy, this speech is invalidating. And some mashayikh hold that neither the imam's prayer nor the follower's prayer becomes invalid, because the earlier athar 'Indeed the Messenger of Allah recited...' and 'common prayer in Surah al-Mu'minun' is absolute, and its absoluteness requires that the prayer of the prompter and imam not be invalid. The author of Hidayah gave guidance to both: the follower should not hasten in prompting, and the imam should not compel them to prompt, but rather when he has recited the obligatory amount, he should bow or move to another verse.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding talqin (prompting) in prayer. It addresses the situation where the imam recites incorrectly or hesitates, and a follower prompts him by reciting the correct verse. The ruling stated in the matn is that if the imam moves to another verse (i.e., abandons the verse he was on and starts another), then the prompter's prayer is invalidated. Additionally, if the imam accepts the prompt and repeats it, his prayer is also invalidated. The reasoning is that this constitutes speech (talk) and prompting without necessity, which is prohibited in prayer. The text then mentions a difference of opinion: some mashayikh argue that neither prayer is invalidated, citing an athar (narrative) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) recited 'Farnee' or a common prayer in Surah al-Mu'minun, which indicates that such prompting was allowed. However, the author of Al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, opts for the ruling of invalidation, as reflected in the matn. He then advises both the imam and the follower: the follower should not rush to prompt, and the imam should not force the congregation to prompt him. Instead, if the imam has completed the obligatory recitation (one verse according to Abu Hanifa, three verses according to the Sahibayn), he should proceed to bowing or move to another verse. This guidance aims to prevent unnecessary speech in prayer. This passage is classified as an intra-Hanafi dispute because of the differing views among later mashayikh.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting the imam by reciting the correct verse when the imam hesitates or makes a mistake.
لقمہ (luqma): The prompt given by the follower to the imam.
مفسد (mufsid): That which invalidates an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a follower prompting the imam in prayer when the imam moves to another verse?
A) Both follower's and imam's prayers are valid.
B) Follower's prayer is invalid, imam's prayer is valid.
C) Both follower's and imam's prayers become invalid if imam accepts the prompt.
D) Only imam's prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Talqin (prompting) in prayer is generally invalidating for both parties, but there is a valid scholarly difference; the mufta bihi is invalidation unless necessity forces otherwise.

Responding with 'La ilaha illallah' in Prayer: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on responsive speech in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on responding with 'La ilaha illallah' in prayer, explain the proof of each side in the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Even dhikr uttered as a response in prayer can invalidate it if intended as speech.

This lesson examines a delicate intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a praying person responds to an external question with the words 'La ilaha illallah'? While the words are pure praise, the context of response changes their legal status. We will explore the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad against Abu Yusuf, and understand why the relied-upon position treats such speech as invalidating.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the exact scenario: a person in prayer hears someone ask 'Is there any deity other than Allah?' and responds with 'La ilaha illallah' intending to answer. Determine the legal question at hand.
The intent (qasd) is critical: if the response is merely informing others of being in prayer, the ruling differs.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the prayer becomes invalid (fasid). Abu Yusuf holds it remains valid. Note that this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not an inter-madhhab one.
All three are Hanafi imams; the dispute is within the school.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that the words are thana' (praise of Allah) in their literal meaning. Praise does not become invalidating by the intention of the speaker; the essence of the speech is dhikr.
He relies on the literal wording (dalalat al-lafz) rather than the context of utterance.
4
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They argue that the speech was uttered in a responsive context (mukhrij al-jawab) and is capable of being a response. Therefore, it is treated as kalam al-nas (human speech), analogous to tasmit (saying 'Yarhamukallah' in reply to a sneeze) and istirja' (saying 'Inna lillah' upon hearing news of death).
The analogy (qiyas) to tasmit and istirja' is central. Both are situations where dhikr-like words become invalidating when used as responses.
5
Determine the tarjih and practical consequence
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, making it the mufta bihi. Thus, in practice, if a praying person responds with 'La ilaha illallah' intending to answer, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: one view saves the prayer, the other requires repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَلَوْ أَجَابَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ رَجُلًا بِلَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ فَهَذَا كَلَامٌ مُفْسِدٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَكُونُ مُفْسِدًا. وَهَذَا الْخِلَافُ فِيمَا إِذَا أَرَادَ بِهِ جَوَابَهُ. لَهُ أَنَّهُ ثَنَاءٌ بِصِيغَتِهِ فَلَا يَتَغَيَّرُ بِغَرَضِهِ. وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ أَخْرَجَهُ مُخْرَجَ الْجَوَابِ وَهُوَ يَحْتَمِلُهُ فَيُجْعَلُ جَوَابًا كَالتَّشْمِيتِ وَالِاسْتِرْجَاعِ، عَلَى الْخِلَافِ فِي الصَّدْرِ.

تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی کے سامنے کسی نے کہا: هَلْ مِنْ إِلَهٍ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ؟ تو مصلی نے سن کر لا إله إلا الله کہا۔ اب یہ کلام دو حال سے خالی نہیں: یا تو اس سے جواب کا قصد کیا ہوگا یا اپنے نماز میں ہونے کی اطلاع کا ارادہ ہوگا۔ اگر دوسری صورت ہے تو اس کا حکم آگے آئے گا۔ اگر پہلی صورت ہے تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ کلام اپنے معنی موضوع لہ کے اعتبار سے ثناء باری ہے، اور ثناء باری نماز کو فاسد نہیں کرتی۔ اور طرفین (ابو حنیفہ اور محمد) کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام کو جواب کے طور پر استعمال کیا گیا ہے اور یہ جواب کا احتمال رکھتا ہے، لہذا اس کو جواب قرار دیا جائے گا، جیسے تشمیت (يرحمك الله) اور استرجاع (انا لله وانا اليه راجعون)۔ البتہ استرجاع میں اختلاف ہے: بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس میں بھی وہی اختلاف ہے، اور بعض نے کہا کہ امام ابو یوسف نے استرجاع کے مفسد ہونے میں طرفین کی موافقت کر لی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کے قول کو اختیار کیا ہے۔
If someone responds in prayer to a man with 'La ilaha illallah', then this is invalidating speech according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf said it is not invalidating. This dispute is when he intended by it to answer him. His proof is that it is praise in its wording, so it does not change by his intent. Their proof is that he uttered it in the context of a response, and it is capable of that, so it is considered a response, like tasmit (saying 'Yarhamukallah') and istirja' (saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un'), with the same dispute in the earlier part. Explanation: The scenario is that someone in front of the praying person said: 'Is there any deity other than Allah?' The praying person heard and said 'La ilaha illallah'. This speech is either intended as a response or as informing that he is in prayer. If the latter, its ruling comes later. If the former, then according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the prayer becomes invalid; according to Abu Yusuf, it does not. Abu Yusuf's proof is that this speech is praise of Allah in its literal meaning, and praise does not invalidate prayer. Their proof is that the speech was uttered in the context of a response and it is capable of that, so it is treated as a response, like tasmit and istirja'. However, regarding istirja', there is a difference: some mashayikh said the same dispute applies, and some said that Abu Yusuf agreed with the two that istirja' is invalidating. The author of Hidayah adopted the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in this issue.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer when a person in prayer responds to someone with the words 'La ilaha illallah'. The scenario is that someone asks a question implying polytheism, and the praying person responds with the declaration of monotheism. The key issue is whether this constitutes invalidating speech (kalam mufsid). Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that it does invalidate the prayer because the speech is used in the context of a response, and any speech in prayer that is not Quran or dhikr intended for prayer is invalidating. They argue that even though the words are praise, the fact that it was uttered as a response to someone makes it kalam al-nas (human speech) and thus invalidating. Abu Yusuf argues that the words themselves are dhikr and praise of Allah, and the intent does not change their literal meaning; therefore, it is not invalidating. The dispute is compared to other cases like tasmit (responding to a sneeze with 'Yarhamukallah') and istirja' (saying 'Inna lillahi...' upon hearing news of death). For istirja', there is a further difference: some scholars apply the same dispute, while others say Abu Yusuf agrees it is invalidating. The author of Al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, favors the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, making it the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana'): Praise of Allah, which is considered beneficial speech in prayer.
تشميت (tasmit): Responding to a sneeze by saying 'Yarhamukallah'. Analogized to this case.
استرجاع (istirja'): Saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' upon hearing news of death. Also analogized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling if a person in prayer responds to someone's question by saying 'La ilaha illallah'?
A) The prayer is valid because it is dhikr.
B) The prayer becomes invalid.
C) The prayer is valid only if the person intended praise.
D) The prayer is invalid only if the imam accepts it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that responding with 'La ilaha illallah' in prayer invalidates it, because the responsive context makes it human speech.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istirja' in Prayer
intra-Hanafi dispute on whether istirja' during prayer invalidates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on istirja' during salah and explain the reasoning behind the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Istirja' in prayer invalidates because it expresses grief, contradicting worship; Abu Yusuf's agreement is disputed.

This passage from al-Hidayah explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement: does saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' (istirja') during prayer invalidate it? The discussion reveals two opinions among later mashayikh regarding Abu Yusuf's stance. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyse how illa (effective cause) is used to distinguish between types of speech in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is saying 'Inna lillahi...' in prayer after hearing news of death. The disputed hukm is whether this invalidates the prayer (fasid) or not.
Istirja' is considered kalam an-nas (human speech) by most Hanafis.
2
Distinguish the two views among the mashayikh
Some mashayikh say the case is mukhtalaf fih: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say invalid, Abu Yusuf says not. Others say it is muttafaq alayh: all three agree it invalidates.
The difference hinges on whether Abu Yusuf changed his view or maintained his earlier position.
3
Understand the reasoning behind invalidation
Istirja' is for expressing grief (izhar al-musiba), which is contrary to the purpose of prayer (worship and praise). Prayer was not prescribed for that, so it invalidates.
Compare with 'la ilaha illallah', which is praise and thus aligns with prayer's purpose.
4
Analyze the author's preference
The author of al-Hidayah says the view that it is disputed (mukhtalaf fih) is correct, meaning the ikhtilaf remains unresolved in his estimation.
This indicates caution: the stronger view (based on reasoning) is that it invalidates, but fatwa may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر مصلی کے سامنے کسی نے کہا کہ فلاں مر گیا پس مصلی نے کہا انا للہ وانا الیه راجعون، تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ یہ صورت بھی مختلف فیہ ہے یعنی طرفین کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فاسد نہیں ہوگی۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ یہ صورت متفق علیہ ہے یعنی امام ابو یوسف نے استرجاع کے مفسد صلوۃ ہونے میں طرفین کی موافقت کی ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک فرق کیا ہے کہ لا الہ الا اللہ مفسد نہیں اور استرجاع مفسد ہے، اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ استرجاع اظہار مصیبت کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور نماز اس کے لئے مشروع نہیں کی گئی اور لا الہ الا اللہ تعظیم اور توحید کے ترجمہ کے لئے ہے، اور نماز کی مشروعیت بھی اسی کے لئے ہے کیونکہ مصلی حمد و ثنا میں مشغول ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ استرجاع منافی صلوۃ ہونے کی وجہ سے مفسد ہے اور لا الہ الا اللہ چونکہ منافی صلوۃ نہیں اس لئے یہ کلمہ مفسد نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مختلف فیہ ہونے کا قول صحیح ہے۔
The author of al-Hidayah said: If someone says to a person in prayer that so-and-so has died, and the person in prayer says 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un', then there is disagreement among the mashayikh (scholars). Some mashayikh said that this case is also disputed: according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the prayer becomes invalid, and according to Abu Yusuf it does not. And some mashayikh said that this case is agreed upon: Abu Yusuf agreed with the two that istirja' invalidates prayer. As for the question of what is the difference according to Abu Yusuf between 'la ilaha illallah' (which he considers non-invalidating) and istirja' (which he considers invalidating), the answer is that istirja' is for expressing grief, and prayer was not prescribed for that; while 'la ilaha illallah' is for glorification and tawhid, and prayer is prescribed for that, because the person in prayer is engaged in praise and thanks. The conclusion is that istirja' invalidates because it is contrary to the nature of prayer, whereas 'la ilaha illallah' does not invalidate because it is not contrary to the nature of prayer. The author of al-Hidayah said that the view that it is disputed (mukhtalaf fih) is correct.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' (istirja') during prayer when one hears news of death. There is a difference of opinion among the later mashayikh: some consider it to be disputed like the previous case (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it invalidates, Abu Yusuf says it does not), while others say it is agreed upon that it invalidates, and even Abu Yusuf agrees because istirja' is fundamentally different from 'la ilaha illallah'. The reasoning is that istirja' is an expression of grief or consolation, which is not part of the purpose of prayer. In contrast, 'la ilaha illallah' is inherently dhikr and praise, which aligns with the purpose of prayer. The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) prefers the view that it is disputed, meaning the same ikhtilaf applies, but he does not clearly state the mufta bihi. However, the weight of the argument suggests that since istirja' is more clearly contrary to prayer, the position that it invalidates is stronger.

Key Terms
استرجاع (istirja'): Saying 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un' upon hearing news of a calamity.
مختلف فیہ (mukhtalaf fih): A ruling that is disputed among the Hanafi imams or later scholars.
متفق علیہ (muttafaq alayh): A ruling that is agreed upon among the Hanafi scholars, i.e., no ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that istirja' invalidates prayer while 'la ilaha illallah' does not?
A) Istirja' is a longer phrase.
B) Istirja' expresses grief, which is opposite to prayer's purpose; 'la ilaha' is praise.
C) Istirja' is not from the Quran.
D) The Prophet specifically forbade istirja' in prayer.

Key Takeaway
Istirja' in prayer invalidates because its purpose (grief) contradicts the worshipful nature of salah, though Abu Yusuf's disagreement remains a valid ikhtilaf.

Using Tasbih to Alert in Prayer Does Not Invalidate
ruling with proof (hadith) and consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that using tasbih to alert others during prayer does not invalidate the prayer, and cite the primary proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Tasbih for alerting in prayer is valid and not speech that invalidates.

A common concern among those learning the rulings of prayer is whether any form of communication during salah breaks it. This lesson addresses a specific allowance: using tasbih (saying 'Subhanallah') or reciting a Quranic verse to alert someone that you are in prayer. The passage establishes the ruling with clear proof and consensus, distinguishing between the methods for men and women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what specific act is being discussed and what the ruling is. The act is using tasbih or a verse to alert another person during prayer. The ruling is that the prayer is not invalidated; it remains valid.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the evidence cited. The proof is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that instructs men to say tasbih and women to clap when something happens during prayer.
The hadith is categorized as ahad, but its meaning is clear and accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling. The imperative 'فليسبح' (let him say tasbih) indicates permissibility (ibaha) in this context, and the Prophet's own practice confirms that such alerting does not constitute invalidating speech.
The command is specific to alerting, not general conversation.
4
Note the consensus (ijma')
The passage states that this ruling is by consensus (bil-ijma'), meaning all Hanafi scholars agree. This strengthens the authority of the ruling.
There is no intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point.
5
Apply the gender distinction
The hadith differentiates between men and women: men use tasbih (verbal), women clap (tasfiq). This avoids distraction from a woman's voice.
The clapping is defined as striking the back of the right hand on the left hand.

This shows that such communication is legitimate and does not break the prayer. The distinction between men and women is clear: men use verbal tasbih, women use clapping. The wisdom is that a woman's voice might be distracting, so she uses physical action instead. This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah and is universally accepted among Hanafis.

Reciting Tasbih to Inform in Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof and consensus on tasbih in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that reciting tasbih or Quran to inform someone in prayer does not invalidate the prayer, and explain the dalil and the basis for the consensus.

Core Idea
Reciting tasbih to inform another in prayer does not invalidate the prayer by consensus.

During salah, one may need to alert another person that they are engaged in prayer. While deliberate worldly speech invalidates prayer, the Hanafi school, along with the consensus, makes an exception for reciting tasbih (SubhanAllah) or Quranic verses with the specific intention of informing. This lesson examines the ruling, the prophetic proof, and the distinction from invalidating speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is reciting tasbih (or Quran) during prayer with the intention to inform another person that you are in prayer. The ruling is that the prayer remains valid (sahih) and is not invalidated.
The ruling is by consensus (ijma), making it a universally accepted exception.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'When an event occurs to any of you in prayer, let him say tasbih.' This hadith is narrated in Bukhari and Muslim and serves as direct evidence.
The hadith instructs men to say tasbih; women are instructed to clap.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'فليسبح' (let him say tasbih) indicates permissibility. Since the Prophet himself instructed such speech during prayer, it cannot be considered invalidating. The essential purpose is to convey a message without engaging in worldly conversation.
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates permissibility unless there is a contrary indicator.
4
Note the consensus
The matn explicitly states 'by consensus' (بالإجماع). This means all scholars agree on this ruling, eliminating any ikhtilaf. The consensus is based on the clear hadith and the absence of any contradiction.
Consensus (ijma) is a primary source of law in the Hanafi school.
5
Distinguish from invalidating speech
Not all speech in prayer is exempt. Uttering words of worldly grief like 'Inna lillah' (istirja) invalidates prayer because it expresses sorrow, which is contrary to the spirit of salah. Reciting tasbih or Quran remains within the bounds of dhikr.
The distinction lies in the intention and the nature of the words: dhikr vs. worldly expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان اراد به اعلامه انه فى الصلوة لم تفسد بالاجماع لقوله عليه السلام اذا نابت احدكم نائبة في الصلوة فليسبح
And if he intends by it to inform him that he is in prayer, it does not invalidate by consensus, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'When an event occurs to any of you in prayer, let him say tasbih.'
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about speech in prayer. The matn states that if a person in prayer recites tasbih or Quran with the specific intention of informing another person that he is currently engaged in prayer, the prayer remains valid by consensus (ijma). The proof is the Prophet's hadith instructing men to say 'SubhanAllah' and women to clap when needing to alert the imam. The commentary (Ashraf al-Hidaya) explains that this is different from saying 'Inna lillah' (istirja'), which invalidates prayer because it expresses grief, while tasbih and tahlil are forms of dhikr consistent with the purpose of prayer. The Hanafi school follows this consensus, and the ruling covers both kalimah tayyibah and Quranic verses used for informing.

Key Terms
استرجاع (istirjā‘): Saying 'Innā lillāhi wa innā ilayhi rāji‘ūn' (to Allah we belong and to Him we shall return), an expression of grief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Prayer is valid

Key Takeaway
Reciting tasbih or Quran with the intention to inform in prayer does not invalidate the prayer, based on prophetic instruction and consensus.

Invalidation of Prayer by Starting Another After One Rak'ah
Ruling that starting another prayer after one rak'ah invalidates the first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that beginning another prayer after one rak'ah invalidates the first, and explain the principle that a valid commencement of a second prayer necessitates exiting the first.

Core Idea
Once you validly intend another prayer, the first is void.

Imagine you have prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr and then decide to switch to Asr or a voluntary prayer. Does your Zuhr continue or is it spoiled? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the very act of beginning another prayer, even with a silent intention, invalidates the first. The reason is that starting a valid new prayer requires you to exit the current one, and that exit renders the first prayer void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is praying one rak'ah of Zuhr and then starting Asr or nafl. The ruling: Zuhr is invalidated (naqaḍa).
Memorize the exact scenario: after one rak'ah, not later.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is 'because his commencement in something else is valid, so he exits (from Zuhr)'. Meaning the second prayer is validly begun, and that act forces exit from the first.
The principle: a valid entrance into a new prayer necessitates exiting the current one, voiding it.
3
Apply to both fard and nafl
The ruling applies whether the second prayer is another fard (Asr) or a voluntary (nafl). No distinction is made.
This extends to any prayer, including qada or sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صلى ركعة من الظهر ثم افتتح العصر و التطوع فقد نقص الظهر لانه صح شروعه في غيره فيخرج
And whoever prays one rak'ah of Zuhr then begins Asr or a voluntary (prayer) has invalidated Zuhr because his commencement in something else is valid, so he exits (from Zuhr).
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This ruling addresses a specific scenario: a person has started Zuhr prayer and performed one rak'ah, then changes his intention to Asr or a nafl prayer. According to the Hanafi school, this new intention is a valid commencement (shurū‘) of another prayer, which necessarily requires exiting the first. Therefore, the Zuhr prayer becomes invalid (bāṭil). The commentary explains that the proof is that the second prayer is validly begun, so it takes him out of the first. There is no distinction between fard and nafl in this regard. The ruling applies whether he physically raises his hands for takbir or merely makes the intention in the heart.

Key Terms
نقص (naqaḍa): In this context, it means 'invalidated' or 'spoiled'.
افتتح (iftataḥa): He begins/commences (a prayer).
شروعه (shurū'uhu): His commencement (into a new prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Zuhr is valid only if you finish the rak'ah first

Key Takeaway
Praying one rak'ah of a fard prayer and then beginning another prayer (fard or nafl) invalidates the first because the valid commencement of the second necessitates exiting the first.

Re-entering the Same Prayer After One Rak'ah
Ruling that repeating intention for the same prayer does not exit it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person re-intends the same obligatory prayer while already in it, and explain why the subsequent intention is void.

Core Idea
Re-intending a prayer you are already in is a void intention; the original prayer continues unchanged.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a person begins Zuhr, completes one rak'ah, and then (perhaps forgetfully) makes a new intention for the same prayer. Does this restart the prayer or invalidate what has been performed? The Hanafi answer is straightforward: the second intention is legally ineffective (laghw), and the prayer continues with the rak'ah already counted. Understanding this ruling clarifies the role of intention (niyyah) as an initiating act, not a continuous requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text describes a person who has already started praying Zuhr and completed one rak'ah, then makes a new intention for Zuhr again.
This is a hypothetical but instructive case from classical fiqh.
2
State the ruling
The prayer remains the same (hiya hiya) and the first rak'ah suffices (yujtaza'u bi-tilka al-rak'ah). The renewed intention has no effect.
The ruling is valid (sahih) and the prayer continues.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The reason given: 'because he intended to begin the very same thing he is in' (li-annahu nawā al-shurū' fī 'ayn mā huwa fīh). Since he is already engaged in that prayer, the new intention is redundant and thus void (laghat niyyatuhu).
The key phrase is 'ayn mā huwa fīh – the exact same act.
4
Determine the effect on the first rak'ah
Because the intention is void and the prayer continues unchanged, the first rak'ah counts toward the total. If he subsequently completes the remaining rak'ahs, the fard is fulfilled.
This contrasts with cases where the intention changes the act itself.
5
Consider practical implications
If the person mistakenly thinks the first rak'ah was invalid and prays four more without sitting for the final tashahhud, his prayer may become invalid due to missing the obligatory sitting. But under the correct understanding, he should continue and complete the prayer normally.
The ruling prevents unnecessary repetition or invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو افتتح الظهر بعد ما صلى منها ركعة فهى هى و يجتزئ بتلك الركعة لانه نوی الشروع فی عين ما هو فيه فلغت نيته و بقى المنوى على حال
And if he begins Zuhr after having prayed from it one rak'ah, then it is the same (prayer) and that rak'ah suffices, because he intended to begin the very same thing he is in, so his intention becomes void and the intended remains as it was.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This ruling contrasts with the previous one. If a person has started Zuhr and performed one rak'ah, then (perhaps forgetfully) makes a new intention for Zuhr again, the second intention is ineffective because he is already in that prayer. The rak'ah he already performed counts towards the total. The commentary explains that the intention (niyyah) is for the exact same act (ayn mā huwa fīh), so it is لغو (lāghw, void). The prayer continues as before. This has practical consequences: if he then prays a total of four rak'ahs (including the first one), the fard is fulfilled. But if he mistakenly thinks the first rak'ah was invalid and prays four more without sitting for the final tashahhud (qa‘dah akhīrah), his prayer may become invalid if the obligatory sitting is missed.

Key Terms
لغت نيته (laghat niyyatuhu): His intention becomes void (lāghw) because it has no effect on the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
You pray one rak'ah of Zuhr, then (thinking you haven't started) intend Zuhr again. What happens?
A) The first rak'ah is invalid; you start over
B) The first rak'ah counts; you continue
C) You must repeat both rak'ahs
D) The prayer becomes nafl

Key Takeaway
Re-intending an obligatory prayer while already in it has no effect; the prayer continues with the already performed rak'ahs.

Reciting from the Mus-haf During Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation from mus-haf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa rules that reciting from the mus-haf invalidates prayer, contrast it with the Sahibayn's position, and identify the mufta bihi ruling in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: excessive action invalidates; Sahibayn: combining worships is valid but makruh; later school follows Sahibayn.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: does an imam's recitation from the mus-haf (physical Quran) during prayer invalidate the prayer? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the actions required—holding, looking, turning pages—constitute 'amal kathīr, which breaks the unity of prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that both recitation and looking at the mus-haf are acts of worship, so combining them is permissible, albeit disliked due to resemblance to the People of the Book. By studying this dispute, you will understand how different usul principles—the definition of 'amal kathīr, the nature of worship, and qiyas—lead to divergent rulings within the same school.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Identify the ruling: reciting from the mus-haf invalidates the prayer. Note the dalil: the actions are excessive (amal kathīr) and learning from the mus-haf is analogous to talqīn from another person.
The key term here is 'amal kathīr.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
State that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the prayer is valid but disliked. Their dalil: combining two acts of worship (recitation and looking) does not invalidate; the dislike is due to resemblance to Ahl al-Kitāb.
3
Compare the proofs
Contrast the two lines of reasoning. Abu Hanifa focuses on the physical actions; the Sahibayn focus on the spiritual nature of the acts. Identify the illa (effective cause) for each.
Consider: which approach gives more weight to the physical vs. the spiritual?
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's response to the Sahibayn is that the physical actions are indeed excessive and the analogy to talqīn holds. Note that the Sahibayn do not directly respond to this; rather, they view the actions as part of worship.
How does the difference in defining 'amal kathīr affect the ruling?
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
Later Hanafi practice follows the Sahibayn: valid but makruh. The practical consequence: the imam's prayer does not need to be repeated, but it is discouraged.
Why might the later school prefer this view?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا قرأ الامام من المصحف فسدت صلاته عند ابي حنيفة وقالا هى تامة لانه عبادة انضافت الى عبادة الا انه بكره لانه يشبه بصنع اهل الكتاب ولابي حنيفة ان حمل المصحف والنظر فيه وتقليب الأوراق عمل كثير ولانه الفن من المصحف فصار كما اذا تلقن من غيره
When the imam recites from the mus-haf, his prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is complete, because it is an act of worship added to worship, except that it is disliked (makruh) because it resembles the practice of the People of the Book. And for Abu Hanifa is that holding the mus-haf, looking into it, and turning the pages is excessive action, and because he learns from the mus-haf, so it becomes like when one learns from someone else.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam reciting directly from the Quran (mus-haf) during prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the prayer is invalid (fāsid) because the actions involved—holding the mus-haf, looking at it, and turning pages—constitute excessive movement (amal kathīr), which breaks the prayer. Additionally, receiving recitation from the mus-haf is analogous to learning from another person (talqīn), which is not allowed in prayer. The two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad al-Shaybānī), however, rule that the prayer is valid but disliked (makrūh tanzīhan), because recitation and looking at the mus-haf are both acts of worship; combining two worships does not invalidate. The dislike is due to resemblance to the practice of the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitāb). The commentary notes that according to Abu Hanifa's reasoning, there is no difference between a mus-haf placed on a stand (mawḍū‘) and one held in the hands. According to the disciples' view, there is a difference (holding is worse). The relied-upon position in later Hanafi fatwa is the view of the Sahibayn, as it is more lenient and widespread.

Key Terms
عمل كثير (‘amal kathīr): Excessive physical action that breaks the unity of prayer, such as multiple movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning, which of the following is the primary reason reciting from the mus-haf invalidates prayer?
A) It is disrespectful to the Quran.
B) It involves holding, looking, and turning pages—excessive action.
C) It distracts the worshipper.
D) It is not permitted by the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the muftā bihi (relied-upon) position is that reciting from the muṣ-ḥaf during prayer is valid but makrūh tanzīhan; the earlier view of Abū Ḥanīfa that it invalidates is not acted upon in fatwa.
