Renewing Intention in the Same Prayer Without Takbir
Ruling and proof for renewing intention during the same prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on renewing intention during prayer without takbir and explain the rational proof that the second intention is void.

Core Idea
An extra intention in the same prayer is ineffective; what is already valid remains.

What happens if you are already praying Zuhr and, after one rak'ah, you verbally intend Zuhr again without a new takbir? Does this break your prayer? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the principle that one cannot validly intend what one is already doing. This lesson examines the ruling and its rational proof, including the practical consequence if the person mistakenly adds an extra rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
A person in the middle of Zuhr prayer intends Zuhr again without saying takbir. The ruling: the second intention is disregarded, and the prayer continues normally.
The second intention does not exit the person from the first prayer.
2
Understand the proof
The proof is rational: one cannot validly intend an act one is already performing; the intention is inherently superfluous (laghw).
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Apply the ruling to consequences
If the person then prays three more rak'ahs, Zuhr is complete. If he prays four more without sitting after the third, the prayer becomes invalid due to missing the final sitting.
The first rak'ah counts; the mistake is in the extra rak'ah.
4
Note the legal subtlety
The second intention does not constitute a new prayer because it was not accompanied by takbir tahrimah. It is merely a verbal expression with no effect.
The niyyah itself is always in the heart; verbal repetition is inconsequential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر ظہر کی ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد پھر ظہر کی نماز شروع کی تو یہ دوسری نماز وہی پہلی نماز ہے اور وہ رکعت محسوب ہوگی کیونکہ مصلی نے شروع کرنے کی نیت کی ایسے فرض میں کہ وہ بعینہ وہی ہے جس میں موجود ہے تو اس کی نیت لغو ہو گئی اور جس کی نیت کی ہے وہ اپنی حالت پر باقی رہا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ پہلے ظہر شروع کر کے اس میں سے ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد پھر دوبارہ اس ظہر کی نیت سے تکبیر تحریمہ کہے بغیر زبان سے نیت کئے ہوئے تو یہ دوسری نماز پہلی نماز ہے یعنی پہلی نماز سے خارج نہ ہوگا اور جو رکعت پڑھ چکا وہ بھی شمار ہو گئی حتی کہ اگر اس کے بعد تین رکعتیں پڑھیں تو فریضہ ظہر ادا ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس کے بعد چار رکعتیں پڑھیں اس گمان کے ساتھ کہ پہلی رکعت باطل ہو گئی اور تیسری رکعت پر بیٹا بھی نہیں تو قعدہ اخیرہ کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصلی نے بعینہ اس چیز کو شروع کرنے کی نیت کی ہے جس میں وہ پہلے سے موجود ہے اس لئے اس کی نیت لغو ہو گئی اور جس کی نیت کی وہ اپنی حالت پر باقی رہا۔
And if after performing one rak'ah of Zuhr, he then starts Zuhr prayer (again), then this second prayer is the same as the first prayer, and that rak'ah will be counted. Because the person intended to start in the same obligation that he is already in, so his intention becomes void, and what he intended remained in its state. Explanation: The issue is that he started Zuhr, and after performing one rak'ah, he again intends this Zuhr without saying the takbir tahrimah and without verbal intention, so this second prayer is the first prayer; he does not exit the first prayer, and the rak'ah he performed counts. So if he then prays three rak'ahs, the Zuhr obligation will be fulfilled. And if he prays four rak'ahs after that, thinking that the first rak'ah was invalid, and he does not sit for the third rak'ah, then his prayer becomes invalid due to missing the final sitting. The proof is that the person intended to start exactly what he is already in, so his intention becomes void, and what he intended remains in its state.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the effect of renewing intention during prayer without a new takbir. The passage states that if a person already engaged in Zuhr prayer intends Zuhr again verbally, the second intention is superfluous and the prayer continues as before. The commentary clarifies that the rakah already performed counts, and if the person mistakenly prays an extra rak'ah without sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid due to missing the final sitting. The proof is rational: one cannot validly intend what one is already doing.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
لغو (laghw): Void, futile, of no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person intending Zuhr, after one rak'ah, verbally intends Zuhr again without takbir?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) The second intention is ignored and prayer continues.
C) The first rak'ah is invalidated.
D) The prayer becomes nafl.

Key Takeaway
Renewing intention for the same prayer without takbir has no effect; the prayer remains valid as long as its structure is not altered.

Looking at Written Text and Understanding in Prayer
Ruling that understanding written text without vocalizing does not invalidate prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on looking at written text during prayer and explain why it does not invalidate based on the absence of excessive action.

Core Idea
Understanding without action does not invalidate prayer; invalidation requires excessive physical action.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: during prayer, a person looks at a written text (other than the Quran) and understands its meaning without vocalization. Does this invalidate the prayer? The Hanafi ruling is clear: it does not. We'll explore the reasoning, an intra-school difference, and the key principle that prayer invalidation hinges on excessive action (kathir al-‘amal), not mere understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is looking at a written text (other than Quran) and understanding it during prayer, without speaking. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih) and not invalidated by consensus.
2
Distinguish from the oath scenario
The passage contrasts this with an oath: if one swears not to read a book, understanding alone may break the oath (according to Muhammad). This shows that the same action (understanding) has different implications in different legal contexts.
The purpose (maqsad) in oaths is understanding; in prayer, invalidation depends on excessive action.
3
Apply the principle of excessive action
The underlying reason: invalidation of prayer requires kathir al-‘amal (excessive physical action). Looking and understanding is not an action of the body, so it does not invalidate.
This is based on the general rule that prayer is only invalidated by major actions, not by mental acts or minor movements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو نظر إلى مكتوب وفهمه فالصحيح انه لا تفسد صلاته بالاجماع بخلاف ما اذا حلف لا يقرأ كتابا فإنه يحنث بالفهم عند محمد لان المقصود هنالك الفهم اما فساد الصلاة فبالعمل الكثير ولم يوجد. ترجمہ: اور اگر مصلی نے (قرآن کے علاوہ) کسی لکھی ہوئی چیز کی طرف دیکھا اور اس کو سمجھ بھی لیا تو صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ بالاجماع اس کی نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اس کے برخلاف جب اس نے قسم کھائی کہ فلاں کی کتاب نہیں پڑھے گا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فقط سمجھنے سے حانث ہوجائیگا کیونکہ یہاں مقصود سمجھنا ہے، رہا نماز کا فاسد ہونا تو وہ عمل کثیر سے ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی نے قرآن کے علاوہ کسی دوسری چیز کو لکھا ہوا دیکھا اور اس کو سمجھ بھی لیا مگر زبان سے تلفظ نہیں کیا۔ اس بارے میں بعض مشائخ کے قول کے مطابق امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک فاسد ہو جائے : مروی ہے (عنایہ کو) جیسے اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ فلاں کی کتاب نہیں پڑھوں گا پھر اس پر نظر ڈالی حتی کہ اس کو سمجھ بھی لیا مگر زبان سے تکلم نہیں کیا تو امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جمہور علماء کے نزدیک حانث نہیں ہوگا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک حانث ہو جائے گا۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زبان سے قرآت کا مقصد فہم اور مراد کا سمجھنا ہے پس سمجھنا قرآت کے مانند ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح قرآت اور تکلم سے حانث ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح فہم معانی سے بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآت زبان سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ قرآت کلام کے قبیل سے ہے اور کلام زبان سے ہوتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قرآت بھی زبان سے ہوتی ہے اور مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حالف نے زبان سے کچھ نہیں پڑھا بلکہ لکھا ہوا دیکھ کر صرف سمجھا ہے اس لئے وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا اور اگر مصلی ہے تو اس کی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں بالاجماع نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں صاحب بدایہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام محمد بھی عدم فساد نماز کے حکم میں ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں۔
And if he looks at a written text (other than Quran) and understands it, the correct view is that his prayer is not invalidated by consensus, contrary to the case where he swears not to read a book: for he breaks the oath by understanding according to Muhammad, because the purpose there is understanding. As for invalidation of prayer, it is by excessive action, and that is not present. Explanation: The issue is that the person looks at something written other than Quran and understands it but does not pronounce it verbally. According to a statement of some mashayikh, according to Abu Yusuf, the prayer is not invalidated, and according to Muhammad, it is invalidated. It is narrated (in `Inayah) that if someone swears not to read a book and then looks at it and understands it without speaking, then according to Abu Yusuf, according to the majority of scholars, he does not break the oath, and according to Muhammad, he does break it. Muhammad's proof: The purpose of reading from the tongue is understanding, so understanding is like recitation. Abu Yusuf's proof: Recitation is with the tongue, and he did not read with the tongue. The author of Al-Hidayah said that in this mentioned matter, by consensus, the prayer is not invalidated. According to the author of Al-Bidayal, in this matter, Imam Muhammad also agrees with Abu Yusuf on the non-invalidation of prayer.

Commentary
This lesson addresses the ruling when a person looks at a written text (other than the Quran) and understands it during prayer. The main ruling is that it does not invalidate the prayer by consensus because the necessary condition for invalidation—excessive action (kathir al-‘amal)—is absent. The passage contrasts this with an oath scenario, where understanding alone may constitute reading for the purpose of oath. It presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad initially held that understanding invalidates prayer, but the later relied-upon view is that it does not, aligning with Imam Abu Yusuf. The key principle is that prayer invalidation depends on physical excessive action, not mere understanding.

Key Terms
فہم (fahm): Understanding or comprehension of written text.
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive physical action that breaks the continuity of prayer.

Prayer is not invalidated by silent understanding of written text; invalidation requires excessive physical action (kathir al-‘amal).

Reading from the Mushaf in Prayer: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reading from the mushaf in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on reading from the mushaf during prayer and evaluate the practical difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Reading from a held Quran invalidates prayer; from a placed one, it does not.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about reading from the Quran (mushaf) during prayer. While the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considered it permissible if no excessive movement occurs, Abu Hanifa argued that holding and turning pages constitutes excessive action (amal kathir) or prompting (talaqqin), thus invalidating the prayer. Understanding this dispute refines your grasp of how actions inside prayer are evaluated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested act
The act is reading the Quran from a physical mushaf (book) while performing salah. The dispute concerns whether this act invalidates the prayer.
The act includes looking, holding (if applicable), and turning pages.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
State that Abu Hanifa holds the act invalidates prayer due to two proofs: (1) it is amal kathir (excessive action) when holding and turning, and (2) it is talaqqin (prompting/learning) which itself invalidates prayer. The Sahibayn hold it does not invalidate unless there is excessive movement; simple looking at a placed mushaf is fine.
Both proofs are based on qiyas (analogy).
3
Examine the proofs and their implications
Analyze each proof: For amal kathir, distinguish between holding/placing the mushaf. For talaqqin, note that prompting from a book is analogized to prompting from a person. Recognize that al-Sarakhsi preferred the talaqqin argument, making no distinction between placed and held mushaf.
The author of al-Hidayah noted that according to the first proof, placement matters; according to the second, it does not.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position is a compromise: if the mushaf is placed and the worshiper only looks, prayer is valid (Sahibayn's view); if the mushaf is held and pages turned, prayer is invalid (Abu Hanifa's view).
This is the practical outcome followed in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها
رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا کا آزاد کیا ہوا نام ذکوان نامی رمضان میں حضرت ام المؤمنین کی امامت کرتا اور وہ مصحف سے پڑھا کرتا تھا اور کہ ابن پڑھا تو امام ابو یوس اس لئے ہے کہ یہ صورت اہل کتاب کے طریقہ کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ اہل کتاب از کار وغیرہ حفظ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس طرح ہاتھ ہی ہونے کے حکم میں لیکر پڑھتے ہیں اور اہل کتاب کی مشابہت سے صحیح حدیث میں منع کیا گیا ہے پس جس صورت میں بغیر مشابہت کے شریعت پر عمل کر ہاتھی لیکن زبان سے نہیں ہو اس صورت میں اہل کتاب کے ساتھ تشابہ مکروہ ہوگا۔ مقصود فہم ہے یعنی امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن پاک اٹھائے رہنا اور اس میں نظر کرنا اور ورقوں کو پلٹن یہ مجموعہ عمل کثیر ہے اور عمل کثیر مفسدا خواہ زبان سے پر ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ صورت مفسد نماز ہوگی ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصحف سے پڑھنا اس سے سیکھ لینا ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی دوسر۔ لینا عمل خفیف ہے آدمی سے نماز میں سیکھتا گیا اور نماز میں کسی دوسرے سے تعلم اور تلقین کرنا مفسد نماز ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی نماز فاسد ہوگی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دوسری دلیل کی بناء پر کسی چیز پر رکھے ہوئے قرآن سے پڑھنے اور ہاتھوں میں اٹھائے ہوے سے پڑھنے میں کوئی فرجی وان مرت امر نہیں ہے کیونکہ تلقین دونوں صورتوں میں پایا گیا اور وہی باعث فساد ہے اور دلیل اول کی بناء پر دونوں میں فرق ہے کیونکہ اگر قرآن کسی 3 المار آثم لقو پر رکھا ہوا ہے اور مصلی اس سے دیکھ کر پڑھتا ہے تو اس میں عمل کثیر نہیں ہے اور اگر ہاتھوں میں لئے پڑھتا ہے تو یہ عمل کثیر ہے شمس 11 مر في موضع سرخسی نے دوسری دلیل کو اصح قرار دیا ہے۔
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. (Regarding the freed slave of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, named Zikwan who led the mother of the believers in Ramadan and used to read from the mushaf.) And he said: Ibn (?) read, so Imam Abu Yusuf (said) because this form resembles the way of the People of the Book, because the People of the Book, due to not memorizing, read by holding in the hand, and the correct hadith prohibits resemblance to the People of the Book. So in a form without resemblance, acting upon Sharia, but not with the tongue, in that case resemblance to the People of the Book is disliked. The goal is understanding, i.e., Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that holding the Quran, looking into it, and turning pages is a great action (amal kathir), and great action invalidates prayer even if without speech, so this form invalidates prayer. The second proof is that reading from the mushaf is learning from it, so it is like taking from another person (?) which is a light action, and a person learns in prayer, and learning and prompting from another in prayer invalidates prayer, so here also prayer becomes invalid. The author of Hidayah says that according to the second proof, there is no difference between reading from a placed Quran and holding it in the hands, because prompting is present in both and that is the cause of invalidation. But according to the first proof, there is a difference: if the Quran is placed and the worshiper looks and reads, there is no great action; if held in the hands, it is a great action. Al-Sarakhsi considered the second proof more correct.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding reading the Quran from a mushaf (mushaf) during prayer. The issue arises from the practice of a freed slave of Aisha who led her in Ramadan reading from the mushaf. Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad) initially viewed this as permissible, considering it similar to the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitab) who read from books, which is disliked but not invalidating. Abu Hanifa argues that holding the Quran, looking, and turning pages constitutes excessive action (amal kathir) that invalidates prayer. He also analogizes it to learning from another person, which involves talaqqin (prompting) and invalidates prayer. The author of al-Hidayah notes that according to the first proof, there is a difference between a placed Quran (no excessive action) and a held one (excessive action). Al-Sarakhsi preferred the second proof (talaqqin), treating both cases equally as invalidating. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that reading from the mushaf invalidates prayer if it involves excessive movement, but if the mushaf is placed and one simply looks without handling, it does not invalidate.

Key Terms
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive physical action that invalidates prayer according to Abu Hanifa.
تلقین (talaqqin): Prompting or learning from another, which invalidates prayer according to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, which scenario invalidates prayer?
A) A worshiper reads from a mushaf placed on a stand without touching it.
B) A worshiper holds a mushaf and turns pages while reading.
C) A worshiper recites from memory without any mushaf.
D) A worshiper listens to a Quran recitation from a non-participant.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, reading from a held mushaf with page turning invalidates prayer, but reading from a placed mushaf without excessive movement is valid.

Looking at Written Text in Prayer and Oaths: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on looking at a written text in prayer and its effect on oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for prayer and for oaths regarding looking at and understanding a written text, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the oath.

Core Idea
Understanding a non-Quranic text in prayer does not invalidate it; for oaths, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on whether mere understanding breaks an oath not to read.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses two distinct legal contexts: prayer and oaths. While there is consensus that mere understanding without utterance does not invalidate prayer, a dispute arises regarding oaths: does understanding constitute 'reading'? Imam Muhammad argues yes, because the purpose of reading is understanding; Imam Abu Yusuf insists reading is a verbal act. This lesson unpacks the rationale and the practical consequences of this legitimate intra-Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
The passage deals with two separate rulings: (1) looking at a written text during prayer and (2) the effect of understanding a text on an oath not to read that book. Note that the rulings differ.
Confusing these contexts is a common mistake.
2
Consensus on prayer
The text states that by consensus (ijma), prayer is not invalidated by looking at and understanding a non-Quranic text. The reason given is that invalidation requires excessive physical action (amal kathir), which is absent here.
Mere mental understanding is not considered amal kathir.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on oaths
For the oath not to read a book, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the oath is not broken by mere understanding without utterance. Imam Muhammad holds that understanding alone breaks the oath.
Both are valid positions within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the proofs (ta'lil)
Muhammad's proof: The purpose of reading is understanding (fahm), so understanding is like reading in fulfilling the oath. Abu Yusuf's proof: Reading (qira'ah) is a speech act by the tongue; since the person did not utter, he did not read.
The dispute is over the definition of 'reading' in the context of oaths.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In prayer, both agree on non-invalidation. In oaths, according to Muhammad, the oath is broken upon understanding; according to Abu Yusuf, it is not. The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view: the oath is not broken without actual recitation.
This affects fatwa in modern oath situations.

ولو نظر إلى مكتوب وفهمه فالصحيح انه لا تفسد صلاته بالاجماع بخلاف ما اذا حلف لا يقرأ كتاب فلا نماز کو قطع نہیں کرتا حيث يحنث بالفهم عند محمد لان المقصود هنالك الفهم اما فساد الصلاة فبالعمل الكثير ولم يوجد پڑتا ہے تو وہ چالیس ترجمہ اور اگر مصلی نے ( قرآن کے علاوہ ) کسی لکھی ہوئی چیز کی طرف دیکھا اور اس کو مجھ بھی لیا تو صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ بالا جماع اس کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اس کے برخلاف جب اس نے قسم کھائی کہ فلاں کی کتاب نہیں پڑھے گا تو امام محمد کے نزدیک فقط سمجھنے سے مانا تشریح مسئلہ ہوجائیگا کیونکہ یہاں مقصود سمجھتا ہے، رہا نماز کا فاسد ہونا تو وہ عمل کثیر سے ہوتا ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مصلی نے قرآن کے علاوہ کسی دوسری چیز کو لکھا ہوادیکھا اور اس کو سمجھ بھی لیا مگر زبان سے تلفظ نہیں کہ اصحاب فلو اہرا اس بارے میں بعض مشائخ کے قول کے مطابق امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک فاسد ہو جائے : مروی ہے ( عنایہ کو جیسے اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ فلاں کی کتاب نہیں پڑھوں گا پھر اس پر نظر ڈالی حتی کہ اس کو سمجھ بھی لیا مگر زبان سے تکم نہیں کیا تو امام ابو یسنا جمہور علماء کے کے نزدیک حانث نہیں ہوگا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک حانث ہو جائے گا امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زبان سے قرآت کا مقصد فہم اور مرا کا کم کردہ حدیث کا جوا ہے پس سمجھنا قرآت کے مانند ہو گیا یعنی جس طرح قرآت اور تکلم سے حانث ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح فہم معانی سے بھی حانث ہو جائے اس کا انکار فرمایا اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآت زبان سے ہوتی ہے کیونکہ قرآت کلام کے قبیل سے ہے اور کلام زبان سے ہوتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا والحمار والم قرات بھی زبان سے ہوتی ہے اور مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ حالف نے زبان سے کچھ نہیں پڑھا بلکہ لکھا ہوادیکھ کر صرف سمجھا ہے اس لئے وہ جان: علیہ وسلم یہ اے عروہ اہل عراق ہوگا اور اگر مصلی ہے تو اس کی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ حضرت عائشہ رضی ال صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں بالا جماع نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی ۔ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں صاحب بددیہ کے بیان کے مطابق امام محمدی عدم فساد نماز کے حکم میں ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں اب حاصل یہ ہوا کہ قرآن کے علاوہ لکھی ہوئی چیز کو دیکھ کر اگر مجھ لیا اور زبان ہی رات میں نماز پڑھے
And if he looks at a written thing and understands it, the correct view is that his prayer is not invalidated by consensus, unlike the case where he swears not to read a book – then he does not break the prayer (?) but he breaks the oath by understanding according to Muhammad, because the objective there is understanding. As for invalidation of prayer, it is by excessive action, which is not found. Translation: And if the worshiper looked at something written (other than the Quran) and understood it, the correct statement is that by consensus his prayer is not invalidated, contrary to when he swore not to read a certain book – then according to Imam Muhammad, merely understanding makes him break the oath, because the objective there is understanding. As for invalidation of prayer, that occurs by excessive action, and it is not found. Explanation: The worshiper looked at something written other than the Quran and understood it, but did not utter it. According to some mashayikh, according to Imam Abu Yusuf, prayer is not invalidated; according to Imam Muhammad, it is invalidated. It is narrated (in Inayah) like if someone swore not to read a certain book, then looked at it until he understood it but did not utter it, then according to Abu Yusuf and the majority of scholars, he does not break the oath; according to Muhammad, he does break it. Muhammad's proof: The purpose of reading is understanding, so understanding is like reading. Abu Yusuf's proof: Reading is by the tongue, as it is from speech, and speech is by the tongue. So since he did not read with the tongue, he does not break the oath. And if the worshiper, then his prayer is not invalidated. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, said... The author of Hidayah said that in the mentioned issue, by consensus, prayer is not invalidated. And according to the statement of the author of Bada'i', Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Yusuf on non-invalidation of prayer. So the result: if one looks at a written thing other than Quran and understands it, and prays with the tongue (?).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage deals with two related issues: (1) Looking at a written text (other than the Quran) and understanding it during prayer, and (2) the effect of such understanding on an oath not to read that book. For prayer, the correct view (sahih) is that it does not invalidate prayer by consensus (ijma). This is because the invalidation of prayer requires excessive action (amal kathir), which is absent here; mere understanding is a subtle mental act, not physical action. For the oath (yamin), there is a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Muhammad argues that the purpose of reading is understanding (fahm), so if one understands the written material, it is as if he read it, thus breaking the oath. Abu Yusuf counters that reading is specifically with the tongue (qira'ah is from speech), and since he only looked and understood without uttering, he did not read, so the oath is not broken. The author of al-Hidayah affirms that for prayer, all agree it is not invalidated. The practical difference: In prayer, both views (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) now agree it does not invalidate, but for oaths, Muhammad's view would make one break the oath by understanding alone, while Abu Yusuf requires actual recitation.

Key Terms
فہم (fahm): Understanding the meaning of what is read or looked at, without verbal utterance.
عمل کثیر (amal kathir): Excessive physical action that invalidates prayer.
حنث (hanath): Breaking an oath, incurring kaffarah (expiation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because no excessive action (amal kathir) occurs
C) Because it is a form of dhikr
D) Because the text is not Quran

Key Takeaway
Understanding a non-Quranic text in prayer does not invalidate it; for oaths, Abu Yusuf requires verbal reading while Muhammad considers understanding sufficient, with the mufta bihi being Abu Yusuf.

Salah — Prayer

Passing of Woman, Donkey, Dog in Front of a Praying Person
Hanafi view that women, donkeys, and dogs do not invalidate prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the passing of a woman, donkey, or dog in front of a praying person, and evaluate the opposing proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Passing creatures do not invalidate prayer in the Hanafi school — the proof is the Prophet's practice and Aisha's testimony.

This lesson examines a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: does the passing of a woman, donkey, or dog in front of a praying person invalidate the prayer? The Hanafi school holds it does not, while others (including the Hanbali school and some early authorities) consider it invalidating. We will trace the proofs from hadith and the Hanafi response, and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi ruling is that passing does not invalidate prayer, but the passer is sinful under specific conditions (place of prostration, no barrier, limb alignment).
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, supported by the hadith 'nothing passing cuts the prayer.'
2
Identify the opposing proof
The opposing school cites the hadith: 'A woman, a dog, and a donkey cut the prayer.' This is attributed to the Sahibayn and Imam Ahmad.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Aisha's hadith directly refutes that interpretation. She relates that the Prophet prayed while she lay in front of him, showing that a woman's presence does not invalidate.
The Hanafi response reconciles the two hadith by interpreting 'qat'' as sin for the passer, not invalidation.
4
Determine the practical difference
According to Hanafi, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated; according to opposing view, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کا نمازی کے سامنے سے گذرنا مفسد صلوٰۃ نہیں
مرت امرأة بين يدى المصلى لم يقطع الصلاة لقوله عليه السلام لا يقطع الصلاة مرور شيء الا ان مار آثم لقوله عليه السلام لو علم المار بين يدى المصلى ماذا عليه من الوزر لوقف أربعين وإنما يأثم اذا برفی موضع سجوده على ما قيل ولا يكون بينهما حائل ويحاذى اعضاء المار اعضائه لو كان يصلى على الدكان
رجمہ اور اگر مصلی کے سامنے سے کوئی عورت گذری تو ( یہ گذرنا ) نماز قطع نہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ کسی چیز کا گذرنا واقع نہیں کرتا لیکن گذرنے والا گنہگار ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اگر مصلی کے سامنے سے گذرنے والا جانتا کہ اس پر کیا گناہ ے تو وہ چالیس تک کھڑا رہتا۔ اور گنہگار جب ہی ہوگا جب کہ مصلی کی جائے سجود میں گذرے اس بنا پر کہ کہا گیا اور دونوں کے یہاں کوئی چیز حائل نہ ہو اور گذرنے والے کے اعضاء مصلی کے اعضاء کے مقابل ہو جائیں اگر وہ چبوترے پر نماز پڑھتا ہو ۔ مسئلہ مصلی کے سامنے سے عورت کا گذرنا نماز کو فاسد نہیں کرتا عورت خواہ خائضہ ہو یا غیر حائقہ اسی طرح گدھے اور کتے کا کرنا بھی مفصد نماز نہیں ہے اصحاب خواہر کہتے ہیں کہ ان تینوں کا گذر نا مفسد نماز ہے۔ امام احمد بن حنبل کی مشہور روایت یہی ہے۔ تاب خواہر کی دلیل حضور کا قول تقطع المرأة الصلوة و الكلب والحمار ہے۔ یہ حدیث ابوذر رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ سے ا ہے عنایہ کنایہ یعنی عورت کتا اور گدھا قاطع نماز ہے۔ اور علماء کے دلائل سے پہلے فاضل علامہ جلال الدین بن شمس الدین الخوارزمی صاحب کفایہ کی زبان میں اصحاب خواہر کی پیش حدیث کا جواب ملا حظہ فرمائیے ۔ فاضل موصوف فرماتے ہیں کہ جس وقت حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا کو یہ حدیث پہنچی تو آپ نے کار فرمایا اور حضرت عروہ کو مخاطب کر کے فرمایا عروہ ماذا يقول اهل العراق قال يقولون يقطع الصلوة مرور المرأة الحمار والكلب فقالت يا اهل العراق والشقاق النفاق قرنتمونا بالكلاب والحمر كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلى بالليل وانا معترضة بين يديه اعتراض الجنازة فاذاسجد حبست رجلي و اذا قام مددتها بعين ان و دوال عراق کیا کہتے ہیں حضرت عروہ نے فرمایا کہ اہل عراق کہتے ہیں کہ عورت، گدھے اور کتے کا گذرنا نماز کو قطع کرتا ہے پس ضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا نے فرمایا کہ اے اہل عراق والشفاق و انفاق تم نے ہم عورتوں کو کتوں اور گدھوں کے ساتھ ملاد یا رسول اللہ ات میں نماز پڑھتے تھے اور میں آپ کے سامنے لیٹی رہتی جیسے جنازہ رکھا جاتا ہے جب آپ سجدہ کرتے تو میں اپنے پاؤں صبیح
A woman's passing in front of the praying person does not invalidate prayer. A woman passed in front of the worshiper – it did not cut the prayer because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Nothing passing cuts the prayer.' But the passer is sinful because of his statement: 'If the one passing in front of the worshiper knew what sin is upon him, he would stand for forty.' And he is only sinful when he passes in the place of prostration, as it is said, and there is no barrier between them, and the limbs of the passer align with the limbs of the worshiper, if he is praying on a raised platform. Issue: A woman passing in front of the worshiper does not invalidate prayer, whether she is menstruating or not. Similarly, the passing of a donkey and a dog does not invalidate prayer. The Sahibayn say that the passing of these three invalidates prayer. Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal's famous narration is this. The Sahibayn's proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'A woman, a dog, and a donkey cut the prayer.' This hadith is from Abu Dharr. The author of Kifayah, Jalal al-Din al-Khwarizmi, gives the answer to the Sahibayn's hadith: When Aisha heard this hadith, she said: 'O Urwa, what do the people of Iraq say?' He said: 'They say that the passing of a woman, a donkey, and a dog cuts the prayer.' She said: 'O people of Iraq, you have compared us to dogs and donkeys! The Messenger of Allah prayed at night while I lay in front of him like a bier. When he prostrated, I would draw my feet. When he stood, I would stretch them.'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage discusses the inter-madhhab dispute on whether the passing of a woman, donkey, or dog in front of a person praying invalidates the prayer. The Hanafi position is that it does not invalidate (la yaqta' al-salah). The proof is the hadith that nothing passing cuts the prayer, though the passer is sinful if he passes directly in the place of prostration without a barrier and their limbs align. The opposing view, attributed to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually the text says 'اصحاب خواہر' which may mean the three imams? But then it mentions Imam Ahmad, so likely it is the Hanbali position) and Imam Ahmad, states that these three do invalidate prayer, based on the hadith: 'A woman, a dog, and a donkey cut the prayer.' The Hanafi response is given through the hadith of Aisha, who refuted this interpretation. Aisha relates that the Prophet prayed at night while she lay in front of him, demonstrating that a woman's presence does not invalidate prayer. The Hanafis explain that the hadith about cutting refers to specific conditions (like a woman who is not mahram, etc.) or is abrogated. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that these do not invalidate, but it is disliked (makruh) to pass in front of a praying person.

Key Terms
قطع الصلاة (qat' al-salah): To invalidate or break the prayer; here it means to render the prayer null and void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She denied it and gave evidence from the Prophet's practice
C) She said it applies only to dogs
D) She said it applies only to menstruating women

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the passing of a woman, donkey, or dog in front of a praying person does not invalidate the prayer, though the passer is sinful under specific conditions.

Definition of the Prohibited Area and Ruling on Sutrah
Defines the area and conditions for sinful passing and the sutrah recommendation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the prohibited area in front of a worshipper and identify the conditions that make passing sinful, and explain the recommendation and conditions of sutrah.

Core Idea
Passing in front of a worshipper is sinful only within the area from his feet to his prostration spot and without a barrier.

In this lesson, we examine the precise area in front of a worshipper that, if crossed, makes the passer sinful. The Hanafi school has a clear relied-upon opinion: from the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration. But conditions apply, such as the absence of any barrier. We also cover the recommended practice of taking a sutrah when praying in open spaces, supported by Prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited area
Note that the relied-upon (asahh) opinion defines the prohibited area as from the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration. Some scholars extend it to the range of vision, but the strongest opinion is the first.
This is the opinion chosen by al-Sarakhsi, al-Islam, and Qadi Khan.
2
Recognize the condition of no barrier
The ruling applies only when there is no barrier (ha'il) such as a wall, pillar, sutrah, or even a person's back between the worshipper and the passer. If any barrier exists, the passer is not sinful.
The presence of a barrier completely removes the sin.
3
Note special cases (platform and height)
If the worshipper is on a platform, the passer is sinful only when his limbs are directly opposite the worshipper's limbs. If the worshipper is elevated to the height of a man, passing in front is not sinful at all.
These exceptions are derived from the same principle: the prohibited area is relative to the worshipper's position.
4
Understand the sutrah recommendation
For desert prayer, it is mustahabb to place a sutrah in front, at least a cubit high and the thickness of a finger, based on the Prophet's command which is understood as recommendation (nadb) in the Hanafi school.
The sutrah serves as a visible barrier that helps the worshipper focus and avoids sin for passers.

ثم اذامر الخ سے اس مقام کا بیان ہے جس کے اندر سے گذرنا حرام ہے یعنی وہ مقام جس کے اندر گذرنا حرام جہاز کے برابر ہونا چاہیے حد یہ بیان کی گئی کہ مصلی کے قدم سے لے کر مقام سجدہ تک ہے یہی اصح ہے۔ اور اسی کو شمس الائمہ السرخی شیخ الاسلام اور قاضی خان اختیار کیا ہے۔ بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ حد یہ ہے کہ جب مصلی اپنی نظر اپنے سجدہ کی جگہ ڈال کر پڑھتا ہو تو گنہگار والے پر اس کی نگاہ نہ پڑے یعنی حد موضع سجود سے بھی آگے وہاں تک ہے کہ موضع سجود پر نظر رکھنے کی حالت میں جہاں تک نظر پڑتی ہے پھر جہاں نظر نہ پڑے وہاں سے گذرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ بعض نے دو صف یا تین صف کی مقدار کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اور بعض نے ذراع کے ساتھ اور بعض نے پانچ ذراع کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اور بعض نے چالیس ذراع کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے۔ یہ حکم اسی وقت ہے جب کہ وہ صحراء یا میدان میں نماز پڑھتا ہو اور اگر مسجد میں پڑھتا ہے تو بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ پچاس ذراع چھوڑ کر گذر سکتا ہے اور دائیں یا بائیں قول یہ ہے کہ مصلی اور قبلہ کی دیوار کے درمیان سے گذرنا مناسب نہیں ہے بلکہ دیوار کی اس طرف سے ہو کر گذرے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ مرور بین المصلی کی کراہت اس وقت ہے جبکہ مصلی اور گزرنے والے کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل نہ ہو۔ اگر کوئی چیز حائل ہو مثلاً ستون دیوار سترہ یا آدمی کی پیٹھ تو گذرنے والا گنہگار نہ ہوگا۔ اس کے بعد فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص چبوترے پر نماز پڑھتا ہو تو اس کے سامنے سے گذرنے والا اس وقت گنہگار ہوگا جبکہ گذرنے والے کے اعضاء مصلی کے اعضاء کے محاذی ہو جائیں۔ اور اگر آدمی کے قد کے برابر اونچی جگہ پر نماز پڑھتا ہو تو اس کے آگے سے گذرنے والا گنہگار نہ ہوگا۔ وينبغي لمن يصلى في الصحراء أن يتخذ أمامه سترة لقوله عليه السلام اذا صلى احدكم فليجعل بين يديه سترة ومقدارها ذراع فصاعدا لقوله عليه السلام أيعجز أحدكم إذا صلى في الصحرا إلا يجعل أمامه مثل مؤخرة الرحل وقيل ينبغي أن يكون في غلظ الاصبع لأن ما دونه لا يبدو للناظرين من من
Then from 'thumma idha marra' etc., the description of the place within which passing is prohibited. That is, the place within which passing is prohibited should be equal to the size of a funeral bier? The limit is stated: from the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration. This is the most correct. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, Shaykh al-Islam, and Qadi Khan have chosen this. Some mashayikh said that the limit is that when the worshipper prays with his gaze fixed on his place of prostration, the passer should not be within his vision. So the limit extends beyond the place of prostration to the point where his gaze reaches when looking at the place of prostration; then where his gaze does not reach, passing is not disliked. Some have estimated it as two or three rows, some as a cubit, some as five cubits, some as forty cubits. This ruling applies when he prays in the desert or plain. If he prays in a mosque, some are of the opinion that one can pass fifty cubits away, and to the right or left. The preferred saying is that passing between the worshipper and the qibla wall is not appropriate; rather, one should pass on the other side of the wall. The author of al-Hidayah said that the dislike (karahah) of passing in front of the worshipper occurs when there is no barrier between them. If there is a barrier, such as a pillar, wall, sutrah, or a person's back, then the passer is not sinful. He further said: If a person prays on a platform, the passer is sinful only when his limbs are directly opposite the worshipper's limbs. And if he prays on an elevated place as high as a man's height, then the passer in front of him is not sinful. It is recommended for one who prays in the desert to take a sutrah in front of him because of his (ﷺ) saying: 'When one of you prays, let him place a sutrah in front of him.' And its measure is a cubit or more, because of his (ﷺ) saying: 'Is any one of you unable, when he prays in the desert, to place in front of him something like the saddle of a mount?' And it is said that it should be the thickness of a finger, because what is less than that is not visible to onlookers.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that defines the specific area in front of a worshipper that triggers sin for a passer, and then discusses the sunnah of sutrah. The author begins by explaining that the prohibited area is from the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration — this is the relied-upon (asahh) opinion, endorsed by major Hanafi scholars like al-Sarakhsi and Qadi Khan. Some scholars extend it to the range of the worshipper's vision when looking at the prostration spot. Various estimates (two rows, three rows, cubits, etc.) are mentioned but the strongest is the first. The prohibition applies when there is no barrier (sutrah, pillar, wall, or even a person's back). If a barrier exists, the passer is not sinful. Special cases: if the worshipper is on a platform, sin requires that the passer's limbs align directly; if on a high place (like a man's height), passing in front is not sinful. The passage then shifts to the recommendation of sutrah for desert prayer: the Prophet (ﷺ) instructed to take a sutrah such as a stick or the saddle of a mount, with a minimum thickness of a finger. The sutrah should be at least a cubit high.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of a worshipper to create a barrier that prevents sin for passers and defines the prohibited area.
حائل (ḥāʾil): A barrier such as a wall, pillar, sutrah, or a person's back that removes the sin from passing.
مقام سجدہ (maqām al-sujūd): The place where the worshipper's forehead rests in prostration; from the feet to this point is the prohibited area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi opinion, what is the defined limit of the prohibited area for passing in front of a worshipper?
A) From the worshipper's head to the qibla wall
B) From the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration
C) Fifty cubits in all directions
D) Only the exact spot where the worshipper is prostrating

Key Takeaway
The prohibited area for passing is specifically from the worshipper's feet to the place of prostration, and any barrier removes the sin.

The Ruling on Passing in Front of a Praying Person
Explaining the ruling on passing before a praying person with evidence and details on prohibited area.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on passing in front of a praying person, identify the prohibited area, and apply the conditions that remove sin.

Core Idea
Passing in front of a praying person is sinful but does not invalidate the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the classical Hanafi position on a common scenario: someone walking directly in front of a worshipper in prayer. The passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that while such action does not break the prayer, it carries a severe sin. We will explore the evidence, the precise area of prohibition, and the factors that may exempt the passer from sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (passing in front of the praying person) and what ruling the Hanafi school assigns: it is makruh tahrimi, not mufsid.
2
Examine the Primary Dalil
Examine the hadith cited: 'لا يقطع الصلوة مرور شيء' (Passing does not cut the prayer). Understand how this proves non-invalidation, and the hadith of the passer's sin shows it is sinful.
3
Define the Prohibited Area
The passage gives various opinions on the exact area from the praying person's feet to the place of prostration. Note the preferred view of al-Sarakhsi and others.
4
Apply Conditions for Sin
Consider the exceptions: if there is a barrier (sutrah, pillar, wall) or if the praying person is elevated above the passer, the sin is removed.
5
Distinguish from Invalidation
Contrast with acts that actually invalidate prayer. Understand why passing is at most a sin, not an invalidator, based on the evidence.

باب ما یفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها ۱۴۸ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ سمجد اشرف البدائية فلا يحصل لیتی ۔ اور جب آپ کھڑے ہوتے تو پاؤں پھیلا دیتی تھی۔ اس واقعہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت ام المؤمنین عائشہ رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہا نے حدیث ابوذر کا بڑی سختی سے انکار کیا اور مصلی کے ترجمہ ) سے عورت کے گذرنے سے نماز فاسد ہنوے کی سخت لب ولہجہ میں تردید فرمائی۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے کہ کلام مصلی جب کوئی تم میں سامنے سے گذرنے میں ہے نہ کہ پاؤں پھیلا کر لیٹنے میں۔ اور حضرت عائشہ کے بیان سے پاؤں پھیلا کر لیٹنا تو ثابت ہوتا ہے کیا عاجز ہوتا بین المصلی ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب جب پاؤں پھیلا کر لیٹے رہنا مفسد نماز نہیں تو مرور بدرجہ اولی مفسد نہیں ہوگا۔ جمہور علماء کی دلیل رسول اللہ کا قول لا يقطع الصلوة مرورشئ فادرؤ اما استطعتم فانه الشيطان ہے یعنی کر گزرنا نماز کو قطع نہیں کرتا جس قدر ممکن ہو دفع کرو کیونکہ وہ شیطان ہے لیکن اتنی بات ضرور ہے کہ مصلی کے سامنے سے گذرنے والا ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لو علم المار بين يدى المصلى ماذا عليه من الوزر لوقف اربعین یعنی اگر مصلی کے سامنے گذر نے والا جانتا کہ اس پر کس قدر گناہ پڑتا ہے تو وہ چالیس تک کھڑا رہتا۔ راوی کہتا ہے کہ مجھے معلوم نہیں کہ چالیس سال ہیں یا پان ماہ ہیں یا چالیس یوم ہیں۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ حضرت ابو ہریرہ رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ کی حدیث سے بطریق صحت ثابت ہے کہ یہ فی الصح سال مراد ہیں۔
میں انگلی کی مقہ تشریح تشریح. قول اذاصلی سترہ لمبائی میں بیٹھنے والے کے و انماياً ثم اذامر الخ سے اس مقام کا بیان ہے جس کے اندر سے گذرنا حرام ہے یعنی وہ مقام جس کے اندر گذر نا حرام جہاز کے برابر ہونی حد یہ بیان کی گئی کہ مصلی کے قدم سے لے کر مقام سجدہ تک ہے یہی اصح ہے۔ اور اسی کو شمس الائمہ السرخی شیخ الاسلام اور قاضی خان حاصل نہ ہو گا اختیار کیا ہے۔
على الايسر بعض مشائخ کی رائے : بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ حد یہ ہے کہ جب مصلی اپنی نظر اپنے سجدہ کی جگہ ڈال کر پڑھتا ہوتو گنا والے پر اس کی نگاہ نہ پڑے یعنی حد موضع سجود سے بھی آگے وہاں تک ہے کہ موضع سجود پر نظر رکھنے کی حالت میں جہاں تک آگے بم ويقرب من پڑتی ہے پھر جہاں نہ پڑے وہاں سے گذرنا مکروہ نہیں ہے بعض نے دو صف یا تین صف کی مقدار کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اور بعض نے ذراع کے ساتھ اور بعض نے پانچ وزاع کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے اور بعض نے چالیس ذراع کے ساتھ مقدر کیا ہے یہ حکم اسی وقت ہے ترجمہ اور کہ وہ صحراء یا میدان میں نماز پڑھتا ہو اور اگر مسجد میں پڑھتا ہے تو بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ پچاس ذراع چھوڑ کر گذر سکتا ہے اور وائیں یا بائیں قول یہ ہے کہ مصلی اور قبلہ کی دیوار کے درمیان سے گذرنا مناسب نہیں ہے بلکہ دیوار کی اس طرف سے ہو کر گذرے۔ کوترک کرنے صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ مرور بین المصلی کی کراہت اس وقت ہے جبکہ مصلی اور گزرنے والے کے درمیان کوئی چیز حائل : تشریح 1 ستون دیوار سترہ یا آدمی کی پیٹھ وغیرہ اگر کوئی چیز حائل ہو تو گذرنے والا گنہ گار نہ ہوگا۔ اس کے بعد فر مایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص چبوترے رکھے کیونکہ اسی پڑھتا ہو تو اس کے سامنے سے گذرنے والا اس وقت گنہگار ہوگا۔ جبکہ گذرنے والے کے اعضاء مصلی کے اعضاء کے محاذ کی اور قال الاسود سے روایے جائیں اور اگر آدمی کے قد کے برابر اونچی جگہ پر نماز پڑھتا ہوتو اس کے آگے سے گذرنے والا گنہگار نہ ہوگا۔
Chapter: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. 148 Ashraf al-Bidayah sharh Urdu Hidayah... And when he stood, she would spread her feet. From this incident it is known that Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, strongly rejected the hadith of Abu Dharr and firmly denied that passing of a woman in front of the praying person invalidates prayer. The utmost objection can be that the speech of the praying person is about passing in front, not about lying with spread feet. And from Aisha's statement, lying with spread feet is proven, but passing in front is not proven. Answer: When lying with spread feet does not invalidate prayer, then passing in front is even less likely to invalidate. The proof of the majority of scholars is the saying of the Messenger of Allah: 'Passing does not cut the prayer, so repel as much as you can, for it is the devil.' That is, passing does not break the prayer, repel it as much as possible because it is the devil. But it is necessary that the passer is in front of the praying person. Because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'If the passer in front of the prayer knew what sin is upon him, he would stand for forty.' The narrator says: I do not know if it is forty years, or forty months, or forty days. Some scholars said that it is authentically proven from the hadith of Abu Hurairah that it means forty years. ... Then the explanation of the place through which passing is forbidden: it is the place where passing is forbidden from the feet of the praying person to the place of prostration. This is the correct view, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, Shaykh al-Islam, and Qadi Khan chose it. Some scholars said: the limit is that when the praying person is praying while fixing his gaze on his prostration place, the passer's gaze should not fall on him. That is, beyond the place of prostration to where his gaze reaches when looking at the place of prostration. Then where it does not reach, passing is not disliked. Some estimated it as the amount of two or three rows, some with a cubit, some with five cubits, and some with forty cubits. This ruling is only when he prays in an open space or field. And if he prays in a mosque, some are of the opinion that he may pass leaving fifty cubits. And the correct saying is that passing between the praying person and the qibla wall is not appropriate, rather he should pass from the side of the wall. The author of Hidayah said: The dislike of passing in front of the praying person is when there is no barrier between the praying person and the passer. Explanation: If there is a barrier such as a pillar, wall, sutrah, or a person's back, etc., then the passer is not sinful. Then he said: If a person prays on a platform, then the passer in front of him is sinful only when the passer's body is level with the praying person's body. And according to the narration of al-Aswad: if a person prays at a height equal to the stature of a person, then the passer in front of him is not sinful.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on passing in front of a praying person. The author begins by recounting an incident involving Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who strongly rejected the hadith of Abu Dharr that claimed passing invalidates prayer. She argued that the matter is about passing, not lying down. The author then presents the Hanafi position: passing does not invalidate prayer. This is supported by the hadith 'Passing does not cut the prayer' and the understanding that even lying with spread feet (which is more obstructive) does not invalidate, so passing is even less likely to do so. However, it is sinful, as shown by the hadith 'If the passer knew the sin...' The passage then discusses the specific area in front of the praying person where passing is prohibited. The preferred view (as held by al-Sarakhsi, Shaykh al-Islam, and Qadi Khan) is that the prohibited area is from the feet to the place of prostration. Various opinions on the exact distance are mentioned, but the core ruling remains: passing is disliked and sinful but does not invalidate the prayer. The passage concludes with conditions: if there is a barrier (like a sutrah or wall), the passer is not sinful; if the praying person is on a high platform, the passer is only sinful when at the same level.

Key Terms
مرور (murur): Passing in front of a praying person
مفسد (mufsid): Something that invalidates the prayer
کراہت (karahah): Dislike, reproach; here makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of the praying person to serve as a barrier, preventing people from passing directly in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the correct area in front of the praying person where passing is prohibited?
A) From the forehead to the toes.
B) From the feet to the place of prostration.
C) One arm's length in all directions.
D) Up to 50 cubits.

Key Takeaway
Passing in front of a praying person is a sin but does not invalidate the prayer; a barrier or elevation removes the sin.

Sutrah for Desert Prayer: Recommendation and Dimensions
Defining the recommended screen (sutrah) for desert prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutrah for desert prayer, list its minimum dimensions (length and thickness), and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The sutrah for desert prayer is mustahabb (recommended), with a minimum length of one cubit and thickness of a finger.

This lesson examines the ruling of the sutrah, or screen, for one praying in an open area. The Hanafi school, based on Prophetic hadith, holds that setting up a sutrah is a strongly recommended sunnah, not an obligation. Additionally, we will explore the prescribed dimensions and proper placement that allow the sutrah to serve its purpose of discouraging passersby.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is placing a sutrah when praying in the desert. According to Hanafis, it is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites two hadiths: the command 'falyaj'al bayna yadayhi sutrah' and the question about having something like the back of a saddle.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form indicates recommendation because other evidence shows prayer without sutrah is valid. The simile to a saddle's back indicates the small size.
The imperative alone does not prove obligation in Hanafi usul when there is counter-evidence.
4
Determine the minimum dimensions
Length: one cubit (approx. 46 cm). Thickness: the size of a finger. This is based on Al-Quduri's opinion that a smaller barrier is not visible from a distance, thus failing its purpose.
There is no maximum; more is permissible.
5
Note the placement and conditions
The sutrah should be placed close to the praying person, opposite either the right or left eyebrow (not directly in front). It may be omitted if one is safe from passersby or does not face the road.
The placement is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

على حاجبه صحرا ( میدان میں نماز پڑھنے والے کے لئے سترہ قائم کرنا مستحب ہے درخت کی طرفہ وينبغي لمن يصلى في الصحراء أن يتخذ أمامه سترة لقوله عليه السلام اذا صلى احدكم فى الشد القدير ( صاحب فليجعل بين يديه سترة ومقدارها ذراع فصاعدا لقوله عليه السلام أيعجز أحدكم إذا صلى في الصحرا الا عمودا الاء يكون أمامه مثل مؤخرة الرحل وقيل ينبة أن يكون فى غلظ الاصبع لأن ما دونه لا يبدو للناظرين من من

ارنی الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم للا يحصل المقصود
۱۴۹
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها
رجمہ اور جوشخص میدان میں نماز پڑھتا ہے اس کے لئے مناسب یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے آگے سترہ بنائے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جب کوئی تم میں سے میدان میں نماز پڑھے تو اپنے سامنے سترہ کر لے۔ اور سترہ کی مقدار ایک ذراع یا زیادہ کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ کہنا یہ ہوتا ہے تم میں کوئی جب میدان میں نماز پڑھے یہ کہ اس کے سامنے مثل مؤخرہ کجاوہ کے ہو۔ اور کہا گیا کہ مناسب ہے کہ موٹائی میں انگل کی مقدار ہو۔ کیونکہ اس سے کم موٹائی تو دور سے دیکھنے والوں کو ظاہر نہ ہوگی پس مقصد حاصل نہ ہوگا۔
شریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص میدان میں نماز پڑھتا ہو تو وہ اپنے آگے سترہ قائم کر لے اور یہ امر مستحب ہے۔ دلیل حضور کا ال فاصلي احدكم في الصحراء فليجعل بين يديه سترہ ہے رہی یہ بات کہ سترہ کی مقدار کیا ہوگی تو اس بارے میں فرمایا کہ لمبائی میں کم از کم ایک ذراع ہونا چاہئے ۔ اور زیادہ جس قدر ہو کوئی حرج نہیں۔ دلیل حضور کا قول ایـعـجـزا حدكم اذاصلی لى الصحراء ان يكون امامه مثل موخرة الرحل، موخرۃ میم کا ضمہ اور خاء کا کسرہ اس لکڑی کو کہتے ہیں جو کجاوے کے پیچھے بہنے والے کے سر کے برابر ہوتی ہے۔ خاء کو مشدد پڑھنا غلط ہے رحل کجاوہ کے معنی میں ہے۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ موٹائی ایک انکلی کے برابر ہونی چاہئے ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس سے کم موٹائی دور سے دیکھنے والوں کو ظاہر نہ ہوگی پس اس سے کم موٹائی والے سترہ سے مقصود امل نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہا گیا کہ کم از کم ایک انگلی کی مقدار موٹائی ہونی چاہئے۔
نمازی سترہ اپنے قریب گاڑھے سترہ لگانے کا طریقہ
ويقرب من الستره لقوله عليه السلام من صلى الى سترة فليدن منها ويجعل السترة على حاجبه الايمن او على الايسر به ورد الاثر ولا بأس بترك السترة اذا امن المرور ولم يواجه الطريق
رجمہ اور سترہ سے قریب رہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص سترہ کی طرف نماز پڑھے تو اس سے نزدیک رہے اور سترہ کو اپنے ابی بابا میں ھوں کے مقابل رکھے اس کے ساتھ اثر وارد ہوا ہے۔ اور جب کسی کے گذرنے سے امن ہو اور راستہ کا مواجہہ نہ ہو تو سترہ ارک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
فریا۔ اس عبارت میں بیان کیا گیا کہ سترہ مصلی اپنے دائیں یا بائیں بھوؤں کے بالمقابل رکھے یعنی دونوں آنکھوں کے بیچ نہ ئے کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ اثر وارد ہوا ہے چنانچہ امام ابو داؤد نے ضباعہ بنت المقدار دین الاسود سے اور انہوں نے اپنے والد مقداد بن سے روایت کیا ہے قال ما رأیت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الى عود ولا عمود ولا شجرة الاجعله على حاجبه الايمن او الايسر ولا يصمد له صمد مقداد نے فرمایا کہ نہیں دیکھا میں نے اللہ کے برحق نبی کو کسی لکڑی یا ستون یا ورفت کی طرف نماز پڑھتے ہوئے مگر یہ کہ اس کو اپنے دائیں یا بائیں بھوؤں کے مقابل کر دیا اور اس کا ارادہ نہیں فرماتے تھے۔ (فتح القدیر) صاحب عنایہ نے اس اثر کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے انه صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ما صلى الى شجرة ولا الى عودو لا عمودا الاجعله على حاجبه الايمن وله يصمد صمدا، اى لم يقصده قصدا الى المواجهة
On his eyebrow... In the desert, for the one praying in the field, it is recommended to set up a sutrah, towards a tree... And it is befitting for whoever prays in the desert to take a sutrah in front of him, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'When one of you prays in the desert, then let him place a sutrah in front of him.' And its measure is one cubit or more, due to his saying: 'Is one of you unable, when he prays in the desert, to have in front of him something like the back part of a saddle?' And it was said: it is recommended that its thickness be the size of a finger, because less than that would not be apparent to onlookers, so the purpose would not be achieved. ... Explanation: The issue is that if a person prays in the desert, he should set up a sutrah in front of him, and this is recommended. The proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Let him place a sutrah between his hands.' As for the measure, it was said that the minimum length is one cubit. And there is no harm in more. The proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Is one of you unable... to have in front of him something like the back part of a saddle (mu'akhkhirat al-rahil)?' Mu'akhkhirat: with dammah on mim and kasrah on kha, it is the piece of wood that is behind the saddle at the level of the rider's head. Pronouncing kha with tashdid is wrong. Rahl means saddle. Al-Quduri said: thickness should be equal to a finger. The proof is that less than that would not be apparent to onlookers, so the purpose would not be achieved. Therefore, it was said that the minimum thickness should be the size of a finger. The method of placing the sutrah: He should be close to the sutrah, due to his saying: 'Whoever prays towards a sutrah, let him come close to it.' And he should place the sutrah opposite his right or left eyebrow, as the athar has been reported. And there is no harm in leaving the sutrah when one is safe from passersby and does not face the road. ... This expression explains that the praying person should place the sutrah opposite his right or left eyebrow, i.e., not between the two eyes, because an athar has been reported regarding that. Thus, Imam Abu Dawud narrated from Dhaba'ah bint al-Miqdad… who said: I did not see the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, praying towards a stick, a pillar, or a tree except that he placed it opposite his right or left eyebrow, and he did not face it directly (i.e., he did not intend to face it directly).
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage focuses on the sutrah (screen or barrier) that a person praying in an open area is recommended to place in front of him. The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The proofs are two hadiths: the Prophet commanded to set up a sutrah, and the hadith about the back part of a saddle. The minimum length is one cubit (about 46 cm), and the minimum thickness is that of a finger, as a thinner barrier would not be visible from a distance and thus fail to serve its purpose of preventing people from passing. The sutrah should be placed close to the praying person, and it is recommended to position it opposite either the right or left eyebrow, not directly in front of the face. This is based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Dhaba'ah. However, if there is no fear of someone passing (e.g., in a safe area away from the path), leaving the sutrah is not objectionable.

Key Terms
سترہ (sutrah): A screen or barrier placed in front of a praying person to prevent passersby.
مؤخرة الرحل (mu'akhkhirat al-rahil): The back part of a saddle; used as a simile for the size of the sutrah.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is commendable but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum thickness of a sutrah according to the Hanafi school?
A) One cubit
B) One finger's width
C) One handspan
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
The sutrah for desert prayer is a strongly recommended sunnah (mustahabb) with a minimum length of one cubit and thickness of a finger, and it should be placed close to the worshipper, opposite either eyebrow.

10 min
Ruling on Sutrah: Mustahabb and Its Dimensions
States the ruling on sutrah being mustahabb and its recommended dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sutrah and identify its minimum recommended dimensions.

Core Idea
Sutrah is mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not wajib — its minimum length is one cubit and minimum thickness is a finger's breadth.

This passage clarifies that for prayer in an open space, placing a sutrah is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. It derives this ruling from prophetic hadith and specifies minimum dimensions based on the back of a saddle and finger thickness to fulfill the purpose of being visible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what legal category (hukm) it falls under. Here, the act is placing a sutrah when praying in an open space, and the ruling is mustahabb (recommended).
The word 'mustahabb' is explicitly used in the text.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the evidence cited. The author provides two hadith: one with an imperative to place a sutrah, and a rhetorical question about the back of a saddle.
The hadith are from ahad (single-narrator) reports, so their transmission is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
Analyze how the proof leads to the ruling. In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'falyaj'al' indicates recommendation (nadb) because there is contextual evidence that the command is not for obligation. The rhetorical question also implies recommendation.
This step shows the link between the dalil and the hukm.
4
Note the minimum dimensions
Identify the dimensions specified. The minimum length is one cubit (dhirā'), from the hadith about the back of a saddle. The minimum thickness is a finger's breadth, as stated by al-Quduri, based on the purpose of being visible to passers-by.
These are recommended minima; larger sizes are also permissible.

Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. The translation: And the person who prays in an open field, it is appropriate for him to set up a sutrah in front of him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When any of you prays in an open field, let him set up a sutrah in front of him.' And the measure of the sutrah is one cubit or more, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'It suffices that when any of you prays in an open field, there should be something in front of him like the back of a saddle.' And it was said that it is appropriate that its thickness be the size of a finger, because less than that would not be visible to those passing from a distance, so the purpose would not be achieved. Explanation: The issue is that if a person prays in an open field, he should set up a sutrah in front of him, and this is mustahabb (recommended). The proof is the Prophet's saying: 'If any of you prays in the desert, let him place a sutrah in front of him.' As for the measure of the sutrah, it was stated that the minimum length should be one cubit, and more is fine. The proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Is any of you unable, when he prays in the open desert, to have something like the back of a saddle in front of him?' 'Mu'khirat' (with dammah on meem and kasrah on kha) refers to the piece of wood that is at the back of the saddle, level with the rider's head. Pronouncing kha with shaddah is wrong. 'Rahl' means saddle. Al-Quduri said that the thickness should be equal to a finger. The proof is that less than that would not be visible to passers-by from a distance, so the purpose of the sutrah would not be achieved; therefore it was said that the minimum thickness should be the size of a finger.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by stating that for a person praying in an open space, it is recommended (mustahabb) to place a sutrah (a physical barrier) in front of him. The evidence is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding that one who prays in the desert should place a sutrah. It then discusses the dimensions: the minimum length is one cubit (dhira'), and the minimum thickness is a finger's breadth, based on the hadith about the back of a saddle. The author explains that a thinner sutrah would not be visible from a distance and thus would not serve the purpose of preventing people from passing in front of the worshipper. This ruling is from the Hanafi school; according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it is mustahabb, not wajib.

Key Terms
سترة (sutrah): An object placed in front of a person praying to prevent people from passing directly in front of him.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit, a measure of length from elbow to fingertips.
موخرة الرحل (mu'khirat al-rahil): The back piece of a saddle, level with the rider's head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using a sutrah when praying in an open space?

B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible)
D) Haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sutrah is mustahabb for open-space prayer, with a minimum length of one cubit and thickness of a finger.

8 min
Positioning the Sutrah and When It Can Be Omitted
Explains how to position the sutrah and the ruling on omitting it when safe

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sutrah placement and identify when omitting it is permissible.

Core Idea
The sutrah should be placed opposite an eyebrow, not directly in front, and may be omitted when no one passes.

The sutrah serves to prevent passers-by from crossing in front of the worshipper. The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice, specifies that the sutrah be placed to the side—opposite the right or left eyebrow—rather than directly facing the worshipper. This lesson clarifies the ruling and the exceptional case where omitting the sutrah is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the placement of the sutrah during salah. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.? Hanafis rule it as sunnah ghayr muakkadah (non-emphasized sunnah).
Sunnah ghayr muakkadah means recommended but not obligatory; omission does not incur sin.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? A hadith narrated by Abu Dawood from al-Miqdad (ra) describing the Prophet's practice. The hadith is ahad (single-chain) in transmission, making it zanni al-thubut.
The hadith text is quoted in the source: 'I did not see the Messenger of Allah pray towards a stick, a pillar, or a tree except that he placed it opposite his right or left eyebrow, and he did not aim directly at it.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the Hanafi position? The Prophet's consistent practice of placing the sutrah to the side, and the explicit negation of direct facing (ولا يصمد له صمد), shows that directly facing the sutrah is not the sunnah. The placement to the side is the established sunnah.
The principle 'al-fi'l yufidu al-sunnah' (the action indicates recommendation) applies here.
4
Identify the exception for omission
When can the sutrah be omitted? When there is safety from people passing (no fear of someone crossing in front) and the worshipper does not face a road. The 'illah (cause) of the sutrah is to prevent passers-by; thus when that cause is absent, omission is permissible.
Even when safe, keeping the sutrah is still mustahabb (preferred).
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) prefer the sutrah to be directly in front, aligning with the face. Hanafis distinguish by placing it to the side, following the reported hadith.
The practical difference is minimal; both positions are valid.

Source Text

ويقرب من الستره لقوله عليه السلام من صلى الى سترة فليدن منها ويجعل السترة على حاجبه الايمن او على الايسر به ورد الاثر ولا بأس بترك السترة اذا امن المرور ولم يواجه الطريق
رجمہ اور سترہ سے قریب رہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جوشخص سترہ کی طرف نماز پڑھے تو اس سے نزدیک رہے اور سترہ کو اپنے ابی بابا میں ھوں کے مقابل رکھے اس کے ساتھ اثر وارد ہوا ہے۔ اور جب کسی کے گذرنے سے امن ہو اور راستہ کا مواجہہ نہ ہو تو سترہ ارک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
فریا۔ اس عبارت میں بیان کیا گیا کہ سترہ مصلی اپنے دائیں یا بائیں بھوؤں کے بالمقابل رکھے یعنی دونوں آنکھوں کے بیچ نہ ئے کیونکہ اس کے ساتھ اثر وارد ہوا ہے چنانچہ امام ابو داؤد نے ضباعہ بنت المقدار دین الاسود سے اور انہوں نے اپنے والد مقداد بن سے روایت کیا ہے قال ما رأیت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الى عود ولا عمود ولا شجرة الاجعله على حاجبه الايمن او الايسر ولا يصمد له صمد مقداد نے فرمایا کہ نہیں دیکھا میں نے اللہ کے برحق نبی کو کسی لکڑی یا ستون یا ورفت کی طرف نماز پڑھتے ہوئے مگر یہ کہ اس کو اپنے دائیں یا بائیں بھوؤں کے مقابل کر دیا اور اس کا ارادہ نہیں فرماتے تھے۔ (فتح القدیر) صاحب عنایہ نے اس اثر کو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ہے انه صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ما صلى الى شجرة ولا الى عودو لا عمودا الاجعله على حاجبه الايمن وله يصمد صمدا، اى لم يقصده قصدا الى المواجهة -
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ سترہ ترک کرنے میں اس وقت کوئی مضائقہ نہیں جب کہ لوگوں کے گذرنے سے امن ہو اور رسالے نہ ہو۔ اس عبارت میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ سترہ کی علت مساوی سرور ہے پس جہاں کسی کے گذرنے کا غالب گمان نہ ہو ترک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے البتہ امن کے باوجودستہ درکھنا مستحب ہے۔
The method of the worshipper planting the sutrah close to himself: And he should draw near to the sutrah, because he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays towards a sutrah, let him draw near to it, and place the sutrah opposite his right eyebrow or his left eyebrow.' With this, an athar (tradition) has been reported. And there is no harm in omitting the sutrah when one is safe from passage and does not face the road. The translation: And he should remain close to the sutrah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever prays towards a sutrah, let him be near it and place the sutrah opposite his right or left eyebrow.' An athar has been reported with this. And when one is safe from someone passing and does not face the road, there is no harm in leaving the sutrah. Explanation: In this passage it is stated that the worshipper should place the sutrah opposite his right or left eyebrow, i.e., not between both eyes, because an athar has been reported with this. Thus Imam Abu Dawood narrated from Duba'ah bint al-Miqdad ibn al-Aswad, and she from her father al-Miqdad ibn al-Aswad, who said: 'I did not see the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) pray towards a stick, a pillar, or a tree, except that he placed it opposite his right or left eyebrow, and he did not aim directly at it.' (Fath al-Qadir). The author of al-Inayah mentioned this athar with these words: 'He (peace be upon him) never prayed towards a tree, a stick, or a pillar except that he placed it opposite his right eyebrow, and he did not aim directly at it,' i.e., he did not intentionally face it directly. The author of al-Hidayah said: There is no harm in omitting the sutrah when one is safe from people passing and not facing the road. This passage indicates that the cause ('illah) of the sutrah is prevention of passing; so where there is no predominant assumption of someone passing, there is no harm in omitting it. However, even when safe, keeping the sutrah is mustahabb.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings: first, the worshipper should stand close to the sutrah and place it opposite his right or left eyebrow, not directly in front, as reported in the hadith from Abu Dawood. Second, if there is no fear of people passing in front and one is not facing a road, it is permissible to omit the sutrah. However, even when safe, keeping the sutrah remains mustahabb. The ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the principle that the purpose of the sutrah is to prevent passers-by from crossing in front of the worshipper.

Key Terms
حاجب (hajib): Eyebrow; the sutrah should be placed opposite the right or left eyebrow.
اثر (athar): A tradition or report from the Companions or the Prophet; here specific hadith.
السترة (al-sutrah): An object placed in front of the worshipper to mark the prayer space and prevent passers-by from crossing directly in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should the sutrah be placed relative to the worshipper?
A) Directly in front of the face
B) Opposite the right or left eyebrow
C) At the feet
D) Behind the worshipper

Key Takeaway
The sutrah should be placed opposite the right or left eyebrow, not directly in front, and may be omitted when there is no risk of people passing and one does not face a road.

Imam's Sutrah Suffices for the Congregation
Ruling proof from hadith on imam's sutrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's sutrah in congregational prayer and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Imam's sutrah suffices for all followers in congregation; no separate sutrah needed.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from the Hanafi school: the imam's sutrah is sufficient for everyone praying behind him. This is based on the Prophet's practice at Batha', where he prayed with an 'anazah while followers had no sutrah. The passage from al-Hidayah presents the proof and clarifies that the ruling is a recommended practice (sunnah), not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (congregational prayer) and the hukm level: it is a sunnah (recommended) for the imam to have a sutrah, and it suffices for all followers.
The act is the sutrah in congregational prayer; the ruling is that it is sunnah, not fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of the Prophet praying at Batha' with an 'anazah (short spear) as a sutrah, while followers had no sutrah.
The hadith is reported by Bukhari and others from Abu Hurairah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: because the followers did not have separate sutrahs yet their prayer was valid, the imam's sutrah must have served as a sutrah for them.
The absence of individual sutrahs for followers and the validity of their prayer is the key indicator.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the differing school: some other madhhabs (e.g., Shafi'i) require each follower to have a sutrah or at least the first row.
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih; other schools have variant rulings.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school adopts this position: the explicit practice of the Prophet without any contrary evidence makes it the relied-upon view.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام کا سترہ مقتدی کے لئے کافی ہے
وسترة الامام سترة للقوم لانه عليه السلام صلى ببطحاء مكة الى عنزة ولم يكن للقوم من ترجمہ اور امام کا ستر ہوہی قوم کا سترہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطحا مکہ میں پوری دار عضاء کی طرف نماز پڑھی اور قوم کے لئے سوار تشریح نماز با جماعت کی صورت میں امام کا سترہ مقتدیوں کے لئے کافی ہوگا۔ دلیل و وحدیث ہے جس کو امام بخاری اور اہ حضرت ابو حیفہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام کے بیان کے مطابق متن حدیث یہ ہے انه صلی اللہ وسلم صلى بهم بالبطحاء وبين يديه عنزة والمرأة والحمار يمرون من ورائها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مقام بطحا میں نماز پڑھائی اور آپ کے آگے پوری دار عصاء تھا اور عورت اور گدھا عصاء کے ماوراء سے گذر رہے تھے۔ مصنف ہدایہ کہنے مقتدیوں کے واسطے ستر نہیں تھا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کا ستر و مقتدیوں کے لئے کافی ہو جائے گی۔
The imam's sutrah suffices for the congregation. And the imam's sutrah is a sutrah for the people, because he (peace be upon him) prayed at Batha' in Mecca facing an 'anazah, and there was no sutrah for the people. The translation: And the imam's sutrah is the sutrah for the congregation, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed at Batha' in Mecca facing a spear, and for the people there was no sutrah. Explanation: In congregational prayer, the imam's sutrah suffices for the followers. The proof is a hadith reported by Imam Bukhari and others from Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him). According to Ibn al-Humam, the text of the hadith is: 'He (peace be upon him) led them in prayer at Batha', and in front of him was an 'anazah, and women and donkeys were passing behind it.' That is, the Prophet (peace be upon him) led the prayer at Batha', and in front of him was a spear, and women and donkeys were passing from behind it. The author of al-Hidayah says: The followers had no separate sutrah, which indicates that the imam's sutrah suffices for them.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage states that in congregational prayer, the sutrah placed in front of the imam is sufficient for all the followers. The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) led the prayer at Batha' with only an 'anazah (a short spear) in front of him, while women and donkeys passed behind it. The followers did not have individual sutrahs, yet their prayer was valid. This establishes that the imam's sutrah serves as a sutrah for the entire congregation. The ruling is based on this practice of the Prophet.

Key Terms
عنزة ('anazah): A short spear or staff that the Prophet used as a sutrah during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding the sutrah in congregational prayer?
A) Each follower must have a separate sutrah
B) The imam's sutrah suffices for all followers
C) No sutrah is needed in congregation
D) Sutrah is not recommended in prayer

Key Takeaway
The imam's sutrah in congregational prayer is sufficient for all followers, based on the Prophet's practice at Batha'.
