Requirement of Planting Sutrah vs. Drawing a Line
Dispute on sutrah validity between Hanafi and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirement for sutrah (gharz), distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, and apply the ruling to cases of hard ground or unavailable objects.

Core Idea
A sutrah must physically obstruct passage; a drawn line does not achieve this, so it is invalid in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: what constitutes a valid sutrah during prayer. While the Shafi'i school permits drawing a line, the Hanafi school insists on planting an object (gharz). We will explore the reasoning, practical adjustments, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on sutrah
State the Hanafi rule: a valid sutrah must be planted (gharz) in the ground; simply placing it or drawing a line is not sufficient.
The term 'gharz' implies fixing the object so it stands upright, creating a physical barrier.
2
Recognize the Shafi'i position
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i and some later Hanafi mashayikh hold that drawing a long line on the ground can serve as a sutrah.
This view is based on the idea that a line creates a symbolic barrier.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof (talil)
Understand the Hanafi reasoning: the purpose (maqsud) of a sutrah is to physically obstruct passage between the worshipper and passers-by. A line on the ground does not create any real obstruction, so it is equivalent to having no sutrah at all.
The argument is teleological (talil): the means must fulfill the end.
4
Apply practical variations
If the ground is too hard to plant, the sutrah should be placed lengthwise (not widthwise) to maximize obstruction. If no object is available, drawing a line remains invalid.
The ruling adapts to circumstances while maintaining the principle of physical obstruction.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi practice, a person who prays behind a line has no valid sutrah, so passing in front of them is not sinful for the passer. In Shafi'i practice, the line suffices and the passer must avoid crossing it.
This affects the ruling on whether it is permissible to pass in front of a worshipper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سترہ گاڑھنے کا اعتبار ہے ڈال دینا اور خط کھینچنا کافی نہیں
ويعتبر الغرز دون الالقاء والخط لان المقصود لا يحصل به
ترجمہ اور سترہ کو گاڑ دینا معتبر ہے نہ کہ اس کا ڈال دینا اور نہ خط کھینچنا کیونکہ اس سے مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ماتن نے کہا کہ سترہ کا گاز نا معتبر ہے اس کا زمین پر گاڑنا یا خط کھینچنا معتبر نہیں ہے لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جب زمین را کا گاڑھناممکن ہو اور اگر زمین سخت بوسترہ کا گاڑ ناممکن نہ ہو تو سترہ کو طولا زمین پر رکھدے نہ کہ عرضاً اور طولاً اس لئے رکھے تا کہ ہو کی بیت پر ہو جائے ۔ اور اگرسترہ بنانے کے لئے لکڑی وغیرہ کوئی چیز نہ ہو تو کیا زمین پر خط کھینچنا معتبر ہو گیا یا نہیں تو صاحب عنایہ کے مطابق طرفین سے مروی ہے کہ خط کھینچنا معتبر نہیں ہوگا اور یہ کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ایک طویل خط کھینچ دے اور اس کے قائل بعض مشائخ متأخرین ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے طرفین بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ سترہ سے مقصود مصلی اور گزرنے والے کے درمیان حیلولت ہے اور یہ مقصود اس یہ مقصود اس سے حاصل نہیں :
ہونا اور نہ ہونا دونوں برابر ہیں۔
Planting the sutrah is considered; throwing it down or drawing a line is not sufficient. And planting (gharz) is considered, not throwing down or drawing a line, because the purpose is not achieved by that. Translation: And planting the sutrah is considered, not throwing it down nor drawing a line, because the purpose will not be achieved. Explanation: The author (matn) said that planting the sutrah is required; placing it on the ground or drawing a line is not considered. But this is when planting in the ground is possible. If the ground is hard and planting is not possible, then he should place the sutrah lengthwise on the ground, not widthwise, and place it lengthwise so that it becomes an obstacle. And if there is no object like a stick to make a sutrah, then whether drawing a line on the ground is considered or not? According to the author of al-Inayah, it is narrated from both sides that drawing a line is not considered, and it is nothing. However, Imam al-Shafi'i said that he should draw a long line, and some later mashayikh adopt that. The author of al-Hidayah, while mentioning both sides, said: The purpose of the sutrah is obstruction between the worshipper and the passer-by, and this purpose is not achieved by that (the line). So the line and its absence are equal.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute. The Hanafi school holds that for a sutrah to be valid, it must be planted (gharz) in the ground, not merely laid down or drawn as a line on the ground. The reason is that the purpose of the sutrah is to physically obstruct the passage, which a line does not achieve. If the ground is too hard to plant, the sutrah should be placed lengthwise. If no object is available, drawing a line is not considered valid in the Hanafi school, contrary to the Shafi'i school which permits a long line. The author of al-Hidayah concludes that the purpose is not achieved by a line, so it is as if nothing is there. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a line does not suffice.

Key Terms
غرس (gharz): Planting or fixing the sutrah into the ground.
خط (khatt): A line drawn on the ground as a sutrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the requirement for a valid sutrah when praying in open space?
A) Drawing a line on the ground
B) Planting an object in the ground
C) Simply placing an object on the ground
D) No sutrah is needed

Key Takeaway
A sutrah must be planted; drawing a line is invalid in the Hanafi school.

Repelling a Passer-by During Prayer: Gesture or Tasbih?
Explains how to repel someone passing in front using gesture or tasbih, and the dislike of combining both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passer-by during prayer and identify when combining methods is disliked.

Core Idea
Gesture or tasbih suffices to repel a passer-by; combining both is disliked.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on repelling someone who passes in front of a worshipper during prayer when there is no sutrah. The Hanafi school permits two methods—gesture (isharah) or saying 'Subhan Allah' (tasbih)—but discourages using both together. This ruling is based on prophetic practice and the principle of sufficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is repelling a passer-by in prayer. The ruling is sunnah (recommended) when needed.
2
List the two methods
The two methods are gesture (isharah) and tasbih (saying Subhan Allah).
3
State the ruling on combining
Combining both is makruh tanzih (disliked) because either one alone is sufficient.
4
Identify the dalil
The dalil is the hadith 'فادرؤا ما استطع بالاشارة' and the Prophet's action with Umm Salamah's children.
Also a hadith on tasbih.
5
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'فادرؤا' indicates recommendation, not obligation, as it is for a specific situation.
The Prophet himself demonstrated the method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نمازی سترہ کی عدم موجودگی میں گذرنے والے کو دفع کرے
ويدرا المار اذا لم يكن بين يديه سترة او مر بينه و بين السترة لقوله عليه السلام فادرؤا ما استطع بالاشارة كما فعل رسول الله بولدى ام سلمة او يدفع بالتسبيح لما روينا من قبل ويكره الجمع.
لان باحدهما كفاية
The worshipper should repel the passer-by when there is no sutrah in front of him, or if he passes between him and the sutrah, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Repel as much as you can by gesture,' as the Messenger of Allah did with the children of Umm Salamah. Or he may repel by tasbih (saying Subhan Allah) based on what we have narrated previously. And combining (both) is disliked, because either one suffices.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that if there is no sutrah, or if someone passes between the worshipper and his sutrah, the worshipper should repel the person by gesture (e.g., moving the hand) or by saying 'Subhan Allah' (tasbih). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) repelled by gesture to the children of Umm Salamah, and another hadith about tasbih. It is disliked to combine both gestures and tasbih, as one is sufficient. This ruling applies to all prayers regardless of sutrah presence, but is specifically mentioned here for the case of no sutrah.

Key Terms
اشارة (isharah): A gesture used to repel someone passing in front during prayer.
تسبيح (tasbih): Saying 'Subhan Allah' to alert the passer-by.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passer-by in front of a person praying without a sutrah?
A) Must use both gesture and tasbih
B) May use gesture or tasbih; combining is disliked
C) Must remain silent and not repel
D) Only gesture is allowed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, repelling a passer-by during prayer is recommended using either a gesture or tasbih, and combining both is disliked because one suffices.

6 min
Imam's Sutra Suffices for the Congregation
Ruling with hadith proof on imam's barrier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's sutra and explain the hadith evidence that establishes it.

Core Idea
The imam's barrier in prayer protects the entire congregation.

In congregational prayer, does each worshipper need a personal barrier, or does the imam's sutra suffice? The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, holds that the imam's sutra serves as a sutra for all followers. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the imam's sutra suffices for the followers. What is the legal status (hukm) of the sutra itself?
Sunnah muakkadah for the imam; leaving it without excuse is makruh.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of the Prophet praying at al-Batha with only a spear in front of him, while the congregation had no individual sutras.
Narrated by Bukhari and Abu Hanifah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet did not instruct each follower to have a sutra, so his sutra was sufficient for all.
The explicit statement 'ولم يكن للقوم من سترة' (the congregation had no sutra) is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that each person should have their own sutra in congregation. What is their proof?
They rely on general hadiths about sutra and do not see this incident as overriding them.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) in the school, supported by the explicit practice of the Prophet.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يفسد الصلوة وما يكره فيها
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بایت
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ سترہ ترک کرنے میں اس وقت کوئی مضائقہ نہیں جب کہ لوگوں کے گذرنے سے امن ہو اور رسالے نہ ہو۔ اس عبارت میں اس طرف اشارہ ہے کہ سترہ کی علت مساوی سرور ہے پس جہاں کسی کے گذرنے کا غالب گمان نہ ہو ترک کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے البتہ امن کے باوجودستہ درکھنا مستحب ہے۔

امام کا سترہ مقتدی کے لئے کافی ہے
وسترة الامام سترة للقوم لانه عليه السلام صلى ببطحاء مكة الى عنزة ولم يكن للقوم من سترة
ترجمہ اور امام کا ستر ہوہی قوم کا سترہ ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بطحا مکہ میں پوری دار عضاء کی طرف نماز پڑھی اور قوم کے لئے سوار تشریح نماز با جماعت کی صورت میں امام کا سترہ مقتدیوں کے لئے کافی ہوگا۔ دلیل و وحدیث ہے جس کو امام بخاری اور اہ حضرت ابو حیفہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے روایت کیا ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام کے بیان کے مطابق متن حدیث یہ ہے انہ صلی اللہ وسلم صلى بهم بالبطحاء وبين يديه عنزة والمرأة والحمار يمرون من ورائها یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مقام بطحا میں نماز پڑھائی اور آپ کے آگے پوری دار عصاء تھا اور عورت اور گدھا عصاء کے ماوراء سے گذر رہے تھے۔ مصنف ہدایہ کہنے مقتدیوں کے واسطے ستر نہیں تھا اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کا ستر و مقتدیوں کے لئے کافی ہو جائے گی۔
Chapter of what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. The author of Hidayah said: There is no harm in leaving the sutra when there is safety from people passing and no crowd. This indicates that the cause of sutra is fear of passage, so where there is no predominant fear of anyone passing, there is no harm in leaving it; however, keeping the sutra is mustahab despite safety. The imam's sutra suffices for the congregation because he (peace be upon him) prayed in Batah of Makkah facing a spear and the congregation had no sutra. Explanation: In congregational prayer, the imam's sutra suffices for the followers. The evidence is a hadith narrated by Imam Bukhari and Abu Hanifah. According to Ibn al-Humam, the text is: 'He (peace be upon him) led them in prayer at al-Batha, and in front of him was a spear, and women and donkeys were passing behind it.' The author of Hidayah says: The followers had no sutra, so it is learned that the imam's sutra suffices for the followers.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This is a ruling from Hidayah stating that in congregational prayer, the sutra (barrier) of the imam serves as a sutra for all followers. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet praying in an open area with only a spear in front of him, while the congregation had no individual barriers, yet the prayer was valid. The Hanafi position is that the imam's sutra suffices, as the followers are considered part of the imam's prayer. The cause of the sutra is to prevent passage in front of the worshipper, and if there is no fear of passage, leaving it is permissible but still mustahab to have it.

Key Terms
سترہ (sutrah): An object placed in front of a worshipper to prevent people from passing directly in front.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the sutra in congregational prayer?
A) Each follower must have their own sutra.
B) The imam's sutra suffices for all followers.
C) No sutra is required in congregational prayer.
D) Only the imam needs a sutra; followers may or may not have one.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's sutra in congregational prayer suffices for all followers, as proven by the Prophet's practice.

The Valid Method of Setting Up the Sutra: Planting vs. Line
Ruling on planting vs placing or drawing a line for sutra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement for planting the sutra and explain why drawing a line is invalid.

Core Idea
A sutra must physically obstruct; a line on the ground does not.

When praying, the Hanafi school teaches that a sutra should be placed to prevent passage in front of the worshipper. But what qualifies as a sutra? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the sutra must be planted upright – not merely laid down or drawn as a line. We will explore the reasoning behind this and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Setting up a sutra is sunnah muakkadah. Identify what the text says about the required method.
2
Understand the condition for planting
The sutra must be planted (gharz) if the ground is soft. If the ground is hard, it should be placed lengthwise (not widthwise) to create a vertical barrier.
Placing widthwise would not obstruct passage.
3
Identify invalid methods
Placing the sutra horizontally on the ground or drawing a line on the ground are invalid forms of sutra.
Both fail to provide physical separation.
4
Grasp the rationale
The purpose of the sutra is to create a physical barrier (hailulah) between the worshipper and passersby. A line does not achieve this.
The objective is physical, not symbolic.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i and some later Hanafi scholars permit drawing a line, but the relied-upon Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) rejects it.
The dispute centers on whether the objective can be achieved symbolically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتبر الغرز دون الالقاء والخط لان المقصود لا يحصل به
ترجمہ اور سترہ کو گاڑ دینا معتبر ہے نہ کہ اس کا ڈال دینا اور نہ خط کھینچنا کیونکہ اس سے مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح ماتن نے کہا کہ سترہ کا گاز نا معتبر ہے اس کا زمین پر گاڑنا یا خط کھینچنا معتبر نہیں ہے لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جب زمین را کا گاڑھناممکن ہو اور اگر زمین سخت بوسترہ کا گاڑ ناممکن نہ ہو تو سترہ کو طولا زمین پر رکھدے نہ کہ عرضاً اور طولاً اس لئے رکھے تا کہ ہو کی بیت پر ہو جائے ۔ اور اگرسترہ بنانے کے لئے لکڑی وغیرہ کوئی چیز نہ ہو تو کیا زمین پر خط کھینچنا معتبر ہو گیا یا نہیں تو صاحب عنایہ کے مطابق طرفین سے مروی ہے کہ خط کھینچنا معتبر نہیں ہوگا اور یہ کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ایک طویل خط کھینچ دے اور اس کے قائل بعض مشائخ متأخرین ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے طرفین بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ سترہ سے مقصود مصلی اور گزرنے والے کے درمیان حیلولت ہے اور یہ مقصود اس یہ مقصود اس سے حاصل نہیں :
ہونا اور نہ ہونا دونوں برابر ہیں۔
And planting is considered, not placing or line, because the objective is not achieved thereby. Translation: The sutra being planted is considered, not its being placed or drawing a line, because the objective will not be achieved. Explanation: The matn said that the planting of the sutra is considered; its being placed on the ground or drawing a line is not considered. But this is when the ground is soft and planting is possible. If the ground is hard and planting is impossible, then place the sutra lengthwise on the ground, not widthwise. And if there is no object like a stick to make a sutra, then is drawing a line on the ground considered? According to Sahib al-Inayah, it is narrated from both sides that drawing a line is not considered, and it is nothing. However, Imam al-Shafi'i said that one should draw a long line, and some later mashayikh follow him. Sahib al-Hidayah, mentioning both sides, said that the objective of the sutra is separation between the worshipper and the passerby, and this objective is not achieved by this (line).
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses the valid method of setting up a sutra. The Hanafi ruling is that the sutra must be planted (fixed upright) in the ground, not merely placed horizontally or drawn as a line. The reason is that the purpose of the sutra is to physically block passage, and mere placement or a line does not provide a tangible barrier. However, if the ground is too hard to plant, the sutra may be placed lengthwise (in the direction of qibla) to create a vertical barrier. If no object is available, drawing a line on the ground is not accepted in the Hanafi school, because a line does not physically obstruct. Imam al-Shafi'i permits drawing a line, and some later Hanafi scholars also accepted it, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is not valid. The text also mentions that both opinions exist, but the objective of separation is not achieved by a line.

Key Terms
غرز (gharz): Planting or fixing an object upright in the ground.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on drawing a line on the ground as a sutra?
A) It is valid with a long line
B) It is invalid because it does not obstruct passage
C) It is valid only if no stick is available
D) It is valid for the imam but not for followers

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a sutra must be a physical obstruction; a line on the ground is insufficient.

Repelling a Passerby During Prayer: Ruling and Method
Ruling on repelling passerby in salah: method and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passerby during salah and explain the evidence and method.

Core Idea
Repelling is wajib; use one method—gesture or tasbih—both together is makruh.

When a person tries to pass in front of you during prayer, you are required to prevent them. But how? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, the prophetic evidence, and the proper method—whether by hand gesture or by saying Subhanallah. You will learn why only one method is needed and why combining them is disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the worshipper must do when a passerby approaches. The text states 'wadra al-marra' meaning repel. What is the hukm level? Wajib, based on the command.
The imperative indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the Prophet's command: 'Fadra'u ma istata'tum' (Repel them as much as you can). Also the story of Umm Salamah's children.
Both are ahad hadith but considered sound.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative form 'fadra'u' shows obligation (wujub). The Prophet's practice demonstrates the method by gesture or tasbih.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Determine the method of repelling
The text gives two options: gesture (like hand movement) or saying Subhanallah (tasbih). Both are acceptable individually.
Women may clap instead of tasbih per other hadith.
5
Note the ruling on combining methods
Combining gesture and tasbih together is makruh (disliked) because one method suffices. Using both is unnecessary excess.
This is the Hanafi position; some schools may not specify.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدرا المار اذا لم يكن بين يديه سترة او مر بينه و بين السترة لقوله عليه السلام فادرؤا ما استطع بالاشارة كما فعل رسول الله بولدى ام سلمة او يدفع بالتسبيح لما روينا من قبل ويكره الجمع لان باحدهما كفاية

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مصلی کے سامنے سترو نہ ہو یا سترہ تو ہے مگر سترہ اور مصلی کے درمیان سے کوئی گذرنے کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو تو معملی اس گذرنے والے کو دفع کرے کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ فادرؤا ما استطعتہ یعنی جس قدر ممکن ہو اس کو دفع کرو۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مصلی گذرنے والے کو کس طرح دفع کرے سو اس بارے میں فرمایا کہ اشارے سے دفع کرے جیسا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ام سلمہ کے دو بچوں کو دفع کیا تھا۔ تفصیل صاحب کفایہ اور عنایہ نے یہ ذکر کی ہے ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي في بيت ام سلمته فقام ولدها عمر ليمر بين يديه فاشار اليه ان قف فوقف تم قامت بنتها زينب لتمر بين يديه فاشار اليها ان قفى فابت فمرت فلما فرغ من صلوته قال ناقصات العقل ناقصات الدين صواحب يوسف صواحب كرسف يغلبن الكرام، ويغليهن اللنام، یعنی حضور اقدس فخر دو عالم محسن اعظم ہے حضرت ام سلمہ کے مکان میں نماز پڑھ رہے تھے پس امسلمہ کا فرزند نیک ارجمند عمر کھڑا ہوا تا کہ کائنات کے آقا کے آگے سے ہو کر گزرے آپ نے اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا کہ شہر جا ، سو وہ ٹھہر گیا۔ پھر ام سلمہ کی سادہ لوح صاحبزادی زینب کھڑی ہوئی تا کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے آگے سے گذرے آپ نے اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ک ٹھہر جاؤ لیکن وہ نہ مانی اور گذرگئی پس جب یہ صاحب شریعت اپنی نماز سے فراغت پاچکا تو یوں گویا ہوا کہ ( یہ آدم کی بیٹیاں ناقصات العقل ناقصات دین ، صواحب یوسف اور صواحب کر سف ہیں۔ یہ کریم اور بھلے لوگوں پر غالب آ جاتی ہیں اور کمین لوگ ان پر چڑھ بنتے ہیں ۔ بہر حال اس حدیث سے اشارہ سے دفع کرنا ثابت ہوا۔ یا اس کو تسبیح پڑھ کر دفع کرے۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی ہے یعنی حضور کا قول اذا نابت احدكم نائبته في الصلوة فليسبح اور اشارہ اور تسبیح دونوں کو جمع کرنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کافی ہے۔
And the worshipper should repel the passerby when there is no sutra in front of him, or when (the passerby) passes between him and the sutra, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Repel them as much as you can.' By gesture, as the Messenger of Allah did with the two children of Umm Salamah, or he should repel by tasbih, as we narrated previously. And combining both is makruh, because one of them is sufficient. Translation: The worshipper should repel the passerby when there is no sutra in front of him or when (the passerby) passes between him and the sutra, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Repel them as much as you can.' And he should repel by gesture, as the Prophet did with the two children of Umm Salamah, or he should repel by reciting tasbih, due to the hadith we narrated before. And combining both is makruh, because one is sufficient. Explanation: The issue is that if the worshipper has no sutra, or there is a sutra but someone intends to pass between the worshipper and the sutra, the worshipper should repel the passerby because the Prophet said: 'Repel them as much as you can.' As for how to repel, he said: by gesture, as the Prophet repelled the two children of Umm Salamah. The detail from Sahib al-Kifayah and al-Inayah: The Prophet was praying in the house of Umm Salamah; her son 'Umar stood to pass in front of him, and he gestured to him to stop, so he stopped. Then her daughter Zaynab stood to pass, and he gestured to her to stop, but she did not comply and passed. When he finished his prayer, he said: 'They are deficient in intellect and religion, the women of Yusuf and women of Kirsaf; they overcome the noble and the base overcome them.' So by this hadith, repelling by gesture is proven. Or he should repel by tasbih. The evidence has preceded: the Prophet's saying: 'When something happens to one of you in prayer, let him say subhanallah.' And combining both gesture and tasbih is makruh, because one of them is sufficient.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on repelling someone who tries to pass in front of a praying person when there is no sutra or if they pass between the worshipper and the sutra. The worshipper is required to prevent the passerby as much as possible, based on the general command of the Prophet. The method of repelling is by gesture (such as a hand movement) or by saying 'Subhanallah' (tasbih). The text provides the example of the Prophet gesturing to Umm Salamah's children. It is makruh (disliked) to combine both gesture and tasbih, as one method suffices. The wisdom behind repelling is to preserve the sanctity of prayer and prevent distraction.

Key Terms
تسبیح (tasbih): Saying 'Subhanallah' to alert someone during prayer.
سُتْرَة (sutra): An object placed in front of the worshipper to mark the prayer space and prevent people from crossing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only by raising the voice
B) By gesture or tasbih, but not both together
C) By both gesture and tasbih together
D) By stepping forward

Key Takeaway
Repelling a passerby during prayer is wajib, performed by gesture or tasbih, and combining both is makruh.

Disliked Acts in Salah: Playing with Clothes or Body
Ruling on playing with clothes or body during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on playing with clothes or body during salah and cite the hadith proof that establishes it as makruh.

Core Idea
Playing in prayer is makruh because Allah dislikes it – a hadith and qiyas confirm.

This short but powerful passage from Al-Hidayah establishes one of the fundamental rulings on conduct in salah: the prohibition of idle play (abath). The author provides both a direct hadith and a rational analogy to underscore its gravity. In this lesson, you will unpack the ruling, its evidence, and its classification in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage explicitly rules on 'playing with clothes or body' during prayer. The ruling is makruh (disliked). Note that the author does not specify degrees; later Hanafis differentiate between minor and major abath.
The term abath covers any purposeless fidgeting.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The text cites a hadith: 'Verily Allah has disliked for you three things' and mentions playing in prayer. This is a hadith ahad (solitary narration), so its authority is zanni al-thubut, but the meaning is clear.
The full hadith is recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet explicitly mentioned 'al-abath fi al-salah' as disliked by Allah. The imperative of khushu implies avoiding all unnecessary movement; thus the hadith's indication is direct (qati al-dalala) in establishing prohibition.
Hanafis consider the 'amr of khushu as evidence for wujub; here the explicit dislike confirms makruh.
4
Analyse the qiyas argument
The text adds a secondary proof: 'playing outside prayer is haram, so what about in prayer?' This is an argument a fortiori (qiyas awla). If idle play is haram outside, it is even more prohibited during the most sublime act of worship. This reinforces the ruling.
This qiyas is used as supplementary evidence, not independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكروہات نماز فصل
نماز میں کپڑے، بدن سے کھیلنا اور عبث کام مکروہ ہے
وبكره للمصلى ان يعبث بثوبه او بجسده لقوله عليه السلام ان الله تعالى كره لكم ثلاثا وذكر منها العبث في الصلوة ولان العبث خارج الصلوة حرام فما ظنك في الصلوة
ترجمہ ( یہ ) فصل ( مکروہات نماز کے بیان میں ہے)۔ اور مصلی کے لئے مکروہ ہے یہ کہ کھیلے اپنے کپڑے یا بدن کے ساتھ کیونکہ حضور نے فرمایا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے لئے تین چیزوں کو مکر وہ کیا ہے اور ان تین چیزوں میں سے ایک نماز میں عبث کرنا ہے اور اس لئے کہ عبث خارج صلوۃ حرام ہے پس نماز میں تیرا کیا گمان ہے۔
Chapter on the disliked acts of prayer. It is disliked for the worshipper to play with his clothes or his body, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Verily Allah has disliked for you three things' and mentioned among them playing in prayer. And because playing outside of prayer is haram, so what is your opinion about it in prayer?
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is a new section (fasl) on the disliked acts (makruhat) in salah. The first ruling is that it is makruh for the worshipper to engage in idle play (abath) with his clothes or body during prayer. The evidence is a hadith where the Prophet said Allah dislikes three things, including playing in prayer. The text adds a qiyas argument: if playing is haram outside of prayer, then it is even more serious in prayer. The Hanafi position classifies this as makruh tahrimi? The text says 'makruh' but the comparison with haram suggests it is close to haram. According to Hanafi fiqh, unnecessary movements are makruh tahrimi if they are multiple and consecutive; but this is specifically about playing with clothes or body, which is considered minor and thus makruh tanzihi? The text does not specify, but the ruling is makruh. The lesson is foundational for understanding comportment in salah.

Key Terms
عبث (abath): Idle, purposeless play or fidgeting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that playing with clothes during salah is makruh?
A) A hadith mentioning Allah's dislike of playing in prayer
B) A Quranic verse prohibiting fidgeting
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Qiyas based on eating during prayer

Key Takeaway
Playing with clothes or body during salah is makruh due to clear hadith and qiyas, emphasizing the need for khushu.
